                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Ackee and saltfish recipe Cooking with chillies\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#saltfish #ackeeandsaltfish #saltcod #ackee #sweetpeppers #fry #chillipepper #riceandpeas #thyme #images #seeds \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Ackee and saltfish is Jamaica's national dish. You will probably have to use canned ackee unless you are in the West Indies\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2360\n|PortionCalories = 590\n|DatePublished=1st May 2014\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 1 day, 45 minutes\n|PrepTime = 1 day\n|CookTime =  45 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Ackee and Saltfish CP.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Not for me</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3.5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Not at all keen on this - might be ok with another fish, like basa?</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n\n[[Ackee]] and saltfish is [[Jamaica]]'s national dish.\n\nYou will probably have to use canned [[Ackee|ackee]] unless you are in the West Indies.\n\n[[Salt fish]] is [[Salt cod|salt cod]] which needs to be soaked overnight and rinsed well to rehydrate and remove excess [[Salt|salt]].  Don't [[Boil|boil]] it an an attempt to rehydrate it.  You'll end up with salty rubber!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 tablespoons [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 4 [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and sliced\n| 1 [[Scotch bonnet]] [[Chilli pepper|chilli pepper]], finely chopped with the [[Seeds|seeds]] removed if preferred\n| 450g [1 lb] [[Salt cod|salt cod]] ([[saltfish]])\n| 2 [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]] of any colour, deseeded and chopped\n| 2 [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], chopped\n| 1 400g can of tinned [[Ackee|ackee]]\n| 1 sprig of [[Fresh thyme|fresh thyme]] or 1 level teaspoon of [[Dried thyme|dried thyme]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Soak the [[saltfish]] ([[Salt cod|salt cod]]) overnight in plenty of fresh cold water, changing a few times if you are able.  Rinse well.\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Once the [[saltfish]] has been soaked for 24 hours and rinsed, [[Simmer|simmer]] gently for 25 minutes and discard the water.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Frying pan|frying pan]] or [[Wok|wok]], add the [[Black pepper|black pepper]] and gently [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]] for 5 minutes.  \n|Add the [[Crushed garlic|crushed garlic]] and chopped [[Chilli pepper|chilli pepper]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for another few minutes\n| Add the [[Salt cod|salt cod]] and [[Fry|fry]] for 5 minutes, allowing the flesh to break up a little\n| Stir in the [[Thyme|thyme]], season to taste and serve.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a [[Salad|salad]] or [[Rice and peas|rice and peas]] and plenty of [[Chilli sauce|chilli sauce]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Jamaican recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#saltfish #ackeeandsaltfish #saltcod #ackee #sweetpeppers #fry #chillipepper #riceandpeas #thyme #images #seeds </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "American-style brined roast turkey",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=American-style brined roast turkey a game recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#turkey #roast #brine #brownsugar #roasting #americanstylebrinedroastturkey #unusualrecipes #chicken #thigh #poultry #drumsticks \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Soaking a turkey overnight in a solution of salt and water ensures moist results\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 351\n|PortionCalories = 29\n|DatePublished=3rd January 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = 12\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 1 day\n|PrepTime = 1 day\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Oven roasted brine-soaked turkey-wiki.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Fabulous!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Worth the extra effort!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]])</span></span>\n}}\nMartha Stewart, the American [[Cookery|cookery]] goddess says: \"Soaking a [[Turkey|turkey]] overnight in a solution of [[Salt|salt]] and water ensures moist results. When you add aromatics to the [[Brine|brine]], the resulting [[Roast|roast]] is also infused with a subtle character all its own\"\n\nI've experimented with a similar recipe using [[Chicken|chicken]] and I have to agree!\n\nAllow 2 days for the preparation and cooking of this festive recipe.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 3.8 kg whole turkey [8.5 lb] - see Chef's notes\n| 2 tablespoons of (1/2 stick) [[butter]] to coat skin of [[Turkey|turkey]]\n| &#189; gallon of water\n| 2 cups [[Salt|salt]]\n| &#189; cup firmly packed light [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]]\n| 2 gallons of ice water (50% ice)\n}}\n===Brining===\n\n\n* In 1/2 gallon of water, combine the [[Salt|salt]] and [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]] for the [[Brine|brine]] and bring to a [[Boil|boil]] for about 3 minutes. Remove from heat and add to 5 gallon bucket.\n* Add the remaining ice water.\n* Remove neck, and giblets and the [[Parson's nose]] from [[Turkey|turkey]] and put in 5 gallon bucket. If [[Brine|brine]] won't cover [[Turkey|turkey]] add a little more water.\n* Put bucket in a cold area for 6 to 24 hours.\n\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| The tricky thing about cooking [[Poultry|poultry]] is that the dark [[Meat|meat]] needs to be about 15 [[Degrees|degrees]] hotter than the white [[Meat|meat]]. White [[Meat|meat]] is safe to eat at 165\u00b0F (73.9\u00b0C), which is the temperature at which salmonella instantly dies. (Though 12 minutes at 140\u00b0F (60\u00b0C) will kill it as well, so odds are fairly good that, for a [[Roast|roast]], you'll kill it all on the way to 165\u00b0F (73.9\u00b0C)) The problem is that dark [[Meat|meat]] isn't very good at 165\u00b0F (73.9\u00b0C). Further complicating this is that if the breast meat gets to the 180\u00b0F (82.2\u00b0C) that the dark meat wants to be cooked to, it's going to be dry, flavourless, and generally unpleasant.\n| The white [[Meat|meat]] parts of the [[Turkey|turkey]] are the breasts and wings. The dark [[Meat|meat]] are the [[Thighs|thighs]] and [[Drumsticks|drumsticks]]. Now, the wings and drumsticks are going to cook a bit faster than the bits of [[Meat|meat]] that are better attached to the bird. That said, you want the drumsticks cooked more, so don't worry so much about them. The wings, however, are probably worth attaching more firmly to the bird. You can do this by imagining you were twisting someone's arm behind their back. Do this with both wings. Once you figure out the right twist, you'll find that the tips of the wings will stay firmly in place near the centre of the back of the [[Turkey|turkey]] (near its backbone).\n| Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 260\u00b0C (500\u00b0F - Gas10 -Extremely hot. (You'll drop the temperature later, but start it hot to get a crispier, more flavourful skin. The effect will be to keep the [[Fat|fat]] from melting and rolling down the side of the [[Turkey|turkey]], which is only going to dry it out.) [[Roast]] at lowest level of the [[Oven|oven]].\n| Place the [[Turkey|turkey]] [[Drumstick|drumstick]] side down on a [[Roasting tray|roasting tray]] (with slots to allow drippings through into a pan), or on a rack sitting in a pan. You will need a [[Basting|basting]] tool to get the drippings from this pan throughout the [[Roasting|roasting]] process.\n| Place the [[Turkey|turkey]] in the [[Oven|oven]].\n| After about 30 minutes, drop the heat to 350 \u00b0F (176.7\u00b0C), remove from [[Oven|oven]] and put a tent of [[Aluminium foil|aluminium foil]] loosely over the breast of the [[Turkey|turkey]]. This is going to keep the breast [[Meat|meat]] from overcooking and [[Drying|drying]] out.\n| For optimum safety and uniform doneness, it is recommended to cook [[Stuffing|stuffing]] outside the bird.\n|The internal temperature should be checked with a [[Food thermometer|food thermometer]] and the breast must reach a minimum of 161 \u00b0F (71.67\u00b0C) before removing it from the [[Oven|oven]]. The [[Thigh|thigh]], ideally, will be around 180\u00b0F (82.2\u00b0C) at this point. It should take about 2 &#190; to 3 hours to reach this temperature, a 14-16 pound bird should require a total of 2 to 2 1/2hours of [[Roasting|roasting]].\n| Let the bird stand 15-20 minutes before carving.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nThis recipe will work well with any sized turkey, from  3.8 kg [8.5 lb] to 6.3 kg [14 lb]\n===Recipe source===\n* http://en.wikibooks.org/wiki/Cookbook:Roasted_Brined_Turkey\n==See also==\n* '''[[Meat cooking time calculator Metric|A comprehensive guide to roast meat cooking times]]''' - give the time you want to carve your roast and we'll give you a timed step by step roasting guide\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Game recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Pickled]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#turkey #roast #brine #brownsugar #roasting #americanstylebrinedroastturkey #unusualrecipes #chicken #thigh #poultry #drumsticks </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Arnab bil tomatich (Rabbit with tomato); a  recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#rabbit #harissa #garlic #simmer #butter #onion #smen #tomato #bayleaves #unusualrecipes #sauce \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This rabbit recipe is from Algeria. \n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2113\n|PortionCalories = 528\n|DatePublished=19th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 55 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour 35 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Arnab bil tomatich (Rabbit with tomato) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Algerian rabbit?</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">What's not to like?</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nThis rabbit recipe is from Algeria.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 tablespoons [[olive oil]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[smen]] ([[Clarified butter|clarified butter]]) or 25 g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], finely chopped\n| [[Garlic]] to taste, finely chopped\n| 1 kg boneless [[Rabbit|rabbit]] [[Meat|meat]], cut into small chunks\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| 1 teaspoon or more of [[Harissa|harissa]]\n| 2 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]]\n| 600 ml water or [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]]\n| 450 g ripe [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]] and chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e diluted in 150 ml water\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] and the [[smen]] or [[Butter|butter]] in a large pan, add the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and saut\u00e9 until the onion is soft.\n| Add the [[Rabbit|rabbit]] pieces, stir, cover and [[Fry|fry]] for 15-20 minutes, stirring often to ensure that the [[Meat|meat]] is sealed on all sides.\n| Stir in the [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]], [[Harissa|harissa]], [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]], [[Cumin|cumin]] and water or [[Stock|stock]] and bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| Reduce the heat, cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 40 minutes.\n| Stir in the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e into the pan and [[Simmer|simmer]] for a further 20-30 minutes until the [[Sauce|sauce]] has thickened and the [[Rabbit|rabbit]] is tender.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Steamed rice|steamed rice]] or [[Pasta|pasta]].\n===Variations===\nInstead of [[Rabbit|rabbit]], you could use [[Chicken|chicken]] or [[Turkey|turkey]], both of which are consumed in Algeria.  Alternatively, you could try [[Pheasant|pheasant]] or [[Partridge|partridge]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Arnab bil tomatich (rabbit with tomato)]]\n[[Category:Algerian recipes|Arnab bil tomatich (rabbit with tomato)]]\n[[Category:Game recipes|Arnab bil tomatich (rabbit with tomato)]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Arnab bil tomatich (rabbit with tomato)]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Arnab bil tomatich (rabbit with tomato)]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Arnab bil tomatich (rabbit with tomato)]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Arnab bil tomatich (rabbit with tomato)]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Arnab bil tomatich (rabbit with tomato)]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rabbit #harissa #garlic #simmer #butter #onion #smen #tomato #bayleaves #unusualrecipes #sauce </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Baba ghanoush",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Baba ghanoush, Greek recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#babaghanoush #barbecue #tahini #aubergines #paprika #oliveoil #pittabreads #lemon #aubergine #yogurt #garlic \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Baba Ghanoush or Baba-Ganouj, babaganus, patlican salatasi (Turkish), melitzanosalata (Greek), mutabal (Armenian), salata de vinete (Romanian), Baigan\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2401\n|PortionCalories = 600\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = My version, with the addition of a roasted red pepper\n|Servings = 4 as a mezze\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 35 minutes\n|PrepTime = 35 minutes\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Baba ghanoush recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n}}\n\nBaba Ghanoush or Baba-Ganouj, babaganus, patlican salatasi (Turkish), melitzanosalata (Greek), mutabal (Armenian), salata de vinete (Romanian), Baigan Bharta (Hindi) ,Vangyache Bharit (Marathi), padlizs\u00e1nkr\u00e9m (Hungarian) is a kind of popular Middle Eastern dish made primarily of [[aubergine]] ([[eggplant]]) , [[mashed]], and mixed with various seasonings. Frequently the [[aubergine]] is [[baked]] or [[broiled]] over an open flame before peeling, so that the pulp is soft and has a smoky taste.\n\nBaba ghanoush is usually eaten as a dip with [[pita bread]], and is sometimes added to other dishes. It is usually of an earthy light brown colour.\n==A better recipe than this one!==\nAfter a few experiments, I've come up with a recipe that is far superior to the original in my opinion.  It's not too different but the addition of more [[garlic]], frying the garlic and adding the roasted [[red pepper]] makes it more robust and adds a little sweetness too.\n\n* '''[[Baba ghanoush with roasted red pepper]]'''\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 3 [[aubergines]]\n| 4 tablespoons light [[tahini]]\n| 2 [[cloves garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[yogurt]]\n| Juice from half a [[lemon]] or [[lime]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[paprika]]\n| 4 [[Pitta breads]] or [[crispbreads]]\n| Handful of crushed [[walnuts]] or [[toasted]] flaked [[almonds]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cook the [[aubergines]] over a hot grill or [[barbecue]]  until the skins are well burnt\n| Turn them regularly\n| You can also impale them on [[skewers]] (better metal than wooden ones) and roast them over the [[barbecue]], again turning often\n| Set them aside to cool\n| Halve them and scoop out the soft flesh\n| Put the flesh into a [[food processor]] together with the [[Garlic|garlic]],  [[yogurt]] and [[tahini]]. Season to taste with [[salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n| Blend into a smooth paste and add the [[lemon]] or [[lime juice]]\n| Drizzle with the [[olive oil]] and sprinkled with [[paprika]] and crushed [[nuts]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with warm [[pitta breads]] or [[crispbread]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Turkish Hummus?</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Not really an aubergine fan as I find them a bit dull, but this is a good way to eat them, if you have to.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Greek recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Turkish recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#babaghanoush #barbecue #tahini #aubergines #paprika #oliveoil #pittabreads #lemon #aubergine #yogurt #garlic </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Baba ghanoush with roasted red pepper",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Baba ghanoush with roasted red pepper a Greek recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pittabreads #aubergines #tahini #babaghanoushwithroastedredpepper #barbecue #redpepper #yogurt #lemon #aubergine #mashed #almonds \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I think this version is more interesting and has a degree of sweetness\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1421\n|PortionCalories = 355\n|DatePublished=30th March 2014\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = 4 as a mezze\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 35 minutes\n|PrepTime = 35 minutes\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Baba ghanoush recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Thanks Jerry</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Much nicer then the original recipe</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Barbecuing the aubergines.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Roasting the aubergines and red pepper on a barbecue]]\nBaba Ghanoush or Baba-Ganouj, babaganus, patlican salatasi (Turkish), melitzanosalata (Greek), mutabal (Armenian), salata de vinete (Romanian), Baigan Bharta (Hindi) ,Vangyache Bharit (Marathi), padlizs\u00e1nkr\u00e9m (Hungarian) is a kind of popular Middle Eastern dish made primarily of [[aubergine]] ([[eggplant]]) , [[mashed]], and mixed with various seasonings. Frequently the [[aubergine]] is [[baked]] or [[broiled]] over an open flame before peeling, so that the pulp is soft and has a smoky taste.\n\nBaba ghanoush is usually eaten as a dip with [[pita bread]], and is sometimes added to other dishes. It is usually of an earthy light brown colour.\n\nThe [[Baba ghanoush|original baba ghanoush recipe can be found here]], but I think this version is more interesting and has a degree of sweetness.\n\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 [[aubergines]]\n| Half a [[red pepper]]\n| 2 heaped tablespoons light [[tahini]]\n| 4 fat [[cloves garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 4 tablespoons of olive oil\n| 3 tablespoons [[yogurt]]\n| Juice and zest from half a [[lemon]] or [[lime]]\n| A good pinch of salt\n| A pinch of whole cumin seeds\n| 4 [[Pitta breads]] or [[crispbreads]]\n| A few olives, walnuts or [[toasted]] flaked [[almonds]] to garnish\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Brush the [[aubergines]] and the [[red pepper]] with a little olive oil and roast over a hot grill or [[barbecue]]  until the skins are well burnt\n| Turn them regularly, about 5 to 6 minutes a side will be fine.\n| You can also impale them on [[skewers]] (better metal than wooden ones) and roast them over the [[barbecue]], again turning often\n| Set them aside to cool, ideally in a sealed [[Lock & Lock]] box\n| Scoop out the soft flesh, discarding the outer skin but reserving some of the toasted sut surfaces.\n| Crush the garlic and saute in 4 tablespoons of [[olive oil]]. Don't let it burn.  At the last minute, add the whole cumin seeds.  Allow the oil to cool before processing.\n| Put the scooped flesh into a [[food processor]] together with the [[Garlic|garlic]],  [[yogurt]] and [[tahini]]. Season to taste with [[salt]]\n| Blend into a smooth paste and add the [[lemon]] zest and juice\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe, garnished with olives and nuts, accompanied by warm [[pitta breads]] or [[crispbread]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Greek recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Turkish recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pittabreads #aubergines #tahini #babaghanoushwithroastedredpepper #barbecue #redpepper #yogurt #lemon #aubergine #mashed #almonds </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Baharat",
                "revisions": [

                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Baharat recipe Accompaniments \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#baharat #spice #paprika #spices #nutmeg #cuminseeds #blackpepper #dried #corianderseeds #cinnamon #blackpeppercorns \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Baharat is a spice mixture or blend used throughout the Levant, in Lebanese, Syrian, Jordanian, Iraqi, Libyan and Palestinian cuisine\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 20\n|PortionCalories = 20\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Baharat in a large airtight container\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 3\n|TotalTime = 15 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Baharat.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Lovely warm spice</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.8</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Great for sprinkling on veggies!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n<!-- [[Image:Baharat recipe.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Typical baharat ingredients]] -->\nBah\u0101r\u0101t is a [[Spice|spice]] mixture or blend used throughout the Levant, in Lebanese, Syrian, Jordanian, Iraqi, Libyan and Palestinian cuisine. Baharat, in Arabic, means \"[[Spices|spices]]\". The name originated in Medieval India, as Bh\u0101rat, a Sanskrit name for India, was the source of these [[Spices|spices]]. The mixture of finely [[Ground|ground]] spices is often used to season [[Lamb|lamb]], [[Fish|fish]], [[Chicken|chicken]], [[Beef|beef]], and [[Soups|soups]]. Additionally, it may be used as a [[Condiment|condiment]], to add more flavour after a meal has been prepared.\n\nUnless you are going to use tons of the stuff, assume half or even a quarter of a teaspoon for one part\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 parts [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| 3 parts [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]]\n| 3 parts [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]]\n| 3 parts [[Cloves|cloves]]\n| 4 parts [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| 1 part [[Cardamom pods|cardamom pods]]\n| 3 parts [[Nutmeg|nutmeg]]\n| 6 parts [[Paprika|paprika]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Grind all of the ingredients to a fine powder in a [[Spice|spice]] mill or [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]].\n| [[Dried]] and pulverised [[Kaffir lime leaves|kaffir lime leaves]] can also be added to taste.\n| The mixture can be rubbed into [[Meat|meat]] or mixed with [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and [[Lime juice|lime juice]] to form a [[Marinade|marinade]].\n}}\n\n===Servings===\nServes 20 - Makes a small jar of baharat\n===Variations===\n'''Possible ingredients may be:'''\n[[Allspice]]\n[[Black peppercorns]]\n[[Cardamom seeds]]\n[[Cassia bark]]\n[[Cloves]]\n[[Coriander seeds]]\n[[Cumin seeds]]\n[[Nutmeg]]\n[[Dried red chili peppers]] or [[Paprika|paprika]]\nTurkish baharat includes [[Mint|mint]] as a key ingredient. In Tunisia, bharat refers to a simple mixture of [[Dried|dried]] rosebuds and [[Ground cinnamon|ground cinnamon]], often combined with [[Black pepper|black pepper]]. In the Gulf States, loomi (dried black [[Lime|lime]]) and [[Saffron|saffron]] may also be used for the kebsa [[Spice|spice]] mixture (also called \"Gulf baharat\").\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#baharat #spice #paprika #spices #nutmeg #cuminseeds #blackpepper #dried #corianderseeds #cinnamon #blackpeppercorns </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Barbecued Harissa lamb, Barbecue recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#lamb #barbecuedharissalamb #barbecue #garlic #lemon #harissa #seeds #homemadepittabreads #pestleandmortar #miseenplace #griddled \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A kettle barbecue will give this lamb a deeply smoky flavour, but you can cook it just as well on an open one\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4952\n|PortionCalories = 825\n|DatePublished=19th August 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Served in a [[homemade pitta bread]] with a salad\n |Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 1 hour\n |PrepTime = 30 minutes\n |CookTime = 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Barbecued Harissa lamb recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">As good as it looks</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">The perfect spicy kebab, made at home.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nA kettle [[Barbecue|barbecue]] will give this [[Lamb|lamb]] a deeply smoky flavour, but you can cook it just as well on an open one.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 tablespoon of [[coriander seeds]] \n| 1 tablespoon of [[cumin seeds]] \n| 3 tablespoons of Belazu Rose [[Harissa]] \n| juice of 1 [[lemon]] \n| Belazu [[extra virgin olive oil]] \n| 3 cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]] \n| 1.6 kg leg of [[lamb]], boned and butterflied (ask your butcher to do this for you)\n| I used a frozen half-leg of lamb and [[butterflied]] it myself.  It was a bit of a fiddle but it worked out fine in the end! \n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 230\u00b0 C (450\u00b0 F - gas 8) if not using a [[Barbecue|barbecue]]\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Marinaded half-leg of lamb cooked.jpg|After 3 hours in the oven\nImage:Marinaded half-leg of lamb.jpg|Marinaded, ready to cook\nImage:Butterflied half-leg of lamb.jpg|A poorly butterflied leg of lamb\nImage:Half-leg of lamb.jpg|Half-leg of (frozen) lamb, defrosted<br />[\u00a36.50 Morrisons - August 2013]\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the [[Seeds|seeds]] in a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]] and crush slightly. \n| Mix the [[Harissa]], [[Lemon|lemon]], 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Spices|spices]] together, smear over the [[Lamb|lamb]]\n| [[Marinate|marinate]] for at least one hour. \n| Season well and cook on a heated [[Barbecue|barbecue]] with the lid on for 25-30 minutes, turning a couple of times. \n| Allow to rest for 10 minutes before carving.\n}}\n(''[[Olive]] magazine'')\n\n===Serving suggestion===\nServe in [[homemade pitta breads]] with a selection of chopped salad vegetables.\n\n===Chef's notes===\nWhen preparing this dish, the decision to barbecue or not was weather dependant, in the end I decided not to barbecue.  After butterflying the half-leg of lamb, and seeing how cartilaginous and sinewy the meat was, I thought slow cooking would give a far better result than cooking quickly in the oven or even barbecuing.  This was a great decision as the resulting meat just fell apart, juicy and tender.\n\nI placed marinated meat on an uncovered grill tray at the top of the highest setting on my oven (260\u00b0C [500\u00b0F) Gas 10]\tand left for 15 minutes, then I reduced the oven to 180\u00b0C [350\u00b0F - Gas 4] placed meat in an oven tray covered in tin-foil and cooked for another 2.5 hours.  It looks burnt from the picture, but if you look at the kebab in the pitta you'll see how tender it was - with no gristle.\n\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/products/extra virgin-olive-oils.html Belazu Extra virgin olive oil]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/rose-harissa.html Belazu Rose Harissa]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mutton recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lamb #barbecuedharissalamb #barbecue #garlic #lemon #harissa #seeds #homemadepittabreads #pestleandmortar #miseenplace #griddled </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Andy Bates turns baker, whipping up this surprisingly easy no-fuss [[Flatbread|flatbread]] ([[pitta bread]]). Your guests will love the way it pops on the BBQ, and that you went the extra mile to make homemade simple and fresh [[Bread|bread]] for their [[Sausages|sausages]]!\n\nThis recipe is reproduced courtesy of [[Debbie&andrew's sausages|debbie&andrew's sausages]]\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 500g [[Strong white flour|strong white flour]] or Udi's [[Gluten free|gluten free]] [[All purpose flour|all purpose flour]] Mix \n| 10g [[Salt|salt]]\n| 25g [[Caster Sugar|caster sugar]]\n| 10g instant [[Yeast|yeast]]\n| 20ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 360ml tepid water\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Mix together the [[Flour|flour]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Yeast|yeast]]. Add the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and 270ml of the water. Mix the ingredients together. Gradually add the remaining water until all the flour has come away from the sides of the bowl and you have a soft [[Dough|dough]].\n| Place the [[Dough|dough]] on the worktop and [[Knead|knead]] for 5-10 minutes. The dough will be wet in the beginning but will form a smooth dough once kneaded. Place in an oiled bowl, cover and leave to double in size.\n| Remove the [[Cling Film|cling film]] and [[Punch|punch]] back the [[Dough|dough]] (feels good!). On a floured surface, tear off a piece of dough roughly the size of a golfball and roll into a circle about 5-10mm thick.\n| Just before [[Baking|baking]], [[Brush|brush]] the surface of the [[Breads|breads]] with [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and place on the [[Barbecue|barbecue]] for 3-4 minutes on each side. Nice, simple and fresh [[Flatbreads|flatbreads]], perfect with your favourite [[Sausages|sausages]].\n}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Gluten free recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Debbie&andrew's sausage recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n{{Template:DebbieAndAndrew attribution}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#dough #oliveoil #sausages #barbecueflatbread #yeast #pittabread #flatbreads #punch #baking #bread #brush </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Basal mahchi (Stuffed onions)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Basal mahchi (Stuffed onions), Egg recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#onions #parsley #almonds #lamb #raisins #butter #yoghurt #egg #breadcrumbs #boil #simmer \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Throughout North Africa and the Middle East, the onion is a favourite vegetable and there are many versions of this recipe\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1572\n|PortionCalories = 262\n|DatePublished=17th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Basal mahchi (Stuffed onions) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Just like stiffed mushrooms</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.25</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">..only more onioney!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nThroughout [[North Africa and the Middle East]], the [[Onions|onion]] is a favourite [[Vegetable|vegetable]] and there are many versions of this recipe.  This particular one comes from the city of Benghazi in Libya.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 6 large [[Onions|onions]], peeled and left whole with roots intact\n| 175 g [[Minced|minced]] [[Lamb|lamb]]\n| 25 g chopped [[Almonds|almonds]]\n| 25 g [[Raisins|raisins]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| 110 g [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Parsley|parsley]], finely chopped\n| 25 g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 300 ml [[Yoghurt|yogurt]]\n| 1 large [[Egg|egg]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Bring the [[Onions|onions]] to the [[Boil|boil]] in a large saucepan, reduce the heat and them [[Simmer|simmer]] for 10-12 minutes.\n| Drain and set aside until cool enough to handle.\n| Carefully slice &frac12; cm from each root end and using an [[Apple|apple]] corer, hollow out the centre until the outer layers about 1 cm thick.\n| Chop the removed [[Onion|onion]] layers and place in a large bowl with the [[Lamb|lamb]], [[Almonds|almonds]], [[Raisins|raisins]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]], [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]] and 2 tablespoons of the [[Parsley|parsley]].  Mix well.\n| Fill the [[Onions|onions]] with the mixture and place them a a greased ovenproof dish.\n| Dot the [[Onions|onions]] with the [[Butter|butter]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 1 hour at 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4).\n| Mix the [[Egg|egg]] with the [[Yoghurt|yogurt]] thoroughly and pour over the [[Onions|onions]].\n| Continue [[Baking|baking]] for a further 10 minutes, then garnish with the remaining [[Parsley|parsley]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Bread|bread]], [[Salad|salad]] or [[Pickles|pickles]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Basal mahchi (stuffed onions)]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes|Basal mahchi (stuffed onions)]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes|Basal mahchi (stuffed onions)]]\n[[Category:Libyan recipes|Basal mahchi (stuffed onions)]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Basal mahchi (stuffed onions)]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Basal mahchi (stuffed onions)]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Basal mahchi (stuffed onions)]]\n[[Category:Starters|Basal mahchi (stuffed onions)]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Basal mahchi (stuffed onions)]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#onions #parsley #almonds #lamb #raisins #butter #yoghurt #egg #breadcrumbs #boil #simmer </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Basbousa",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Basbousa, Greek recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#basbousa #semolina #butter #honey #bakingpowder #bakingsoda #boil #cream #almond #bake #bakingtray \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Basbousa, basboosa,(Arabic), ravani (Turkish) or revani (Greek \u03c1\u03b1\u03b2\u03b1\u03bd\u03b9 and \u03c1\u03b5\u03b2\u03b1\u03bd\u03b9) is a sweet cake made of a semolina soaked in syrup\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3681\n|PortionCalories = 245\n|DatePublished=27th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 15 - Makes 1 cake\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 40 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Basbousa recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Kate Bush song, shurely?</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">So this is what she was singing about, it must be good \ud83e\udd13</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\n\n'''Basbousa''', '''basboosa''',(Arabic), '''ravani''' (Turkish) or '''revani''' (Greek \u03c1\u03b1\u03b2\u03b1\u03bd\u03af and \u03c1\u03b5\u03b2\u03b1\u03bd\u03af) is a sweet cake made of a [[Semolina|semolina]] soaked in syrup. [[Coconut]] is a popular addition to the cake. Although Greeks of Southern Greeks call it '''ravani''', in the north it is called '''revani''', as in Turkish, specifically in the town of Veria where it has been the traditional dessert for many years.\n\nIt is found in the cuisines of the eastern Mediterranean under a variety of names. It appears to be a variant of the Egyptian dish '''ma'mounia'''. Basbousa is very common is Arabia.\n\nBasbousa is routinely called \"'''Hareesa'''\" in arabic countries such as Palestine. It is said to have originated as Hareesa before subsequent movements by other countries (such as Iraq, Turkey, and Libya) who shifted the name to Basbousa.\n\nThere are many varieties, of which this is just one!\n\n\n'''Syrup'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2.25 cups [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 1.5 cups water\n| [[Juice]] of 1 [[Lemon|lemon]] (or 2 tablespoons [[Orange juice|orange juice]])\n| 1 teaspoon [[Honey|honey]]\n}}\n'''Cake'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 cups [[Semolina|semolina]]\n| 1 cup [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 113 g (4 oz) [[Butter|butter]], softened\n| 1 cup whole [[Milk|milk]]\n| 1.5 teaspoons [[Vanilla extract|vanilla extract]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Baking powder|baking powder]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Baking soda|baking soda]]\n| 2 [[free range eggs]]\n| [[Blanched]] split [[Almonds|almonds]] to garnish\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4)\n===Method===\n'''Syrup'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a medium saucepan, dissolve the [[Sugar|sugar]] in water.\n| Add the [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] and bring to a [[Boil|boil]].\n| Once the syrup starts to [[Boil|boil]], stir in the [[Honey|honey]].\n| Reduce the heat and allow [[Simmer|simmer]]  for about 8-10 minutes.\n| Remove from heat and set aside.\n}}\n'''Cake'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Lightly grease and [[Flour|flour]] a 23 cm x 30 cm (9\"x12\") [[baking tray]].\n| [[Cream]] the [[Butter|butter]] and [[Sugar|sugar]] in a mixing bowl.\n| Add the [[Eggs|eggs]] and stir in the [[vanilla]].\n| In a separate bowl, combine [[Semolina|semolina]], [[Baking powder|baking powder]], and [[Baking soda|baking soda]].\n| Slowly add to [[Butter|butter]] and [[Egg|egg]] mixture and then stir in the [[Milk|milk]].\n| Pour the mixture into [[Baking|baking]] dish and smooth with a spatula.\n| Take a knife and scribe a diamond pattern in the top and place an [[Almond|almond]] in the centre of each diamond. [[Bake]] for 25 minutes.\n| Remove cake from [[Oven|oven]] and the pour syrup over the cake until no more can be absorbed.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nAllow to cool for 20 minutes before serving.\n\nServe with [[Cinnamon ice-cream|cinnamon ice-cream]]\n===Variations===\nA little [[Rose water|rose water]] can be added in place of the water.\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Greek recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Turkish recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#basbousa #semolina #butter #honey #bakingpowder #bakingsoda #boil #cream #almond #bake #bakingtray </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

Add some [[Beans|beans]] for body, [[Peppers|peppers]] for richness and [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]], just because you can, you have a complete, gorgeous meal. Try it\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 400 g can of [[Haricot beans|haricot beans]], rinsed many times and then drained.\n| 2 sweet [[Bell peppers|bell peppers]], any colour.\n| 1 [[Fennel bulb|fennel bulb]], sliced finely, green tops reserved, if you are lucky enough to find a seller that retains them!\n| Half an [[Onion|onion]], very thinly sliced.\n| A small handful of freshly chopped [[oregano leaves]].\n| A large handful of freshly chopped [[parsley leaves]].\n| 1 tablespoon of [[olive oil]]\n| [[Sea salt]] & [[freshly ground black pepper]] to taste.\n| A squeeze of fresh [[lemon juice]].\n| 1 teaspoon [[fennel seeds]], bruised in a [[mortar and pestle]].\n| 3 teaspoons of [[sherry vinegar]].\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* [[Roasted red pepper|Roast the bell peppers as shown here]], remove skin and seeds then tear into strips.\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the beans, sliced [[fennel]], [[fennel seeds]] and [[onions]] together with the [[roasted pepper]] strips in a serving bowl. Add the [[parsley]], [[oregano]] and reserved [[fennel tops]] if you had any. Toss well.\n| Drizzle with [[sherry vinegar]], [[lemon juice]] and [[olive oil]], Season with salt and pepper and toss again..\n}}\n===Alternatives===\nTry a variety of [[beans]], most beans work very well in a salad like this.  [[Butter beans]], [[chick peas]]. [[kidney beans]] etc.  Dried beans are good too if you remember to prepare them ahead of time.\n\nTry [[cumin seeds]] instead of [[fennel seeds]]\n===Chef's note===\nIf you can't find [[sherry vinegar]], then try harder as it's an invaluable condiment Or use [[red wine vinegar]] with a pinch of sugar!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#sherryvinegar #fennelseeds #beansaladwithfennelandroastedpeppers #beans #fennel #oliveoil #onion #lemonjuice #salad #bellpeppers #fennelbulb </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

The salty toasted halloumi cheese compliments the sweet falafel\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4440\n|PortionCalories = 740\n|DatePublished=13th August 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 6\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour 10 minutes\n|PrepTime =  40 minutes\n|CookTime =  30 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Beetroot falafel with toasted halloumi cheese recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Perfect veggie meal</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Just made this again for some vegetarian friends who thought it was fabulous!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis [[Vegetarian|vegetarian]] [[Salad|salad]] make a visually exciting meal that is also healthy.  The salty  [[Toasted|toasted]] [[Halloumi cheese|halloumi cheese]] compliments the sweet [[Falafel|falafel]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 1 x 250 g pack of [[Halloumi cheese|halloumi cheese]]\n| 1 medium [[Onions|onion]], peeled and sliced\n| 2 teaspoons [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], ground to a fine powder [[coffee grinder]] or a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]]\n| 1 teaspoon of [[coriander seeds]], ground to a fine powder [[coffee grinder]] or a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]]\n| 1 teaspoon of [[fenugreek seeds]], ground to a fine powder [[coffee grinder]] or a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]]\n| 1 teaspoon of [[chilli powder]]\n| 1 tablespoon of freshly chopped [[parsley]]\n| 1 [[Free range egg|free range egg]]\n| 300 g (10.5 oz) pre cooked (but not pickled) [[Beetroot|beetroot]]. Trimmed, peeled and very roughly chopped\n| 100g (4 oz) [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]]\n| 2 x 400g cans of [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] drain and rinsed well under cold running water\n| 1 tablespoon light [[Tahini|tahini]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n'''to serve'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 300 ml [[Yogurt|yogurt]]\n| 1 tablespoon light [[Tahini|tahini]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add a tablespoon or so of the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] to a [[Frying pan|frying pan]] and give it a good twist of [[Black pepper|black pepper]].\n| Saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]] over a low heat for about 5 minutes - don't [[Brown|brown]] them.\n| Add the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] and [[Fry|fry]] for a further minute or so.\n| Allow to cool for a few minutes then add to a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade.  Don't run until all of the ingredients have been added\n| Add to this; the [[Beetroot|beetroot]], [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]], 1 tablespoon of [[Tahini|tahini]], the [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]] and the [[Egg|egg]].\n| Blitz to a rough consistency, don't over-[[Blend|blend]]. Aim for some texture, not babyfood.\n| Ideally, leave the mixture to rest for 30 minutes or more before cooking to allow the breadcrumbs to rehydrate a little\n| Using you hands, form into about 20 golf-ball sized balls and them flatten into patties.  A great tip from Jamie Oliver's 15 minutes meals, when moulding [[falafel]]s is to wet your hands first.  This prevents the gooey mixture from sticking to your hands.\n| Gently [[shallow fry]] for 15 to 20 minutes until crusted and caramelised on the outside.  \n| Meanwhile, slice the [[Halloumi|halloumi]] width-wise into about 10 slices, [[Spray|spray]] with [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and [[Griddle|griddle]] until nicely [[Toasted|toasted]] - it won't melt.\n| Mix a tablespoon or so of the [[Tahini|tahini]] into the [[Yogurt|yogurt]], season and mix well to serve as a [[Dip|dip]].\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Beetroot falafel balls.jpg|Half to cook now, half to freeze\nImage:Beetroot falafel with toasted halloumi cheese_ingredients.jpg|Beetroot falafel mixture, ready to rest\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe on a bed of [[Green salad|green salad]] with the [[Toasted|toasted]] [[Halloumi|halloumi]], the [[Yogurt|yogurt]] [[Dip|dip]] and warm [[Pitta breads|pitta breads]].\n===Variations===\nThese could also be [[oven baked]] or [[Deep-fried|deep-fried]] until crisped on the outside.\n\nThese could be shaped into balls, laid out on [[greaseproof paper]] over a baking tray, placed in the [[freezer]] then bagged up once completely frozen for later use.  I would be inclined to allow them to completely defrost before cooking, especially if you were to fry them.\n===Chef's notes===\nI did make these with whole spices, but the effect was rather bland so have amended to finely ground spices which should 'spread' the flavour further.\n\nThe falafel pictured were oven baked.  Next time I would flatten them and shallow fry them so the outsides caramelise.  This did not happen with oven baking.\n\nOven directions: Heat [[Oven|oven]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6), [fan oven 180\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour], spread out on a baking tray and spray or brush with [[olive oil]] before baking for 3 minutes.\n{{SeeAlso-HalloumiRecipes}}\n* [[Beetroot recipes|Our favourite beetroot recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Greek recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes]]\n[[Category:Turkish recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beetrootfalafelwithtoastedhalloumicheese #tahini #oliveoil #yogurt #coffeegrinder #mortarandpestle #toasted #beetroot #falafel #breadcrumbs #dip </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Belazu Chicken Couscous, Meat recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#belazuchickencouscous #couscous #arganoil #ginger #chicken #onion #saffron #harissapaste #wok #bouquetgarni #herb \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is a great recipe for you to try out your argan oil\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2795\n|PortionCalories = 465\n|DatePublished=28th July 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 45 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Belazu Chicken Couscous recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Lovely harissa</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Harissa paste makes the difference. To be honest, I could not tell if the argan oil made it taste any different.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Belazu Chicken Couscous simmer.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chicken ready to simmer]]\nThis is a great recipe for you to try out your [[argan oil]].  It's also a nice way to cook chicken.\n\nTraditional [[Harissa paste|harissa paste]] really [[Spices|spices]] up the [[Couscous|couscous]].\n\nTo serve less, use the same amount of rub and herbs, just cover with less stock.  One chicken leg per person is ample.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.3 kg [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces (6 chicken legs) \n| 1 teaspoon [[Ground|ground]] [[Ginger|ginger]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Black pepper|black pepper]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]] \n| 1 sachet [[Saffron|saffron]] filaments \n| 4 tablespoons of [[Belazu]] [[Argan oil]] \n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and sliced\n| 200 ml [[Chicken stock]] or [[vegetable stock]] to cover the chicken pieces.\n| Big sprig of your choice of herbs - [[Bouquet garni|a good list of suggestions here]]\n| 120 g [[couscous]] (''Follow the link for cooking instructions'')\n}}\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces in a bowl with the [[Ginger|ginger]], [[Pepper|pepper]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Saffron|saffron]]. Rub these in using your hands.\n|[[Brown|brown]] in a [[wok]] or [[Casserole dish|casserole dish]] with the [[argan oil]].\n| Add the sliced [[Onion|onion]], and soften for 2-3 minutes, then top up with enough stock to just cover the chicken pieces.\n| Make a [[Herb|herb]] bundle by tying the herb sprigs together with [[kitchen string]] and add to the [[wok]] or [[Casserole|casserole]]. | Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] then reduce to a [[Simmer|simmer]] for 30 minutes or until cooked.\n| Remove the cooked chicken and serve, discarding the stock and herbs.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with  [[Harissa paste|harissa paste]] and [[Barley|barley]] [[Couscous|couscous]] or normal couscous.\n===Chef's notes===\nThe original recipe did not specify the cuts of chicken to use, but in this type of dish the flavour is much improved by using cuts that include the bone rather than fillets.  I would skin them first though so the end result is not too greasy.\n\nHalf a [[green pepper]] was chopped and added to the [[couscous]] together with some dried fruit that had been soaked in sherry for 30 minutes.  The rest of the pepper was added to the chicken casserole and discarded once the chicken was cooked.\n\nI used [[fennel]], [[parsley]], [[mint]] and a small amount of [[rosemary]] in my [[bouquet garni]].\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/argan-oil.html Belazu Argan Oil]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/rose-harissa.html Belazu Rose Harissa]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/traditional-barley-couscous.html Belazu Traditional Barley Couscous]\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes|Chicken couscous]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Chicken couscous]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken couscous]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chicken couscous]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes|Chicken couscous]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes|Chicken couscous]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Chicken couscous]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken couscous]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Chicken couscous]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Chicken couscous]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes|Chicken couscous]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#belazuchickencouscous #couscous #arganoil #ginger #chicken #onion #saffron #harissapaste #wok #bouquetgarni #herb </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Berbere recipe, a chili meat rub \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#berbere #ajowan #fry #seeds #cuminseeds #allspice #mortarandpestle #spices #blackpepper #coffeegrinder #cinnamonstick \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A fiery spice mixture originating from the Arabian/African areas around Eritrea, Ethiopia and Somalia\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 24\n|PortionCalories = 24\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 1\n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Berbere spice mix recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Hot, hot, hot!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Nice and spicy</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nA fiery [[Spice|spice]] mixture originating from the Arabian/African areas around Eritrea, Ethiopia and Somalia.\n\nIt is used as a rub for [[Meats|meats]], seasoning for [[Meat|meat]] and [[Lentil|lentil]] [[Stews|stews]] or just as a [[Condiment|condiment]].  As with [[All spice|all spice]] mixes, this is just one variant of many.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 20 [[Dried|dried]] [[Bird's eye chillies|bird's eye chillies]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]]\n| [[Seeds]] from 8 [[Green cardamoms|green cardamoms]]\n| 12 [[Allspice berries|allspice berries]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Ground|ground]] [[Ginger|ginger]]\n| 1 teaspoon white [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Black cumin|black cumin]] [[Seeds|seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Fenugreek seeds|fenugreek seeds]]\n| 8 [[Cloves|cloves]]\n| 2\" [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]], cracked into pieces\n| &#189; teaspoon [[ajowan]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Black peppercorns|black peppercorns]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Roughly crush the [[Chillies|chillies]] and dry [[Fry|fry]] for 3 minutes\n| Add the remaining whole [[Spices|spices]] and dry [[Fry|fry]] for a further 5 minutes\n| Allow to cool\n| Grind to a fine powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]]\n| Store in an airtight container for up to 3 months\n}}\n===Servings===\nServes 10 - Makes 1 jar\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you cannot obtain [[ajowan]], use [[Caraway seeds|caraway seeds]] or [[Dried thyme|dried thyme]] instead.\n\nI have seen versions of this recipe that use [[long pepper]], which can be difficult to obtain in Europe. Use normal [[black pepper]] instead.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Dry fried]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#berbere #ajowan #fry #seeds #cuminseeds #allspice #mortarandpestle #spices #blackpepper #coffeegrinder #cinnamonstick </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Braised lamb shanks (slow cooker recipe)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Braised lamb shanks, a slow cooker recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#couscous #slowcooker #oliveoil #aubergine #shallots #lambstock #vegetable #apricots #unusualrecipes #passata #dice \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is a version of braised lamb shank for cooking in a slow cooker. It's a very nice recipe if you enjoy a sweet and fruity meat crockpot dish\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1333\n|PortionCalories = 666\n|DatePublished=13th May 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Braised Lamb Shanks with plain [[couscous]]\n |Servings = Serves 2 to 4\n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 5 hours 20 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 5 hours \n |Image = [[Image:Braised Lamb Shanks with couscous.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Food of The Gods</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">For mere mortals</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is a version of [[Braised Lamb Shanks|braised lamb shanks]] modified for cooking in a [[slow cooker]].\n\nIt's a very nice recipe if you enjoy a sweet and fruity meat dish.   It goes excellently with [[couscous]] and is quite filling so one lamb shank could stretch to two people.\n\n===Ingredients for 2 to 4 people===\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 or 3 small [[Lamb shanks|lamb shanks]] \n| 200g [[Shallots|shallots]], peeled ([[Shallots|see here for a neat trick]])\n| 1 medium [[Aubergine|aubergines]], cut into small [[Dice|dice]] \n| 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]] \n| 1 tablespoon of [[Harissa paste]] (I use my own and it's quite hot!) \n| Zest of 1 [[Orange|orange]] and [[Juice|juice]] of 2 large [[Oranges|oranges]] (''no more'')\n| 100ml medium [[Sherry|sherry]] \n| 375 g [[Passata|passata]] (or 1 400g can of chopped tomatoes) \n| 150 ml hot [[Vegetable|vegetable]] or [[Lamb stock|lamb stock]] \n| 50g dried [[apricots]] (soaked in the sherry if you have the time)\n| 75 g stoned [[cherries]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{recipeMethod\n\n| Heat just a teaspoon of the the oil in a large flameproof [[dutch oven]] or [[wok]] and [[Brown|brown]] the shanks all over. Allow about 8 minutes to do this as the better the colour now, the better the flavour and look of the finished dish.\n| Remove the [[Lamb|lamb]] and set aside. Add the [[Shallots|shallots]], [[Aubergine|aubergine]] and remaining [[Olive oil|olive oil]] to the [[Casserole|casserole]]. Return the casserole to the hob and cook everything together over a high heat, stirring from time to time, until the shallots and aubergine are golden and beginning to soften.\n| Add all of the ingredients to the [[slow cooker]], set to medium and cook for 5 hours.\n}}\n===Serving suggestion===\nServe with plain [[couscous]].  This is quite fruity and needs a bland accompaniment.\n\n===Chef's note===\nIt would probably be cooked in 3 hours, but I like to stew lamb long and slow if I have the time, it seems to extract all of the flavours.  It certainly smells fantastic during the last few hours of cooking.\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Braised Lamb Shanks after 5 hours.jpg|After 5 hours cooking\nImage:Braised Lamb Shanks ingredients.jpg|Braised Lamb Shanks, the ingredients (for 2)\n</gallery>\n\n==See also==\n* [[Slow roast recipes]]\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/rose-harissa.html Belazu Rose Harissa]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Mutton recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Slow cooked]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#couscous #slowcooker #oliveoil #aubergine #shallots #lambstock #vegetable #apricots #unusualrecipes #passata #dice </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Braised Lamb Shanks with cherries",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Lamb shanks braised in cherries recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#lamb #shallots #cherries #sherry #oliveoil #lambshanks #casserole #aubergines #orange #vegetable #lambstock \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Slow cooking the lamb shanks in sherry tenderises the meat and brings out the best flavours\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3561\n|PortionCalories = 593\n|DatePublished=22nd January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Braised Lamb Shanks with plain [[couscous]]\n |Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 3 hours 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 25 minutes\n |CookTime = 3 hours \n |Image = [[Image:Braised Lamb Shanks recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Cherries, every time</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.2</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Acidic cherries cut through the lamb fat and make a perfect pairing - they look good too.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Slow cooking]] the [[Lamb shanks|lamb shanks]] in [[Sherry|sherry]] tenderises the [[Meat|meat]] and brings out the best flavours.  The [[cherries]] are especially nice in this recipe as they balance the slightly fatty aspect of [[lamb]].\n===Ingredients for 6 people===\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 6 small [[Lamb shanks|lamb shanks]] \n| 450g [[Shallots|shallots]], peeled ([[Shallots|see here for a neat trick]])\n| 2 medium [[Aubergines|aubergines]], cut into small [[Dice|dice]] \n| 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]] \n| 3tbsp [[Belazu]] Rose [[Harissa]] \n| Pared rind of 1 [[Orange|orange]] and [[Juice|juice]] of 3 large [[Oranges|oranges]] \n| 200ml medium [[Sherry|sherry]] \n| 700g jar [[Passata|passata]] \n| 300ml hot [[Vegetable|vegetable]] or [[Lamb stock|lamb stock]] \n| 75g ready-to eat [[Apricots|apricots]]\n| 75g ready to eat [[Cherries|cherries]] \n| Large pinch of [[Saffron strands|saffron strands]]\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3)\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Braised Lamb Shanks ready for the oven.jpg|Ready for the oven\nImage:Shallots and aubergines browned.jpg|[[Shallots]] and [[aubergines]] [[browned]]\nImage:Braised Lamb Shanks ingredients.jpg|Braised Lamb Shanks, the ingredients (for 2)\n</gallery>\n\n===Method===\n\n{{recipeMethod\n\n| Heat just a teaspoon of the the oil in a large flameproof [[Casserole|casserole]] and [[Brown|brown]] the shanks all over. Allow 10-12 minutes to do this as the better the colour now, the better the flavour of the finished dish.\n| Remove the [[Lamb|lamb]] and set aside. Add the [[Shallots|shallots]], [[Aubergine|aubergine]] and remaining [[Olive oil|olive oil]] to the [[Casserole|casserole]]. Return the casserole to the hob and cook everything together over a high heat, stirring from time to time, until the shallots and aubergine are golden and beginning to soften.\n| Lower the heat and add the [[Lamb|lamb]] and all the other ingredients. The liquid should come halfway up the shanks. Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], then cover tightly and put in the [[Oven|oven]] for 2.5 hours. Test the lamb with a fork-it should be so tender it almost falls off the bone.\n| If the cooking liquid looks too thin, remove the [[Lamb|lamb]] to a heated platter, then [[Bubble|bubble]] the [[Sauce|sauce]] on the hob until reduced and thickened. Return the lamb to the [[Casserole|casserole]] and served with [[Couscous|couscous]].\n}}\n===Ingredients for 2 or 3 people===\nIngredients adjusted for 2 or 3.\n* 2 or 3 small [[Lamb shanks|lamb shanks]] \n* 200g [[Shallots|shallots]], peeled ([[Shallots|see here for a neat trick]])\n* 1 medium [[Aubergine|aubergine]], cut into small [[Dice|dice]] \n* 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]] \n* 1 tablespoon of [[Harissa paste]] (I use my own and it's quite hot!) \n* Zest of 1 [[Orange|orange]] and [[Juice|juice]] of 2 large [[Oranges|oranges]] \n* 100ml medium [[Sherry|sherry]] \n* 375 g [[Passata|passata]] (or 1 400g can of chopped tomatoes) \n* 150 ml hot [[Vegetable|vegetable]] or [[Lamb stock|lamb stock]] \n* 50g dried [[apricots]] (soaked in the sherry if you have the time)\n* 75 g stoned [[cherries]]\n* Pinch of [[Saffron strands|saffron strands]]\n(''Good House Keeping'') \n==See also==\n* [[Slow roast recipes]]\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/rose-harissa.html Belazu Rose Harissa]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Mutton recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes|Lamb shanks]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lamb #shallots #cherries #sherry #oliveoil #lambshanks #casserole #aubergines #orange #vegetable #lambstock </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Remove from the pan immediately. Grind into a powder using a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]] or the end of a [[Rolling pin|rolling pin]] in a bowl.\n| Put the [[Beans|beans]] in a large pan and add the [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]], [[Onion|onion]], [[Paprika|paprika]], [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and 6 tablespoons of cold water. Season, cover and bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| Turn down the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]], covered, for 10-15 mins until the [[Beans|beans]] are tender. (Less for [[defrosted]] [[Frozen|frozen]] [[Beans|beans]]). If necessary, top up the water.\n| Add the [[Coriander|coriander]], [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] and [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], then adjust the seasoning.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot or warm with [[Couscous|couscous]] and [[Griddled|griddled]] [[Lamb|lamb]] or river [[Trout|trout]].\n===Variations===\nTry this with other beans or even peas. [[French beans]] would be nice though you would probably want to reduce the cooking time a little.\n(''Good Housekeeping'')\n\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/products/extra virgin-olive-oils.html Belazu Extra virgin olive oil]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/belazu-pickled-lemons.html Belazu Preserved Lemon]\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#broadbeanswithpreservedlemon #beans #broadbeans #belazu #frozen #onion #defrosted #cuminseeds #coriander #preservedlemon #simmer </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Broad Beans with Preserved Lemon a vegetarian fruit recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#beans #coriander #preservedlemon #defrosted #cuminseeds #belazu #broadbeans #frozen #onion #lemon #oliveoil \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Baby broad beans are the best to use with this preserved lemon vegetarian recipe\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 471\n|PortionCalories = 78\n|DatePublished=22nd January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Broad Beans with Preserved Lemon\n |Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 5 minutes\n |CookTime = 25 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Broad Beans with Preserved Lemon recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Brilliant pairing</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">So tangy</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nBaby [[Broad beans|broad beans]] are the best to use with this recipe.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] \n| 500g (11lb 2 oz) small [[Broad beans|broad beans]], podded and shelled or [[Frozen|frozen]], [[defrosted]] \n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], thinly sliced \n| 1 tablespoon [[Smoked paprika|smoked paprika]] \n| 4 tablespoons of [[Belazu]] [[Extra virgin olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]] \n| 1 medium bunch of [[Coriander|coriander]], roughly chopped \n| &frac12; a [[Belazu]] [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] thinly sliced \n| [[Juice|juice]] of 1 [[Lemon|lemon]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Dry fry]] the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] in a small [[Frying pan|frying pan]] for 30 seconds until you smell the aroma. Remove from the pan immediately. Grind into a powder using a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]] or the end of a [[Rolling pin|rolling pin]] in a bowl.\n| Put the [[Beans|beans]] in a large pan and add the [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]], [[Onion|onion]], [[Paprika|paprika]], [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and 6 tablespoons of cold water. Season, cover and bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| Turn down the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]], covered, for 10-15 mins until the [[Beans|beans]] are tender. (Less for [[defrosted]] [[Frozen|frozen]] [[Beans|beans]]). If necessary, top up the water.\n| Add the [[Coriander|coriander]], [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] and [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], then adjust the seasoning.\n}}\n===Variations===\nTry this with other beans or even peas. [[French beans]] would be nice though you would probably want to reduce the cooking time a little.\n\n(''Good Housekeeping'')\n\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/products/extra virgin-olive-oils.html Belazu Extra virgin olive oil]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/belazu-pickled-lemons.html Belazu Preserved Lemon]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beans #coriander #preservedlemon #defrosted #cuminseeds #belazu #broadbeans #frozen #onion #lemon #oliveoil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

I prefer this cold or at room temperature though but just serve it directly if you want it hot.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 teaspoon [[Vegetable|vegetable]] [[Bouillon|bouillon]] powder or &#189; [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]] cube\n| 120 g dried [[couscous]]\n| Splash of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 2 Small [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Raisins|raisins]] or [[Sultanas|sultanas]]\n| 5 [[Dried apricots|dried apricots]]\n| &#189; a small head of [[Broccoli|broccoli]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Almond flakes|almond flakes]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Chop the [[Dried fruit|dried fruit]], place in a saucer and pour over the [[Sherry|sherry]].  Leave for as long as you can so the [[Fruit|fruit]] soaks up the sherry.\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Using [[Boiling|boiling]] water, make up 1.5 x the volume of the [[Couscous|couscous]] (1.5 cups of [[Stock|stock]] to 1 cup of couscous)\n| Add the [[Couscous|couscous]] to a bowl and pour over the [[Stock|stock]].  Mix well and leave until the water is absorbed, about 10 minutes.\n| [[Boil]] or [[Steam|steam]] the [[Broccoli|broccoli]] so it is to your liking.  Chop into small pieces.\n| [[Roast]] the [[Peppers|peppers]], remove the [[Seeds|seeds]] and membrane and chop into small pieces.\n| Toast the [[Almond flakes|almond flakes]] until [[Browned|browned]], be careful not to burn them as they turn very [[Bitter|bitter]] when burnt.\n| Pour the [[Dried fruit|dried fruit]] and any remaining [[Sherry|sherry]] over the [[Couscous|couscous]], add a splash of [[Olive oil|olive oil]], stir in the [[Broccoli|broccoli]] and [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]], garnish with the [[Toasted|toasted]] [[Almonds|almonds]] and serve.\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#couscous #broccoli #broccolicouscous #sherry #stock #oliveoil #sweetpeppers #almondflakes #driedfruit #sultanas #boil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

-->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 6658\n|PortionCalories = 1109\n|DatePublished=18th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6 to 12\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour\n |Image = [[Image:Broudou bil hout (Fish soup) (TM) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span
