It's absolutely gorgeous on its own but goes well on the side of all sorts of [[Pork|pork]] and [[Fish dishes|fish dishes]]\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 200g [[Freekeh]] \n| 2 [[Fennel|fennel]] bulbs, trimmed and thinly sliced. If there are any fronds at the top, reserve for garnish \n| 2 [[Leeks|leeks]], washed and thinly sliced \n| 2 [[Courgettes|courgettes]], thinly sliced or spiralised \n| 1 tablespoon [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]], lightly crushed \n| A small handful each of fresh [[Mint leaves|mint leaves]], [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and curly [[Parsley|parsley]], finely chopped \n| 150g [[Green olives|green olives]], quartered \n| 100g [[Blanched|blanched]] [[Almonds|almonds]], [[Toasted|toasted]] and roughly chopped \n| 1 small hot [[Chilli|chilli]], very finely chopped \n| [[Juice]] of half a [[Lemon|lemon]] \n| 1 tablespoon [[White wine|white wine]] or [[Rice vinegar|rice vinegar]] \n| [[Extra virgin Olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]] \n| [[Salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat your [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Turn the [[Oven|oven]] on to 180C/gas mark 4. Set the freekeh soaking in cold water. \n| Put the [[Fennel|fennel]], [[Leeks|leeks]] and [[Courgettes|courgettes]] on a backing tray in one layer. Season with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]], give them a good drizzle of [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and sprinkle with the crushed [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]]. Put them in the [[Oven|oven]] when it\u0092s up to temperature, setting your timer for 20 minutes \n| When the freekeh has been soaking for 20 minutes, drain and put into a [[Saucepan|saucepan]] with 750mls of water. Put on a medium heat and bring gently to a [[Boil|boil]]. Lower the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for about 12 minutes, or just tender and chewy. Drain and set aside \n| When the veggies have been [[Baking|baking]] for 20 minutes, check them for texture and flavour. They should be cooked, but still have a good bite to them, with the [[Leeks|leeks]] in particular nice and crispy around the edges. As soon as they\u0092re done, sprinkle with a little of the [[Vinegar|vinegar]] and set aside. When they\u0092're cool, gently mix the chopped [[Herbs|herbs]] in. Set aside \n| In a bowl, put the [[Olives|olives]], [[Almonds|almonds]], [[Chilli|chilli]] and [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]. Stir well, and set aside \n| When you\u0092re ready to serve, combine the freekeh, the [[Veggie|veggie]] mix and the [[Olive|olive]] mix. Taste, adjust the seasoning with [[Salt|salt]], [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], if you need to, garnish with the [[Fennel|fennel]] fronds, and serve\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Nik and Edwina's Cookbook recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#fennel #leeks #chilli #courgettes #corianderseeds #oliveoil #almonds #lemonjuice #fennelolivefreekehandherbsalad #baking #pork </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It could also be made with [[Duck|duck]] or [[Minced|minced]] [[Beef|beef]] (meatballs).\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.3 kgs (3 lb) [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces, on the bone, skin removed - see [[Jointing a chicken]]\n| 450 g (1lb) ground or well crushed [[Walnuts|walnuts]]\n| 3 large [[Onions|onions]], peeled and thinly sliced\n| 3 cups [[Pomegranate|pomegranate]] juice, or 5 tablespoons of [[Pomegranate molasses|pomegranate molasses/syrup]]\n| [[Sugar]] to taste\n| Sea [[Salt|salt]] to taste\n| 1/3 cup of [[Vegetable|vegetable]] [[Oil|oil]]\n}}\n\n'''To garnish'''\n* [[Toasted]] [[Almond|almond]] flakes and [[Pomegranate|pomegranate]] pips\n\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] in the [[Oil|oil]] for 4 minutes until soft\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces and [[Fry|fry]] with the [[Onions|onions]] until golden [[Brown|brown]]\n| Add 3 cups of hot water and bring to [[Boil|boil]]\n| Lower the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]], covered for 30 minutes, adding more hot water if it starts to dry out\n| Add the [[Salt|salt]], ground [[Walnuts|walnuts]] and [[Pomegranate|pomegranate]] juice or syrup (if using [[Pomegranate syrup|pomegranate syrup]], add 2 more cups of hot water). Simmer until the chicken is properly cooked, a further 15 to 30 minutes.\n| Add [[Sugar|sugar]] to taste if it's too sour for your liking\n| Sprinkle with [[Toasted|toasted]] [[almonds]] and [[Pomegranate|pomegranate]] pips if using\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[Couscous|couscous]] or [[plain boiled rice]]\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}} \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pomegranate #chicken #onions #walnuts #fesenjan #fry #toasted #pomegranatesyrup #almond #duck #beef </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Fried kidneys in pomegranate molasses a beef recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#kidneys #butter #spice #friedkidneysinpomegranatemolasses #pomegranate #parsley #pomegranatemolasses #starter #juice #boil #unusualrecipes \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is my take on a recipe found in a translated Lebanese cook-book from around 1960. Any excuse to use my pomegranate molasses\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2383\n|PortionCalories = 595\n|DatePublished=23rd October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4 as a [[Starter|starter]]\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 35 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Fried kidneys in pomegranate molasses recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n======Best recipe review======\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Highly unusual!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">And very nice, though the pomegranate molasses can be quite hard to find.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is my take on a recipe found in a [translated] Lebanese cook-book from around 1960.  Any excuse to use my [[Pomegranate molasses|pomegranate molasses]].  The original recipe specifies lambs [[Kidneys|kidneys]], I would reduce the number to 4 if you are using [[Beef|beef]] kidneys.\n\nI have kept the original quantities, however for the [[Sake|sake]] of your health, I would reduce the amount of [[salt]] and [[butter]] (or use 50/50 with [[olive oil]]).\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 8 Lambs [[Kidneys|kidneys]]\n| 6 oz [[Butter|butter]] [see note above]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Salt|salt]] [see note above]\n| 4 oz sour [[Pomegranate|pomegranate]] [[Juice|juice]] - Made up from about 1 part [[Pomegranate molasses|pomegranate molasses]] to 3 parts water and mixed well\n| 1 oz [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Spice]] mix [below]\n| Few tablespoons [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| Chopped [[Parsley|parsley]] to garnish\n}}\n'''[[Spice|spice]] mix'''\n* Equal quantities, [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], [[White cumin|white cumin]], [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] and [[Paprika|paprika]], mixed together and finely [[Ground|ground]].\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cut the [[Kidneys|kidneys]] in half lengthwise, trim and remove the skins.\n| Flatten them under a cleaver or a heavy pan, [cut into small pieces if desired]\n| Heat the [[Butter|butter]] and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Kidneys|kidneys]] on both sides until [[Browned|browned]].\n| Remove the [[Kidneys|kidneys]] and keep warm.\n| Fry the garlic until it starts to colour.\n| Add the [[Spice|spice]] mixture and [[Salt|salt]] to the [[Flour|flour]] and mix into what remains of the [[Butter|butter]].\n| Stir until it just begins to [[Brown|brown]] then add the [[Pomegranate|pomegranate]] [[Juice|juice]], allow to [[Boil|boil]], return the [[Kidneys|kidneys]] and cook for a few minutes in the [[Sauce|sauce]].\n| Serve hot garnished with [[parsley]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThe original recipe suggests [[Fried|fried]] or pur\u00e9ed [[Potatoes|potatoes]].  I think it would go nicely with [[Brown|brown]] toast as a [[Starter|starter]].\n===Chef's note===\nWell this was an interesting dish.  I think when I make it again I will brown the kidneys first over a very high heat, in a little oil, and then continue with the sauce.  It was fine with half the butter and mush less salt.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Kidneys]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes|Kidneys]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Kidneys]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes|Kidneys]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes|Kidneys]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes|Kidneys]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Kidneys]]\n[[Category:Starters|Kidneys]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#kidneys #butter #spice #friedkidneysinpomegranatemolasses #pomegranate #parsley #pomegranatemolasses #starter #juice #boil #unusualrecipes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Drain any excess water using a [[Sieve|sieve]].\n| Re-heat the pan or [[Wok|wok]] and stir in the [[Couscous|couscous]], [[Ham|ham]], [[Fruit|fruit]] and [[Nuts|nuts]].\n| Serve!\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Taste Sensation recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#couscous #dried #fruitycajunhamcouscous #chickenstock #parsley #wok #boiling #ham #leeks #clovesofgarlic #garlic </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Ful medames",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Ful medames, Garlic recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#fulmedames #beans #oliveoil #onion #salad #favabeans #bread #garlic #fulbeans #cumin #pittabreads \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Ful medames also Foul Mudammas is one of the national dishes of Sudan and Egypt, often eaten at breakfast\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2703\n|PortionCalories = 675\n|DatePublished=19th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 16 hours, 10 minutes\n |PrepTime = 12 hours 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 4 hours\n |Image = [[Image:Ful medames recipe.jpg|220px|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Looks nasty, tastes ok</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3.4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">They say you eat with your eyes.  'Nuff said. </span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Ful medames''' also '''Foul Mudammas'''  is one of the national dishes of Sudan and Egypt, often eaten at breakfast. It consists of brown [[Fava beans|fava beans]], partially or completely [[Mashed|mashed]], which are slow-cooked and served with [[Olive oil|olive oil]], chopped [[Parsley|parsley]], [[Onion|onion]], [[Garlic|garlic]], and [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]. Ful medames is typically eaten with Egyptian [[Bread|bread]] ('eish masri).\n\nThe dish's name derives from the Egyptian language: ful is the Egyptian word for [[Fava beans|fava beans]], and medames is a Coptic word meaning \"buried.\" The second word hints at the original cooking method, which involved burying a sealed pot of water and [[Beans|beans]] under hot coals. This cooking method for [[Beans|beans]] is mentioned in the Jerusalem Talmud, indicating that it has been used in the Middle East at least since the 4th century.\n\nFul medames was exported from Egypt to the Arab World, particularly the Levant and Somalia. Ful medames came to the Horn of Africa when the Egyptians captured Zeila in the beginning of the 19th century. From there, it spread to other regions. In northern Somalia, ful is eaten with a [[Pancake|pancake]]-like [[Bread|bread]] called [[laxoox]]. Ful is also part of Ethiopian cuisine, where it is served with [[flatbread]] and [[mitmita powder]] or [[berebere spice mix]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g (1 lb) [[ful beans]], soaked overnight, rinsed and drained\n| 1 tablespoon\tfreshly [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]]\n| 6 [[Cloves garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 4 [[Hard-boiled eggs|hard-boiled eggs]], shelled and coarsely chopped\n| 1 handful [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], chopped\n| 1 handful fresh [[Mint leaves|mint leaves]], chopped \n| 2 [[Lemons|lemons]], cut into quarters\n| 1 [[Spanish]] [[Onion|onion]], peeled and sliced\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n'''To serve'''\n* [[Olive oil]]\n* 6 [[Pitta breads]]\n* 200 ml [[Yogurt]]\n* 4 [[Tomatoes]]\n* Half a [[Cucumber|cucumber]]\n* 150 g Mixed [[Salad|salad leaves]]\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[oven]] to 120\u00b0 C (250\u00b0 F - gas &frac12;), [fan oven 100\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the presoaked [[Beans|beans]] in a [[Casserole dish|casserole dish]], fill with water and cover the [[Beans|beans]] by 2 inches    \n| Add half of the [[Cumin|cumin]], Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]] and lots of [[Black pepper|black pepper]], cover and cook for 4 hours until the [[Beans|beans]] are soft.  Don't break the [[Beans|beans]] up.\n| Place the [[Eggs|eggs]], [[Herbs|herbs]], [[Onion|onion]] slices and [[Lemon|lemon]] quarters on separate plates\n| When the [[Beans|beans]] are cooked, stir in the remaining [[Cumin|cumin]] and add [[Salt|salt]] to taste\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe the [[Baking|baking]] dish at the table with the plates of garnish, [[Olive oil|olive oil]], [[Pitta breads|pitta breads]] and [[Salad|salad]]\n===Variations===\nIf you cannot get [[ful beans]], other [[Dried beans|dried beans]] will suffice, though the flavour will not be the same\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#fulmedames #beans #oliveoil #onion #salad #favabeans #bread #garlic #fulbeans #cumin #pittabreads </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]

I squeeze a tangerine into the mixture to get it going, but only because I had one to hand. A tablespoon or so of water would do\n| Pour over the [[lamb]] and marinate in the [[refrigerator]] for an hour\n| Lay the lamb fillets on an oiled [[barbecue]] hotplate\n| Cook for 8 minutes, turning three times in total, check that it's cooked to your liking\n| Rest for 5 minutes\n| Slice thickly and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[Chinese coleslaw]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Lamb]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes|Lamb]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Lamb]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters|Lamb]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Lamb]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Lamb]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Lamb]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#gingerspicedlamb #lamb #foodprocessor #mortarandpestle #coffeegrinder #paprikapowder #blackcumin #ginger #oliveoil #garlic #chinesecoleslaw </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Cook for 10-12 minutes, stirring until the [[Nuts|nuts]] are golden.\n| Meanwhile, put a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]] over a medium-high heat. When hot, add the [[Chicken|chicken]] and cook for 6 to 8 minutes each side, until golden. Set aside, covered with [[Foil|foil]] to keep hot.\n| Meanwhile, stir the [[Bulgur wheat|bulgur wheat]] into the [[Onion|onion]] mixture. Remove from the heat after 30 seconds and add the hot [[Stock|stock]] and [[Currants|currants]]. Cover and set aside for 10-12 minutes or until the stock has been absorbed-the [[Bulgur|bulgur]] [[Wheat|wheat]] will still have a good bite to it. Stir in most of the [[Parsley|parsley]] and some seasoning. Fluff up with a fork.\n| Divide the [[Pilaf|pilaf]] between six plates, top with the [[Chicken|chicken]] and scatter with the remaining [[Parsley|parsley]] to serve.\n}}\n(''Delicious Magazine'')\n\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/early-harvest.html Belazu Early Harvest Extra Virgin Olive Oil Unfiltered]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/products/extra virgin-olive-oils.html Belazu Extra virgin olive oil]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/rose-harissa.html Belazu Rose Harissa]\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #parsley #currants #onion #pilaf #ginger #pinenuts #harissachickenwithbulgurwheatpinenutandparsleypilaf #harissa #bulgurwheat #nuts </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Make a big batch of hot harissa paste with this easy recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#harissapaste #chillies #garlic #oliveoil #preserved_lemons #cumin #lemon #coriander #sterilisedjar #spices #carawayseeds \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Harissa or harissa paste is a very hot chili sauce commonly found in Libya, Tunisia and Algeria. Its main ingredients are chili peppers, combined with spices and herbs such as garlic, coriander and cumin\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 138\n|PortionCalories = 14\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 100\n |Difficulty = 2\n |ImageComment = Ingredients for 1 large jar of harissa paste\n |TotalTime = 1 hour, 35 minutes\n |PrepTime = 1 hour, 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Harissa paste ingredients.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Bulk buy chillies for this</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">A great recipe, but buy your chillies in bulk if you're going to make this.  It's uneconomical if you buy them from the supermarket.  Make loads in one go as it keeps for years and years and does not degrade.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Harissa paste.jpg|thumb|right|300px|Harissa paste]]\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\nHarissa or harissa paste is a very hot chili sauce commonly found in Libya, Tunisia and Algeria. Its main ingredients are [[Chillies|piri piri chili peppers]], [[Chillies|serrano peppers]] or other [[Chillies|hot chili peppers]], combined with [[spices]] and [[herbs]] such as [[garlic]], [[coriander]] and [[cumin]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 100g g (4 oz) dried hot red [[Chillies|red chili peppers]], ideally [[Bird's eye chili peppers]]\n| 2 teaspoons sea [[salt]]\n| 6 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, chopped \n| 2 teaspoons freshly ground [[Cumin|cumin]]\n| 1 teaspoon freshly ground [[black cumin]] seeds\n| 2 teaspoons freshly ground [[caraway seeds]] (optional)\n| 1 chopped, skinned and de-seeded red [[bell pepper]]\n| 1 teaspoon smoked [[paprika]]\n| 2 teaspoons red wine or [[sherry]] vinegar\n| 2 teaspoons [[tomato puree]]\n| Juice and zest from half a [[lemon]] or lime\n| Half of one [[Preserved_lemons|salted lemon]] (optional)\n| [[Olive oil]] to cover paste to assist preservation\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| As already stated, '''ensure the kitchen is well ventilated!'''\n| In a small pan, cover the dried chillies with water, bring to the boil and simmer for 10 minutes\n| Remove from the heat and let it rest for an hour\n| Drain the chillies\n| Place chillies in a food processor with the [[Garlic|garlic]], tomato puree, vinegar, salt and spices\n| Blend to a paste adding the [[lemon]] juice, little by little, until you have the desired consistency\n| Place into a [[sterilised jar]]\n| Add enough [[olive oil]] to cover the paste and prevent it from being exposed to air.\n| Screw on lid tightly and refrigerate\n}}\n===Servings===\nServings: 100 - Makes 1 jar of very hot, very yummy chili paste\n===Variations===\nReduce the salt by half and add the rind and flesh of half a [[Preserved_lemons|preserved lemon]]\n===Chef's notes===\nHandling this amount of [[dried chillies]] at once can be a bit nasty. The dust and vapour that they may give off can make breathing difficult. I'm still coughing half an hour after making this batch. Don't let this put you off though, just take the following precautions.\n# Ensure the kitchen is well ventilated and hold your breath when rinsing out the food processor.\n# Keeps pets out of the kitchen whilst you are making this.\n# Wear rubber gloves if your skin is sensitive\n\nIf your mouth burns after eating harissa, or any other hot sauce, drink plenty of [[milk]] or [[yogurt]].\n\nDrinking water tends to make thing worse, not better.\n\nBecause harissa paste is water based, it will won't keep for long periods, even if refrigerated.  Keeping the surface covered with oil helps to prolong its life a little, however, having made, and consumed litres of my homemade harissa paste, I think I have come up with the way of storing it:\n\n# Once made, only bottle what you are likely to consume within 1 month.  refrigerate and always ensure that it is well covered with oil.\n# Divide the remaining harissa paste into freezer bags about the same size as your fridge bottle and freeze.\n# Refill your fridge bottle with [[defrosted]] harissa paste as your fridge supply runs out.\n\n==See also==\n\n* [[Chilli sauce|Many other chili sauce recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Harissa paste]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces|Harissa paste]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Harissa paste]]\n[[Category:Condiments|Harissa paste]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes|Harissa paste]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Chili pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#harissapaste #chillies #garlic #oliveoil #preserved_lemons #cumin #lemon #coriander #sterilisedjar #spices #carawayseeds </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

Skim carefully\n| Reduce heat to medium and cook until contents are done\n| This requires about four hours\n| Make the [[Sauce|sauce]] by [[Mashing|mashing]] the [[garlic]] in [[Salt|salt]] and [[Mint|mint]] to the [[Vinegar|vinegar]] and mix well\n| Serve the [[Meat|meat]] in one dish and the [[Sauce|sauce]] in another\n| serve some of the [[Broth|broth]] in which the head and feet were cooked\n}}\n\nNote: ''Instead of rose-water you may rub the head and feet with pieces of [[Onion|onion]] or with [[Flour|flour]] and [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]''\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mutton recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#headandfeetofsheepinavinegarsauce #vinegar #garlic #mint #sauce #sheep #split #broth #flour #rosewater #mashed </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

I have made a few small changes, but it's basically the same as i remember it on television.\n\nThe trick is to slice the [[Liver|liver]] thinly and to cook it quickly.\n\nThis would make a great [[Starter|starter]] or lunchtime [[Snack|snack]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 300g lambs' [[Liver|liver]], any veins removed and very thinly sliced\n| 1 small [[Red onion|red onion]], peeled and thinly sliced\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], freshly [[Ground|ground]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]], freshly [[Ground|ground]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Caraway seeds|caraway seeds]], freshly [[Ground|ground]]\n| 1 [[Clove|clove]] of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and thinly sliced\n| Pinch of [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| Pinch of [[Smoked|smoked]] [[Spanish]] [[Paprika|paprika]]\n| Pinch of [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| Splash of [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]]\n| 1 teaspoon of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n}}\n'''add when [[Frying|frying]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 teaspoon [[Butter|butter]]\n| Tiny pinch of the above [[Seeds|seeds]], un-[[Ground|ground]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Place all of the ingredients in a [[Lock & Lock]]-style box, close the lid and shake well to combine.\n| Leave for 30 minutes to [[Marinade|marinade]].\n| Heat a pan or a [[Wok|wok]] over a high flame.\n| Add the [[Liver|liver]] mixture to the pan.\n| Add the [[Butter|butter]] and the whole [[Seeds|seeds]] and saut\u00e9 for about 3 or 4 minutes turning regularly to ensure even cooking.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nWe served this in [[home made pitta breads]] filled with wild [[rocket]] leaves and [[yogurt]].  Can't be beaten!\n===Variations===\nWe couldn't get lambs' [[liver]] today, so went for [[ox]] liver.  As that can be a bit stronger, once it was sliced, I soaked it in milk for 30 minutes which does seem to make it a little milder.\n<gallery widths=270px heights=270px perrow=5>\nImage:Hugh's merguez liver and onions recipe ingredients.jpg|The ingredients: the liver is soaking in milk to make it milder tasting\nImage:Hugh's merguez liver and onions lock and lock box.jpg|Marinating in a lock and lock box\nImage:Hugh's merguez liver and onions frying.jpg|Frying a little at a time\nImage:Hugh's merguez liver and onions serve yourself.jpg|Help yourself\nImage:Hugh's merguez liver and onions recipe.jpg|With wild rocket, yogurt and made-made pitta breads\n</gallery>\n===Recipe source===\n* Hugh Fearnley-Whittingstall from River Cottage [[Vegetarian]] TV program [4th February 2013]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinaded]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#hughsmerguezliverandonions #ground #liver #butter #rocket #seeds #yogurt #vegetarian #corianderseeds #chillipowder #paprika </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Hummus recipe",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Hummus recipe Greek, from Cookipedia.Co.Uk\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chickpeas #hummusrecipe #dried #garlic #oliveoil #zest #tahini #miseenplace #freeze #lemon #dip \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This delicious dip is simple to make and extremely economical if made with dried chickpeas. The recipe given is for 125 g (4 oz) of chickpeas, though\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}} \n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 647\n|PortionCalories = 161\n|DatePublished=17th January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Hummus, served!\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 days, 1 hour, 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 2 days, 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour\n |Image = [[Image:How to cook hummus.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">So Easy!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This could not be more simple - and it tastes fantastic, especially withj chips!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis delicious [[Dip|dip]] is simple to make and extremely economical if made with [[Dried|dried]] [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]].\n\nThe recipe given is for 125 g (4 oz) of [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]], though if you are making it, it's probably better to multiply the quantities and make more then [[Freeze|freeze]] the excess as it freezes really well.\nThe amount of [[Garlic|garlic]] that you add is personal taste. I use much more normally.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 125 g (4 oz) [[Dried|dried]] [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] or 1 large can of chickpeas [about 400g of cooked chickpeas] and omit the soaking stage.\n| [[Zest]] and [[Juice|juice]] of 1 [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| 2 tablespoons light [[Tahini|tahini]]\n| 2 Cloves [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled\n| 120 ml (4 fl oz) [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] to taste\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Soak the [[Dried|dried]] [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] for 24 hours in cold water, refreshing a few times if you can.\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| ''If using canned [[chick peas]], just drain and rinse them with fresh water a few times and go directly to Adding them to the food processor step.''\n| Drain and rinse the soaked [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]].\n| Add to a large pan, cover with water. '''Do not add any [[Salt|salt]]''', otherwise the peas will not absorb the water properly. Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 1 hour or until softened.  They may take a little longer depending on size and age. A pinch of [[baking soda]] (bicarbonate of soda) added to the cooking water will shorten the cooking time.\n| Drain, rinse and allow to cool.\n| Add to a [[Food processor|food processor]] with everything but the [[Olive oil|olive oil]]. Blend to a paste, then as if making [[Mayonnaise|mayonnaise]], gradually drizzle in the [[Olive|olive]] [[Oil|oil]] with the motor running.\n| Taste and adjust the seasoning if needed.  You can always add extra [[Garlic|garlic]] if needed.\n| Adjust the consistency by adding more oil if too thick or a handful of breadcrumbs if it is too liquid.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Hummus recipe blending.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Blending the hummus\nImage:Chickpeas cooked.jpg|thumb|300px|right|500g of cooked chickpeas\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Crispbread|crispbread]] or [[Pittas|pittas]].\n===Variations===\nOmit the [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], [[Zest|zest]] and [[Salt|salt]]. Instead, add the rind of a quarter of a [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] plus 2 tablespoons of the [[Preserved lemon juice|preserved lemon juice]]. [[Preserved lemon hummus|Bulk recipe here!]]. \n\nYou can also cook the chickpeas in a pressure cooker - [[Chickpeas#How_to_cook_chickpeas_in_a_pressure_cooker|details here]]\n===Variations===\nAny tinned beans or pulses work well in this recipe.  I've just made a lovely batch using a mixture of [[cannellini beans]] & [[chick peas]].\n{{SeeAlsoHummus}}\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Greek recipes|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes|Hummus]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Starters|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Turkish recipes|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chickpeas #hummusrecipe #dried #garlic #oliveoil #zest #tahini #miseenplace #freeze #lemon #dip </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Hut bil karfas (Baked fish and celery) a garlic recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#fish #celery #foil #bake #garlic #parsley #oliveoil #pickles #salad #whitefish #seabass \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This spicy fish recipe from Algeria can be made with any firm, white fish fillets\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2375\n|PortionCalories = 395\n|DatePublished=20th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6 - for less<br />see [[Talk:Hut_bil_karfas_(Baked_fish_and_celery)#Quantities for 2|the comments page]]\n |Difficulty = 2\n |ImageComment = Could look better!\n |TotalTime = 2 hours\n |PrepTime = 1 hour, 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 45 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Hut bil karfas (Baked fish and celery) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">0 from 10 for presentation</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">10 from 10 for taste!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis spicy [[Fish|fish]] recipe from Algeria can be made with any firm, [[white fish]] fillets.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g [[Celery|celery]], cut into 5 cm pieces\n| [[Garlic]] to taste, crushed\n| Seasoning\n| 2 teaspoons [[Paprika|paprika]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin|cumin]]\n| Pinch of [[Saffron|saffron]], [[Ground|ground]]\n| 1 teaspoon or more of [[Cayenne pepper]]\n| 45 ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1.8 kg [[Bream|bream]] or [[Sea bass|sea bass]] fillets\n| The [[Juice|juice]] of 1 [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| 340 g [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]] and chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[Parsley|parsley]], finely chopped\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 190\u00b0 C (375\u00b0 F - gas 5).\n* Mix the [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Spices|spices]] and [[Oil|oil]] in a small bowl. \n* Cut slashes in the [[Fish|fish]] and rub the mixture into the fish, pressing well into the slashes. \n* Lay the [[Fish|fish]] on a plate and [[Marinate|marinate]] for 1 hour.\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Hut bil karfas (Baked fish and celery) ready to bake.jpg|Ready for the oven\nImage:Hut bil karfas (Baked fish and celery) marinading.jpg|[[Basa]], marinading\nImage:Marinade for Hut bil karfas (Baked fish and celery) recipe.jpg|The [[marinade]]\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Arrange the [[Celery|celery]] in a single layer in a greased [[Baking|baking]] dish. \n| Place the [[Fish|fish]] on the [[Celery|celery]]. \n| Cover with the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] and [[Parsley|parsley]]. \n| Cover with [[Foil|foil]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 30 minutes. \n| Remove [[Foil|foil]] and [[Bake|bake]] for a further 15 minutes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Salad|salad]] and/or [[Pickles|pickles]].\n\nWe had this with [[pitta breads]] and the delicious Oyi namulh (Korean cucumber salad).  The dish has quite a lot of liquid, which we discarded, a unusual dish, but very tasty.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Hut bil karfas (baked fish and celery)]]\n[[Category:Algerian recipes|Hut bil karfas (baked fish and celery)]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes|Hut bil karfas (baked fish and celery)]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Hut bil karfas (baked fish and celery)]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Hut bil karfas (baked fish and celery)]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Hut bil karfas (baked fish and celery)]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes|Hut bil karfas (baked fish and celery)]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Hut bil karfas (baked fish and celery)]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Hut bil karfas (baked fish and celery)]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#fish #celery #foil #bake #garlic #parsley #oliveoil #pickles #salad #whitefish #seabass </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Injera - Canjeero",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Injera - Canjeero, Vegetarian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#batter #injeracanjeero #millet #pancake #pancakes #teffflour #miseenplace #fermented #tava #plainflour #flour \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Injera or millet bread is Ethiopia's famous pancake-style bread that is similar to a crepe. It is also known as enjera or taita is a pancake-like bread\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1314\n|PortionCalories = 219\n|DatePublished=20th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6 - Makes more than 6 injera\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 day, 3 minutes\n |PrepTime = 1 day\n |CookTime = 3 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Inerja recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">A bit dry</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3.2</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Probably more of a subsistence food than a delicacy.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Injera''' or '''[[Millet|millet]] [[Bread|bread]]''' is Ethiopia's famous [[Pancake|pancake]]-style bread that is similar to a cr\u00eape.\n\nIt is also known as '''enjera''' or '''taita''' is a pancake-like bread made out of [[teff flour]]. It is traditionally eaten in Eritrea, Ethiopia, Somalia (where it is also called '''laxoox''' and '''canjeero'''). Although traditionally made from [[teff flour]] it can also be made from [[millet flour]] which will probably be easier to obtain outside of Africa. It is traditionally made using huge [[tavas]], producing table-cloth sized injera that are consumed with the meal.\n\nIt's probably prudent to reduce the scale here and make them using a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]]!\n\n'''Main ingredients'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 110 g (4 oz) [[Millet|millet]] [[Flour|flour]]\n| 250 g (2 oz) [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Dried active yeast|dried active yeast]]\n| [[Salt]]\n| [[Oil]] for [[Frying|frying]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Mix all of the main ingredients together with enough lukewarm water to produce a pourable [[Batter|batter]].\n* Cover with a damp cloth and leave overnight in a warm place to [[Ferment|ferment]]. \n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Stir the [[Fermented|fermented]] [[Batter|batter]] and add [[Salt|salt]] to taste.\n| Heat a very small amount of [[Oil|oil]] on a [[Tava|tava]] or in a [[Frying pan|frying pan]].\n| Pour a small amount of [[Batter|batter]] into the pan and swill it around as you would with normal [[Pancakes|pancakes]].  Ideally making a very thin [[Pancake|pancake]] that covers the whole pan.\n| Cook until set, which will only take a minute or so.\n| If you've made the [[Pancakes|pancakes]] very thick, you may have to turn them, otherwise, serve immediately.\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#batter #injeracanjeero #millet #pancake #pancakes #teffflour #miseenplace #fermented #tava #plainflour #flour </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Jamie Oliver's lamb kebabs",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Jamie Oliver's lamb kebabs, Meat recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#jamieoliverslambkebabs #lemon #sumac #thyme #foodprocessor #salad #onion #fat #parsley #greekyogurt #cumin \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I saw this kofte-style kebab recipe on the excellent ''Jamie at Home'' series and as I already had the sumac, I thought that I would recreate this dish\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1780\n|PortionCalories = 445\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |ImageComment = Jamie Oliver's lamb kebabs, about to be assembled!\n |TotalTime = 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 10 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Jamie Oliver's lamb kebabs recipe 1.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Healthy food</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">..and delicious too.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nI saw this k\u00f6fte-style kebab recipe on the excellent 'Jamie at Home' series and as I already had the [[Sumac|sumac]], I thought that I would recreate this dish on Cookipedia.\n\nYou will need a [[Food processor|food processor]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500 g (1 lb 2 oz) neck of [[Lamb|lamb]], trimmed of excess [[Fat|fat]] and sinews\n| A handful of freshly chopped [[Thyme|thyme]] leaves\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chili|chili]] powder\n| &#189; teaspoon freshly ground [[Cumin|cumin]] seeds\n| 2 teaspoons of [[Sumac|sumac]] (use rind and juice from &#189; a [[Lemon|lemon]] or [[lime]] if you don't have [[sumac]])\n| A good pinch of sea [[Salt|salt]] and freshly ground [[Black pepper|black pepper]].\n| 1 big handful of shelled [[Pistachio|pistachio]] [[Nuts|nuts]]\n}}\n''' To serve'''\n* A large handful of freshly chopped [[Parsley|parsley]]\n* 1 red [[Onion|onion]], peeled and very thinly sliced\n* Juice from 1 [[Lemon|lemon]]\n* 150g Thick set [[Greek yogurt]]\n* [[Salad]] leaves\n* [[Flour]] [[Tortillas|tortillas]]\n'''TO garnish each kebab\n* A pinch of [[chili powder]]\n* A pinch of [[sea salt]]\n* A pinch of [[cumin powder]]\n* A pinch of [[thyme leaves]]\n* A pinch of [[sumac]]\n* A splash of [[olive oil]]\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Jamie Oliver's lamb kebabs recipe 2.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Cooked to perfection\nImage:Jamie Oliver's lamb kebabs recipe 3.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Ready to go\n</gallery>\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Trim all of the sinews and most of the [[Fat|fat]] from the meat and cut into 2.5 cm (1\") cubes\n| Add the pistachio nuts to a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a steel cutting blade and blitz to rice-sided pieces\n| Add the meat cubes to the food processor.\n| Add the [[Chili|chili]] powder, [[Cumin|cumin]], [[Sumac|sumac]] (or [[Lemon|lemon]]), [[Thyme|thyme]] and [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]].\n| Pulse the [[Food processor|food processor]] until you have a pretty chunky [[Mince|mince]]. Don't puree it to a meat paste!\n| Using about 5 or 6 metal [[skewers]], wrap a good handful of the meat mixture around each skewer.\n| Refrigerate for an hour or two if you can as it will allow the meat to settle and the flavours to mingle.\n| Cook the kebabs on a very hot [[Grill|grill]] or [[Barbecue|barbecue]] for about 4 to 5 minutes, turning now and again.\n| Add the chopped [[Parsley|parsley]] and thinly sliced [[Onion|onion]] to a bowl and squeeze the juice from &#189; a [[Lemon|lemon]] over the [[Onions|onions]]. Add a good pinch of [[Salt|salt]] and toss the mixture well.\n| Warm the [[Tortillas|tortillas]], don't toast them.\n| Season the [[Salad|salad]] leaves with [[Olive|olive]] [[Oil|oil]], the remaining [[Lemon|lemon]] juice and a pinch of [[Salt|salt]].\n| Lay a selection of [[Salad|salad]] leaves on the [[Tortilla|tortilla]], add a dollop of [[Greek yogurt]] and a handful of [[Mint|mint]] and [[Onion|onion]].\n}}\n\nAdd a  pinch of [[chili powder]], [[sea salt]], [[cumin powder]], [[thyme]] leaves and a dash of [[olive oil]] to each kebab as you make them, roll up and serve. I prefer to make them up as I am eating them, but it's your call.\n\n===Chef's note===\nAlthough Jamie put the [[pistachios]] in with the meat, they stayed mainly in one piece (and kept falling off the kebabs), so I would be inclined, next time, to blitz them to small ''rice-sized'' pieces, before adding the meat.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Jamie Oliver's Lamb kebabs]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes|Jamie Oliver's Lamb kebabs]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Jamie Oliver's Lamb kebabs]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Jamie Oliver's Lamb kebabs]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Jamie Oliver's Lamb kebabs]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#jamieoliverslambkebabs #lemon #sumac #thyme #foodprocessor #salad #onion #fat #parsley #greekyogurt #cumin </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

It keeps well, so you can afford to make a\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 629\n|PortionCalories = 39\n|DatePublished=1st February 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Servings: 16 - Makes about a pint of jerk seasoning\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 25 minutes\n |CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Jamie Oliver's jerk seasoning recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Best with chicken</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Some foods just make perfect pairs - Jerk chicken is one of these!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nMake this jerk seasoning to coat roast pork, [[Chicken|chicken]], ham, turkey, sausages - in truth, most meat or fish.\n\nIt keeps well, so you can afford to make a big batch, but because of the volumes, it's worth seeking out an ethnic food supplier for the [[Spices|spices]] as the little supermarket jars are an extremely expensive way to buy spices in quantity. Grind the spices yourself in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] to ensure you get fresh powerful flavours.\n===Adjustments from the Jamie's television recipe===\nI have adjusted the recipe from that seen on the TV program as I thought it was too liquid and way too 'clovey', although it was brilliant.  By the way, Jamie's original was 2 tablespoons of [[clove buds]], 250 ml [[dark rum]], 250 ml [[malt vinegar]].\n</dev>\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 6 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| 2 tablespoons freshly ground [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]]\n| 2 tablespoons ground allspice\n| 2 level teaspoons of clove buds\n| 8 [[habanero chillies]] or [[Scotch bonnet chillies]] or of course any other types of [[Chillies|chillies]] of your choice\n|* I could not get [[habaneroes|habaneros]] so I used 16 medium sized (5 cm) red [[chillies]], the anonymous types that most supermarkets sell. \n| 2 tablespoons freshly grated [[Nutmeg|nutmeg]], (roughly 1 large nutmeg before grating)\n| 8 [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sea salt|sea salt]]\n| 1 tablespoon freshly ground [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| 1 tablespoon freshly ground juniper berries\n| 3 tablespoons freshly picked [[Thyme leaves|thyme leaves]]\n| 200 ml [[dark rum]]\n| 200 ml [[Malt vinegar|malt vinegar]]\n| 2 [[Red onions|red onions]], peeled and quartered. White onions are fine too.\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add everything but the [[rum]], [[Vinegar|vinegar]] and [[Onions|onions]] to a food processor with a metal blade and blitz to a paste\n| Add the [[Onions|onions]], rum and [[Vinegar|vinegar]] and blitz until they are totally combined\n| Store in [[sterilised]] bottles\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nBrush over meat, fish or poultry before cooking.\n\nFor hams, mix in a tablespoon of [[honey]] or [[marmalade]] and brush or spoon over all visible surfaces for the last 30 minutes of cooking.\n===Chef's notes===\nI marinated [[pan fried breaded pork fillets]] for 3 hours in a ladleful of this jerk seasoning and they were brilliant.  As was [[Marmalade glazed jerk gammon]], a version of [[marmalade ham]] that I made using this recipe.\n\n==See also==\n* [[Jerk recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Jamaican recipes\u200e]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#jerkseasoning #darkrum #chillies #maltvinegar #vinegar #onions #garlic #habaneroes #honey #bayleaves #cinnamon </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Do check the chicken stock first as some can be very salty so no extra salt should be needed.\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| 1 [[green chilli]], deseeded and sliced. \n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Turmeric|turmeric]]\n| &frac14; teaspoon [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]]\n| 50 ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| Enough [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] to cover the ingredients of the [[slow cooker]].  Top up with boiling water if needed. \n}}\n''' to serve'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| About 360 g dried couscous, [ 550 g couscous (cooked weight) ] - see [[Couscous|couscous cooking instructions]]\n| Freshly chopped [[parsley]] or [[coriander]] leaves\n| 15 g Toasted [[almond]] slices\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Turkey instead of chicken again.jpg|thumb|300px|right|A whole 1600g turkey leg for \u00a34.50 instead of a small chicken.<br />I only use the sliced thigh and froze the remaining leg.\nImage:Kesksou bil djedj ready to cook.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Slow cooker loaded, ready to cook for 8 hours.\n</gallery>\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put all the ingredients to the [[slow cooker]] and cook for 8 hours on a low setting. \n| Prepare the [[Couscous|couscous]] as shown [[Couscous#How_to_cook_couscous|here]]. \n| To serve make a bed with the [[Couscous|couscous]] and pour the [[Chicken|chicken]] mixture over it.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nI made a similar recipe last week and again, I found Morrison's chicken prohibitively expensive, but a whole 1600g turkey leg for \u00a34.50 was an absolute bargain.  This time I used half and froze the rest.\n\nI you want a thicker gravy, you could stir in a tablespoon or so, of fine [[cornmeal]] 30 minutes before the end of cooking.\n\nIf using a whole turkey leg or similar, cut deep slashes in the meat so it cooks really well.\n===Variations===\nRecipes such as this really do lend themselves to personal variation.  Almost any vegetables can be added to this, but bear in mind that some might turn to mush after the prolonged cooking time in a slow cooker, eg: [[courgettes]].  If possible, pop these in when there is just a few hours left.  \n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Kesksou bil djedj (couscous with chicken)]]\n[[Category:Algerian recipes|Kesksou bil djedj (couscous with chicken)]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Kesksou bil djedj (couscous with chicken)]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Kesksou bil djedj (couscous with chicken)]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Kesksou bil djedj (couscous with chicken)]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Kesksou bil djedj (couscous with chicken)]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Kesksou bil djedj (couscous with chicken)]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Kesksou bil djedj (couscous with chicken)]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#couscous #chicken #diced #slowcooker #turnip #coriander #parsley #chickpeas #cinnamon #cornmeal #carrots </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

East and surrounding countries.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| '''''For the shells:'''''\n| 250 g (8 oz) [[burghul]] (cracked wheat) \n| 500 g (1 lb) minced [[beef]] \n| 1 [[onion]], roughly chopped \n| ground [[white cumin]] seeds\n| 500 g (1 lb) minced [[beef]] \n| [[Salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n| [[Oil]] for [[deep frying]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| '''''For the shells:'''''\n| Soak the [[bulghar]] 20 minutes in cold water, then drain or press dry in a cloth.\n| Blend the [[meat]], [[onion]], [[salt]] and [[pepper]] in a [[food processor]]\n| Process a second time, with the [[bulgar]] until the mixture can be worked like a [[dough]]\n| Finish by hand kneading for a few minutes\n| '''''For the filling:'''''\n| In a [[frying pan]], toast the [[pine-nuts]] until they are golden brown\n| Add the [[oil]] and [[fry]] the [[onions]] until translucent and soft\n| Add the [[meat]], [[salt]] and [[pepper]] and cook until the meat is [[browned]]\n| '''''Assembly:'''''\n| Take an egg-sized portion of the shell mixture and roll into a ball\n| Poke a hole in it with your finger and enlarge the hole to make a tiny container\n| Press some stuffing into the hole and pinch the top to make a seal. They should be 'pointy' at each end. \"[[kibbeh|Lebanese torpedoes]]\n| [[Deep fry]] in small batches until golden brown\n| Drain on kitchen towel and serve hot.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with wedges of [[lemon]] or [[lime]], and though probably not authentic, [[sour cream and chive dip]] goes really well with this dish.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Deep fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#onion #kibbeh #beef #burghul #kibbehrecipe #deepfry #fry #whitecumin #deepfrying #foodprocessor #browned </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

of the [[Spice|spice]] mix over the both sides of the chops.\n| Place the chops on your chosen heat source and cook for about 7 minutes a side.\n| Remove and rest for 5 minutes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with crusty [[Bread|bread]] and the remaining [[Cumin|cumin]] [[Salt|salt]] in a separate dish.\n===Chef's note===\nMost variants of this recipe call for more salt. teaspoon [[Saffron|saffron]] powder \n| 500g shelled [[garden peas]] \n| 2 [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]] and chopped \n| 1 [[Belazu]] [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] or more, cut into pieces \n| a dozen [[Green olives|green olives]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the [[Meat|meat]] in a large pot with the [[Oil|oil]], [[Onion|onion]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]], [[Ginger|ginger]] and [[Saffron|saffron]]. \n| Cover with water and cook, covered, for 1-1&frac12; hours until the [[Meat|meat]] is very tender, adding water to keep it covered in its [[Sauce|sauce]]. \n| Add the [[Peas|peas]], [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] and [[Olives|olives]] and cook uncovered a few minutes longer, until the peas are tender and the [[Sauce|sauce]] reduced. Serve.\n}}\n(''Tamarind & Saffron by Claudia Roden'')\n\n\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Algerian recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Libyan recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n\n\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/belazu-pickled-lemons.html Belazu Preserved Lemon]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/rose-harissa.html Belazu Rose Harissa]\n==See also==\n{{Tagine-recipe-list}}\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lambtagine #belazu #sauce #preservedlemon #ginger #onion #saffron #chillipowder #lamb #harissa #peas </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Lamb tagine with tomatoes and peas",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Lamb tagine with tomatoes and peas a meat recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#celery #lambshank #boiling #sherryvinegar #lambtaginewithtomatoesandpeas #garlic #simmer #saffron #oliveoil #onions #tomatoes \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Another slow-cooked lamb dish that has Middle Eastern origins\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1446\n|PortionCalories = 361\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 hours 50 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime =  2 hours 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Lamb tagine with tomatoes and pea recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Just made this - very nice.</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Made this last night - very nice!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Lamb tagine with tomatoes peas and aubergines.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Ready for a 2 hour simmer]]\nAnother slow-cooked [[Lamb|lamb]] dish that has Middle Eastern origins.  The original recipe was from one of the wonderful Moro books by Sam and Sam Clark, but as always, when it comes to cooking it, I use up bits and bobs found in the fridge and change it out of all recognition to the original recipe.\n\nThe fatty pork chop would '''never''' be in the original recipe which would be muslim in origin, however, it was spare in the fridge and adds a nice flavour to the oil\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 2 teaspoons white [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] & 1 teaspoon [[black cumin seeds]], [[Ground|ground]] to  powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[ras el hanout]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| 1 [[Chile de Arbole]] ground to powder or 1/2 a teaspoon of [[Chili powder|chili powder]]\n| 2 medium [[Onions|onions]], peeled and chopped\n| 4 cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 1 large [[carrot]], peeled and cut into rings\n| 3 [[celery]] hearts with leaves, chopped into moons\n| 1 [[aubergine]], halved and sliced\n| 4 large [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]] and chopped\n| 1 [[Lamb shank]], on the bone\n| 1 large fatty [[pork chop]], cut into cubes \n| A splash of [[sherry vinegar]]\n| 1 650 ml cold water\n| 1 teaspoon [[Saffron strands|saffron strands]]. Stand in 2 tablespoons [[Boiling|boiling]] water for 15 minutes or more\n| 300 g [[Frozen peas|frozen peas]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* [[Skinning tomatoes|Rub the skins off]] the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] by [[Blanching|blanching]] water that has boiled and leave for 4 minutes.\n* Infuse the [[Saffron|saffron]] in 2 tablespoons of [[Boiling|boiling]] water for at least 15 minutes\n* Defrost the peas.\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a large pan, add the [[Olive oil|olive oil]], [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and saut\u00e9 for 5 minutes until the onions have softened. Add the spices, stir-fry and then add the [[pork]] cubes and the [[lamb shank]] and stir-fry so the oil is flavoured with the spices and the meat is browned a little.\n| [[Deglaze]] the pan with a splash of [[sherry vinegar]]\n| Add the [[carrots]], [[celery]], [[aubergines]], [[tomatoes]], cold water and [[Saffron|saffron]] mix, bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 2 hours.\n| Add the [[Peas|peas]], remove the lid and [[Simmer|simmer]] for a further 25 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Couscous|couscous]] or crusty [[Bread|bread]]\n===Chef' note===\nDirectly from the pot it was quite liquid, which went very well with fresh bread, the next day though, the gravy had thickened up naturally. If you wanted a thicker sauce, just stir in a few teaspoons of cornflour, mixed with a tablespoon of water and heat for a few minutes whilst stirring.\n==See also==\n{{Tagine-recipe-list}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#celery #lambshank #boiling #sherryvinegar #lambtaginewithtomatoesandpeas #garlic #simmer #saffron #oliveoil #onions #tomatoes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Lamb tangia",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Lamb tangia, Garlic recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#lamb #lambtangia #preservedlemons #butter #garlic #boiledpotatoes #mortarandpestle #onions #dutchoven #sauce #tangia \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A 5 hour slow-cooked Moroccan lamb dish that would traditionally use a tangia\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1199\n|PortionCalories = 199\n|DatePublished=30th December 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |ImageComment = Slow cooked lamb tangia and couscous\n |TotalTime = 5 hours 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 5 hours\n |Image = [[Image:Slow cooked lamb tangia.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Garlic, garlic, garlic</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Smell this when it is cooking. WOW!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nA 5 hour slow-cooked Moroccan lamb dish that would traditionally use a '''[[Tangia|tangia]]'''.  Our version uses a [[Dutch oven|dutch oven]] and a conventional cooker and is quite similar to [[Jamie Oliver's 4 hour slow roast lamb]] but with a bit more [[Spice|spice]].\n\nTraditionally, this dish would use cheap cuts of [[meat]], [[lamb]] [[shank]], shoulder etc. Although the [[Tangia|tangia cooking process]] was originally a peasant's way of cooking, because it transforms simple food into something so exotic, I think it's worth using really good cuts of [[lamb]].  Feel free to ignore me though!\n\nThe aroma that issues from this dish while cooking will stop you in your tracks.  A really complex [[lemon]] scent, the perfume of [[ground coriander]], roasting [[lamb]] and just a tiny hint of [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[onions]] (and I'm not being sarcastic). It is staggering, so please do try to cook this.\n\nEven if you are making this for less than six people, I would still use the same amount of ingredients, but just reduce the meat per person, and maybe a little less [[butter]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 200 g lean cuts of [[lamb]] per person (eg leg of [[lamb]] steaks  or 1.8 kg shoulder of [[Lamb|lamb]] cut into 6 sections\n| 1.5 [[Preserved lemons|preserved lemons]], flesh removed\n| 2 large [[Onions|onions]], peeled and quartered\n| 1 tablespoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], cracked in a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]]\n| 10 peeled [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves\n| 1 tablespoon [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]], finely ground in a [[coffee grinder]] or [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]]\n| Big handful of [[Parsley|parsley]] - big, big, big!\n| 60g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 160 ml water\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[oven]] to 230\u00b0 C (450\u00b0 F - gas 8)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the water, [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] rinds, [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Onion|onion]], [[Spices|spices]], [[Herbs|herbs]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] into a [[Food processor|food processor]] and blend to a coarse to medium consistency.\n| I am not a fan of lamb fat/oil so if you are like me, trim off the big hunks of fat.\n| Dab the [[Butter|butter]] over the base of a [[Dutch oven]], lay the [[Meat|meat]] in the bottom, pour the blended [[Sauce|sauce]] over the meat and mix very well\n| Cover the [[Meat|meat]] and [[Sauce|sauce]] with a doubled layer of [[grease-proof paper]], cover the pot with a doubled layer of [[tin foil]] and scrunch up around the rim, then press the lid on so there is a really good seal\n| Place the pot in the middle of the oven, '''immediately reduce the heat to 140\u00b0 C (275\u00b0 F - gas 1)''' and slow cook for 5 hours\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Slow cooked lamb tangia ready for the oven.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Ready for the oven\nImage:Slow cooked lamb tangia ready to blend.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Ready to blend\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nCheck for seasoning and then serve hot with [[boiled potatoes]] or [[plain rice]].\n\nWe had this dish with [[couscous]], but it is such a richly flavoured dish, it needs something quite bland as an accompaniment. The [[Colourful couscous recipe|couscous]] we normally cook also tends to be highly flavoured.  On reflection, I would now serve this with plain [[boiled potatoes]], [[plain boiled rice]] or [[couscous]] cooked in light stock, nothing more.\n\n===Substitutes===\nThe [[preserved lemons]] are the cornerstone of this dish and there really is no alternative (don't attempt to make this with fresh [[lemons]]!). [[Preserved lemons]] are really easy to make yourself but do need a month at least to pickle and improve.  I don't know of a UK supplier, do you? Hey, yes I do - Sainsbury's sell [[preserved lemons]], they are made by [[Belazu]].  Enjoy!  (You will need 2 bought lemons to every 1 homemade lemon)\n\n===Variations===\nThis dish could be cooked in a [[slow cooker]] (crock pot).\n==See also==\n\n* [[Slow roast recipes]]\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lamb #lambtangia #preservedlemons #butter #garlic #boiledpotatoes #mortarandpestle #onions #dutchoven #sauce #tangia </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Lamb with garlic, rosemary and anchovies a French recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#vegetables #lambwithgarlicrosemaryandanchovies #lamb #garlic #roastingtray #roast #leek #hotcapersauce #rosemary #anchovies #potatoes \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=The anchovies sound a little odd, but don't be put off, they just melt and give a slightly salty note to the meat, which is complimented by the garlic\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 5153\n|PortionCalories = 1288\n|DatePublished=22nd July 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour 10 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Lamb with garlic, rosemary and anchovies recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Slightly salty..</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">..but not fishy at all.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nThe [[Anchovies|anchovies]] sound a little odd, but don't be put off, they just melt and give a slightly salty note to the [[Meat|meat]], which is complimented by the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Rosemary|rosemary]].  If you cook this with the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] you have a complete meal.\n\nFinish off with lashings of [[balsamic vinegar gravy]] or Jamie Oliver's [[Hot mint and caper sauce|hot mint and caper sauce]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 800g leg of [[Lamb|lamb]] (about half a log)\n| 4 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, peeled and thinly sliced, lengthways\n| 10 [[Anchovy fillets|anchovy fillets]], cut in half, widthways\n| 3 whole [[Rosemary#Sprigs of rosemary|sprigs of rosemary]], remove the leaves of one and chop roughly\n| 1 [[Carrot|carrot]], peeled and quartered\n| 1 [[Parsnip|parsnip]], peeled and quartered\n| 1 [[Leek|leek]], trimmed and cut into thick rings \n| 2 big [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and quartered\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], bruised\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to it's hottest setting.\n* [[Blanch]] the [[Leek|leek]] in [[Boiling|boiling]] water and leave soaking for 10 minutes\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Roasted vegetables.jpg|Vegetables roasted\nImage:Lamb with garlic, rosemary and anchovies ready.jpg|Ready to rumble\nImage:Lamb with garlic, rosemary and anchovies ingredients.jpg|The basics\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Using a small sharp paring knife carefully stab the [[Lamb|lamb]], making deep incisions all over\n| Push the [[Garlic|garlic]] slices, [[Anchovies|anchovies]] and chopped [[Rosemary|rosemary]] into the incisions\n| Line the base of a large [[roasting tray]] with the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and drizzle with a little [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| Cut all of the vegetables into equal-sized chunks so they will cook evenly\n| Season the [[Lamb|lamb]] with [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]], place on top of the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and sprinkle with the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] and lay the other sprigs of rosemary on top of the lamb\n| '''Reduce the heat to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6)''' - this way the oven starts off really hot to sear the meat but quickly cools to roast at the correct temperature.\n| Put a smaller empty [[roasting tray]] in to heat to finish off the [[vegetables]]\n| [[Roast]] the [[Lamb|lamb]] for 30 to 40 minutes, once it is cooked to you liking, remove, keep warm and rest while the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] are completed.\n| Move the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] to the smaller tray and cook until the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] are golden [[Brown|brown]] - about 20 minutes more\n| If making the [[Hot caper sauce]], use the original [[roasting tray]] for this, then you can use all of the lovely juices\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nSlice and serve with the [[Roast|roast]] [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and [[hot caper sauce]]\n===Variations===\nThis is a great recipe for using up any odd vegetables.  Most supermarkets offer quite reasonably priced stew-packs that have a pretty good variety of vegetables, ideal for this dish.\n===Chef's notes===\nBuying [[Frozen lamb - what great value!|frozen lamb for this dish]] makes it really economical (only \u00a36.00 per kilogram 2013)\n==See also==\n* [[Slow roast recipes]]  \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#vegetables #lambwithgarlicrosemaryandanchovies #lamb #garlic #roastingtray #roast #leek #hotcapersauce #rosemary #anchovies #potatoes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Rinse well.\n|Heat the olive oil, with a twist of pepper, in a large pan over medium heat.  Once oil is hot, add the onion and carrots.  [[Saut\u00e9]]  for a few minutes, until the vegetables have started to soften, then add the garlic, stir-fry until the garlic takes some colour.\n|Add the lentils, bay leaf, and stock to the pot.  Simmer over low-medium heat for 25-35 minutes, until lentils are softened.\n}}\n===Serving suggestion===\n\nAdd a squeeze of fresh lemon juice just before serving, serve hot with crusty bread.\n\n===Variations===\n\nSprinkle with [[chili flakes]] for a spicier soup. \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Student recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lentilsoup #lentils #chiliflakes #onion #garlic #bayleaf #carrots #oliveoil #vegetablestock #diced #boiledorsimmered </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
