title": "Liver in sherry vinegar (Lebanese style)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Liver in sherry vinegar (Lebanese style) a meat recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#liver #vinegar #cinnamonstick #garlic #mint #flour #ghee #sherryvinegar #lamb #fry #oliveoil \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=The inspiration for this recipe come from a translation of a 1960's Lebanese cook-book I picked up somewhere\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2164\n|PortionCalories = 541\n|DatePublished=20th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Liver in sherry vinegar (Lebanese style) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Not as nice the second time around</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Maybe it was the liver, but quite tough</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Liver in sherry vinegar (Lebanese style).jpg|thumb|300px|right|Just before the vinegar is added. Note the huge cinnamon stick!]]\nThe inspiration for this recipe come from a translation of a 1960's Lebanese cook-book I picked up somewhere. I have always found [[Vinegar|vinegar]] a good accompaniment for [[Liver|liver]].  The original recipe just stated [[vinegar]], but I have changed this to [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]] because I love it so much.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g [[Liver|liver]] ([[Lamb|lamb]] or [[Veal|veal]] preferred)\n| 1 scant teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| [[Freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 [[Red bell pepper|red bell pepper]], de-seeded and sliced into strips\n| 3 fresh hot [[Chili peppers|chili peppers]], chopped into thin rings and de-seeded if you wish\n| 2.5 cm [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]], left whole, remove at end of cooking\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped finely\n| 5 [[Fat|fat]] [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed mixed with &frac12; teaspoon [[Dried|dried]] [[Mint|mint]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Flour|flour]]\n| 50 ml [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]]\n| 50g [[Ghee|ghee]], [[Butter|butter]] or [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Wash and clean the [[Liver|liver]] and cut into thin slices.\n| Leave in a [[colander]] for 1 hour to drain excess liquid (if you have the time). Toss in the [[Flour|flour]] to coat\n| Melt the [[Ghee|ghee]] in a pan and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Red pepper|red pepper]] and [[Onions|onions]] until they start to [[Brown|brown]], then add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Mint|mint]]. Just before the garlic starts to colour, tip in the [[Liver|liver]].\n| Add the [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]] and cook the [[Liver|liver]] for 10 minutes, turning often.\n| Add the [[Salt|salt]], [[Chillies|chillies]] and [[Vinegar|vinegar]], [[Deglaze|deglaze]] the pan, stir well and allow to reduce by a third\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe immediately, with [[cous-cous]] and vegetables.\n===Chef's note===\nThe recipe originally had 100 ml of [[vinegar]] but I found that too much for my taste so reduced it to 50ml.\n===Variations===\nUse [[red wine]] instead of [[vinegar]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Offal recipes]]\n[[Category:Veal recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#liver #vinegar #cinnamonstick #garlic #mint #flour #ghee #sherryvinegar #lamb #fry #oliveoil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Marinated olives",
                "revisions": [
                    {

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Marinated olives, Spanish recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#olives #marinatedolives #sherryvinegar #marinate #greenolives #spices #chillipowder #blackolives #cuminseeds #garlic #olive \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Having realised that I was bored with pre-prepared stuffed olives, I decided to buy plain olives, complete with stones and marinate them\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1950\n|PortionCalories = 65\n|DatePublished=20th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Servings: 30 - Marinades 1.5 kg of olives\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 1 week\n |PrepTime = 1 week\n |CookTime = None\n |Image = [[Image:Olives in marinade.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Never thought of doing this</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Trouble is, can't find raw olives in bulk \ud83d\ude10</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\n \n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\nHaving realised that I was bored with pre-prepared stuffed [[Olives|olives]], I decided to buy plain olives, complete with stones and [[Marinate|marinate]] them.  I happened to have a lot of olives when I made this, but you easily reduce the quantity.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500 g [[Green olives|green olives]], stones intact\n| 1 kg [[Black olives|black olives]], stones intact\n| [[Olive oil]], to cover\n| 1 bulb or more of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 1-2 teaspoons [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Dried thyme|dried thyme]] or [[Oregano|oregano]]\n| 90 ml [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the olives in an airtight container, such as a [[Lock&Lock boxes|Lock&Lock box]] and add enough olive oil to cover.\n| Stir in the remaining ingredients and shake vigorously.\n| Leave to [[Marinate|marinate]] for at least a week before consumption.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nUse with any recipe that calls for [[Olives|olives]], removing the stones if necessary.  Personally, I just enjoy pigging out on them on their own. \n===Variations===\nTry experimenting with your own choice of [[Herbs|herbs]] and [[Spices|spices]].  My green hojiblanca [[Olives|olives]] originated in the area around Fuente de Piedra in Andaluc\u00eda and the black ones were from Syria.  Use any combination of [[Olive|olive]] type, colour and origin.  Make your blend unique!\n===Chef's notes===\nIt is a good idea to shake the container several times daily as the [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]] sinks to the bottom.\n\nRemove the stones if you wish, but I find that [[Olives|olives]] taste better stoned at the last minute.\n\nDo not throw away the [[Marinade|marinade]] as it can be used as a dressing.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Olives marinated]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#olives #marinatedolives #sherryvinegar #marinate #greenolives #spices #chillipowder #blackolives #cuminseeds #garlic #olive </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This recipe is absolutely ideal for a barbecue\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 288\n|PortionCalories = 72\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Tunisian vegetable seller\n |Servings = 4 as a filling [[Side dish|side dish]]\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Mechouia recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Barbecue?</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.72</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Looks like a market to me</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis traditional Tunisian recipe combines [[Grilled|grilled]] [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and [[Hot chillies|hot chillies]] to make a delicious [[Salad|salad]].\n\nThis recipe is absolutely ideal for a [[Barbecue|barbecue]], espcially one with a hotplate\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 large [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] (plum-type preferred) [about 225 g]\n| 2 green [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]] [about 175 g]\n| 2 fresh [[Poblano chillies|poblano chillies]] [about 110 g]\n| 1 large [[Red onion|red onion]], un peeled\n| 2 large [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, un peeled\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Caraway seeds|caraway seeds]], [[Ground|ground]] to a powder is a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]], [[Ground|ground]] to a powder is a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| [[Zest]] and [[Juice|juice]] from half a [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 12 pitted [[Olives|olives]] (green or black) \n| 1 tablespoon [[Capers|capers]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the whole [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]], [[Chili peppers|chili peppers]], [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] on the [[Barbecue|barbecue]] hotplate, over the coals or even under an [[Oven|oven]] [[Grill|grill]].\n| Turn them often so they are really well charred.\n| Remove the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] as they are done, the [[Garlic|garlic]], for instance will be ready before the [[Onion|onion]].\n| Use the technique [[Roasted red pepper|shown here]], (or your own!), to skin the tomatoes, sweet and hot and peppers.  Remove the seeds and stems from the peppers\n| Remove the really burnt [[Onion|onion]] skin.\n| Cut all of the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] into nibble sized pieces an place in a large serving bowl.\n| Squish the [[Garlic|garlic]] from the [[Cloves|cloves]] with a cloth or a palette knife into a small bowl and mix with the garlic pulp.\n| Add the [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] and [[Zest|zest]] together with the [[Salt|salt]], [[Spices|spices]] and [[Olive oil|olive oil]].  Whisk the dressing and mix in with the [[Grilled|grilled]], chopped [[Vegetables|vegetables]].\n| Garnish with chopped [[Capers|capers]] and [[Olives|olives]]\n}}\n===Variations===\nUse [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] instead of [[Caraway|caraway]] if [[caraway]] is not to your taste.\n\n[[Tuna|Tuna]] flaked into this salad, or sliced [[hard-boiled eggs]] would turn this into a main course.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garlic #vegetables #grilled #mechouia #onion #zest #sweetpeppers #barbecue #tomatoes #oliveoil #ground </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Megadarra in a Squash",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Megadarra served in a Squash recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#rice #onions #lentils #squash #squashes #scoop #spices #orange #chillipowder #lemon #zest \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Pronounced mega-dah-ra, this simple Egyptian dish of rice, lentils and spiced onions is a super thing to squeeze into a squash\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1137\n|PortionCalories = 284\n|DatePublished=16th August 2014\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  50 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Megadarra in a Squash recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Pretty picture</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">And a tasty meal that looks fun too.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nPronounced mega-dah-ra, this simple Egyptian dish of [[Rice|rice]], [[Lentils|lentils]] and spiced [[Onions|onions]] is a super thing to squeeze into a [[Squash|squash]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 4 mini or 1 medium-sized [[Squash|squash]]\n| 75g [[Brown basmati rice|brown basmati rice]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground pepper|freshly ground pepper]]\n| 1 mug of water\n| 400g tin of [[Lentils|lentils]]\n| 2 [[Onions|onions]], thinly sliced\n| 1 tablespoon [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]]\n| A pinch of [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| A pinch of [[Ground cinnamon|ground cinnamon]]\n| 1 [[Orange|orange]] or [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| 200g [[Natural yogurt|natural yogurt]] (optional)\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 180\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Trim the base of your [[Squashes|squashes]] so they sit flat. Cut the top off your [[Squash|squash]] as if you were making a Hallowe\u0092en [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]].\n| [[Scoop]] out the [[Seeds|seeds]] (save them for later they are lovely [[Roasted|roasted]] with [[Sugar|sugar]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Spice|spice]] till golden and crisp). Pop the [[Squash|squash]] on a [[Baking tray|baking tray]]. [[Roast]] for 30 mins or till completely tender.\n| Get a lidded pan hot for your [[Rice|rice]]. Toast for a mo. Add a pinch of [[Salt|salt]] and the water. Cover. Lower heat. [[Simmer]] for 20 mins.\n| Drain your [[Lentils|lentils]]. Rinse. Once the [[Rice|rice]] is done, drain it over the [[Lentils|lentils]]. Set aside.\n| Get a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]] hot. Add a gloss of [[Oil|oil]]. Tumble your [[Onions|onions]] and a good pinch of [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] in. Sizzle [[Onions|onions]] over medium heat for about 10 mins, till golden and a little crisp. Swirl in the [[Spices|spices]]. [[Scoop]] a spoonful of onions into a dish and set aside.\n| Keep the [[Onions|onions]] over medium heat. Fold the [[Rice|rice]] and [[Lentils|lentils]] in. Add a gloss of [[Oil|oil]]. Sizzle for a mo, to give the [[Rice|rice]] a little crispy edge to it.\n| Grate in the [[Zest|zest]] of the [[Orange|orange]] or [[Lemon|lemon]]. Add a good squeeze of [[Juice|juice]]. Taste. Season (and add more [[Spices|spices]]) as needed.\n| Once you're happy with the [[Rice|rice]], stuff it into the cooked and hollowed out [[Squashes|squashes]]. Scatter the reserved [[Onion|onion]] over the top.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a pot of [[Yogurt|yogurt]], dusted with a little [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Squash recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Abel and Cole veg box recipes]]\n{{Template:Abel and Cole veg box recipes attribution}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #onions #lentils #squash #squashes #scoop #spices #orange #chillipowder #lemon #zest </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Minced lamb pittas",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Minced lamb pittas, Greek recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#yoghurt #lamb #pittabreads #mincedlambpittas #onion #garlic #coriander #salad #sesameseeds #tomatoes #cuminseeds \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=The typical North African flavours are unmistakable in this dish. Ideally accompanied by tomatoes, salad, lemon wedges and yogurt\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2063\n|PortionCalories = 1031\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Lamb pittas\n |Servings = Serves 2\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Lamb pittas recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Finger food</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">We don't often have lamb, and minced, even less.  This is a great way to use it and it's not too greasy.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThe typical [[North African]] flavours are unmistakable in this dish.  Ideally accompanied by [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Salad|salad]], [[Lemon wedges|lemon wedges]] and [[Yoghurt|yogurt]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 teaspoons [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon white [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| &frac14; teaspoon [[Ground cinnamon|ground cinnamon]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 2 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 250 g [[Minced|minced]] [[Lamb|lamb]]\n| 4 [[Pitta breads|pitta breads]]\n}}\n'''to garnish'''\n* 1 tablespoon [[Sesame seeds|sesame seeds]]\n* 125 ml [[Yoghurt|yogurt]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Powder the [[Coriander|coriander]], [[Cumin|cumin]], ([[Cinnamon|cinnamon]] if sticks) in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]].\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Frying pan|frying pan]], add the [[Onion|onion]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and all of the [[Spices|spices]] and gently [[Stir fry|stir fry]] for 7 minutes.\n| Turn up the heat a little and add the [[Lamb|lamb]].  [[Fry]] for 9 minutes, stirring often.\n| Stir in the fresh [[Coriander|coriander]] and serve.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe in [[Pitta breads|pitta breads]] with a little [[Salad|salad]] and sliced tomaotes, sprinkle with [[Sesame seeds|sesame seeds]] and serve with [[Yoghurt|yogurt]] as a [[Side dish|side dish]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Greek recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#yoghurt #lamb #pittabreads #mincedlambpittas #onion #garlic #coriander #salad #sesameseeds #tomatoes #cuminseeds </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Mitmita powder",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Mitmita powder recipe Cooking with chillies\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#mitmitapowder #dryroast #coffeegrinder #cardamomseeds #mortarandpestle #fulmedames #clovebuds #sidedish #favabeans #birdseyechilipeppers #groundcumin \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Mitmita (or mit'mitma) is a very spicy powdered seasoning used in the Cuisine of Ethiopia\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 10\n|PortionCalories = 10\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 1\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 35 minutes (incl cooling time)\n |PrepTime = 30 minutes\n |CookTime = 5 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Mitmita powder.jpg|200px|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Is this authentic?</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This sure is tasty, but I'd love to know if it's authentic. Let me know, if you know.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Mitmita''' (or '''mit'mitma''') is a very spicy powdered seasoning used in the Cuisine of Ethiopia. It is orange-red in colour and can contain ground African [[birdseye chili peppers]], [[cardamom seeds]], [[cloves]], [[ground cinnamon]], [[ground cumin]], [[ginger powder]] and [[salt]]. It is used to season the raw beef dish kitfo and may also be sprinkled on [[ful medames]] and [[fava beans]].\nI have search many, many cookbooks for a definitive  mitmitma recipe, without much success. The two recipes below are the closest to the average find\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| A small handful of dried bird's eye chillies\n| 1/2 a teaspoon of black mustard seeds\n*| 1/2 a teaspoon of sea salt\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Dry roast]] the chilies and mustard seeds, taking care they don't pop everywhere.\n| Leave to cool\n| Grind to a fine powder in a [[coffee grinder]] or [[mortar and pestle]]\n| Store in an airtight container\n}}\n==Alternative mit'mita recipe==\n===Ingredient ratios===\n* 10 lb fresh [[bird's eye chillies]]\n** or 2lb dried [[bird's eye chillies]]\n* 2 tablespoons of [[clove buds]]\n* 1/4 cup of brown [[cardamom seeds]], shelled\n* 1 cup salt\n===Method===\n* Dry the chillies in a very low oven or in the sun\n* [[Dry roast]] the remaining spices and allow to cool\n* Grind all the ingredients to a fine powder in a [[coffee grinder]] or [[mortar and pestle]]\n* Store in an airtight container\n===Servings===\nServes 4 as a [[Side dish|side dish]]\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Condiments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Prepared foods]]\n[[Category:Spices]]\n[[Category:Store cupboard items]]\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Dry fried]]\n{{CategoryLineIngredients}}\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#mitmitapowder #dryroast #coffeegrinder #cardamomseeds #mortarandpestle #fulmedames #clovebuds #sidedish #favabeans #birdseyechilipeppers #groundcumin </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

night]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| Grind of fresh [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 4 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 2 cm [[Fresh ginger|fresh ginger]], peeled and finely chopped or [[Grated|grated]]\n| 1 medium [[Carrot|carrot]], peeled and [[Diced|diced]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ground|ground]] [[Turmeric|turmeric]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Chili flakes|chili flakes]]\n| 2 teaspoons freshly [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]] [[Seeds|seeds]]\n| 2 teaspoons freshly [[Ground coriander|ground coriander]]\n| 2.5 cm (1\") piece of [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]]\n| 400g can of [[Plum tomatoes|plum tomatoes]], chopped\n| 800 ml [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 150 g minutes\n| Add the [[Carrot|carrot]] and [[Spices|spices]] and mix well and cook for 2 minutes to coat the [[Vegetables|vegetables]]\n| Add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Stock|stock]] and the milk and whirled into the stew adds a touch of luxury!\n\nThis was made around Christmas time, so the next day, I fried some [[onions]] and [[curry paste]], blitzed the second half of the stew in a [[food processor]], added leftover turkey trimmings and made a wonderful turkey curry. Even after a prolonged period in the blender, the stew still had a fabulous texture with plenty of bite and also colour from the [[spinach]] and [[carrot]] pieces.  This will be made again.  Sorry Gent.\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#moroccanchickpealentilandspinachstew #carrot #onions #dried #lentils #cinnamonstick #spinach #chickpeas #garlic #stock #groundcoriander </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Moroccan lamb, a 30 minute recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#lamb #raselhanout #rice #courgettes #chickpeas #lemonwedges #onions #currants #almonds #cardamoms #spice \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A Moroccan/North African style lamb dish that can be prepared and cooked in 30 minutes. This is not a hot dish but a fragrant one\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1525\n|PortionCalories = 762\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 2\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Moroccan lamb (30 minute recipe) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">One pan lamb!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Wonderful - love the almonds too</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nA [[Moroccan]]/[[North African]] style [[Lamb|lamb]] dish that can be prepared and cooked in 30 minutes.\n\nThis is not a hot dish but a fragrant one.  If you want heat then serve it with [[harrisa paste]] or a [[Hot chilli sauce|hot chilli sauce]].\n\nIf you don't have [[Ras el hanout|ras el hanout]], make a fragrant [[Spice|spice]] mix by [[Grinding|grinding]] up [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], [[Cumin|cumin]], [[cardamoms]] and cook with a few fresh [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 300g [[Fillet of lamb tenderloin|fillet of lamb tenderloin]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 2 teaspoons of [[Ras el hanout|ras el hanout]]\n| 2 small [[Onions|onions]], peeled and thinly sliced\n| 1 [[Red pepper|red pepper]], de-seeded and sliced\n| 150 g [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]], washed, rinsed and drained\n| 125 ml [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]]\n| 125 ml water\n| 1 tablespoon [[Currants|currants]], [[Sultanas|sultanas]] or chopped [[Dried apricots|dried apricots]]\n| 1 small [[Courgette|courgette]], thinly sliced\n| 2 tablespoons flaked [[Almonds|almonds]]\n| [[Greek yogurt]] and [[Lemon wedges|lemon wedges]] to serve\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n\n''' cooking the [[Lamb|lamb]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rub the [[Lamb|lamb]] fillet with 1 teaspoon of [[Ras el hanout|ras el hanout]]\n| Heat 1 tablespoon of [[Oil|oil]] to a shallow pan, [[Brown|brown]] the [[Lamb|lamb]] on either side and then continue to cook until to your liking - remove and keep warm.\n}} \n''' cooking the [[Rice|rice]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In the same pan, heat the remaining [[Oil|oil]] and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] for 3 or 4 minutes.\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] and coat with the [[Oil|oil]], then add the [[Ras el hanout|ras el hanout]], [[Stock|stock]], water and [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]].\n| Cook, covered, for 10 minutes.\n| Add the sliced [[Courgettes|courgettes]] and [[Currants|currants]], mix well, cover and cook for a further 5 minutes so the [[courgettes]] are warmed and the [[Rice|rice]] is cooked.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nSprinkle with [[Almonds|almonds]] and serve with [[Yogurt|yogurt]], [[Lemon wedges|lemon wedges]] and [[Harissa|harissa]] or [[Chilli|chilli]] [[Sauce|sauce]].\n===Variations===\nWe used some leftover [[Chickpea mash|chickpea mash]] instead of canned [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]].\n\nI think that next I would griddle the [[courgettes]] and toast the [[almond flakes]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lamb #raselhanout #rice #courgettes #chickpeas #lemonwedges #onions #currants #almonds #cardamoms #spice </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Moroccan meatloaf with peppers and pistachios",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Moroccan meatloaf with peppers and pistachios a fruit recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pomegranatemolasses #raselhanout #bulgurwheat #fry #moroccanmeatloafwithpeppersandpistachios #onion #egg #apricots #bake #pistachios #bainmarie \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=The economical meal is simple to prepare and cook and ingredients can be easily changed to taste\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2493\n|PortionCalories = 623\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Moroccan meatloaf with pistachios and peppers\n |Servings = Serves 4 to 6 people\n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 3 hours 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 2 hours 45 minutes\n |CookTime = 40 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Moroccan meatloaf with pomegranate molasses recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Fabulous hot or cold</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.8</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Very nice, the pomegranate adds an odd lemony tang which was not unpleasant.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThe economical meal is simple to prepare and cook and ingredients can be easily changed to suit your taste.  It is a wonderfully fragrant dish and would be brilliant for dinner parties (if we had such things). The lamb was perfectly moist and slightly pink in the centre. We had this with [[seedy naans]] and [[tzatziki]].\n[[Image:Moroccan meatloaf with pomegranate molasses.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Fresh out of the oven]]\n \nI 'created' this dish because I wanted to try out my recently obtained [[ras el hanout]] and [[pomegranate molasses]]. \nIf you don't have [[ras el hanout]], see the [[ras el hanout]] page and make your own spice mix.\n\nThough not a replacement for [[pomegranate molasses]], a sprinkle of [[sugar]] or runny [[honey]] and the juice and zest of an [[orange]] or [[tangerine]] would work just as well.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sunflower oil|sunflower oil]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 3 [[Cloves garlic, crushed|cloves garlic, crushed]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[ras el hanout]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chili powder|chili powder]] or [[chili flakes]]\n| [[Freshly ground black pepper]] and salt to taste\n| 500g [[Minced|minced]] [[Lamb|lamb]]\n| 1 [[Egg|egg]], beaten\n| 50 g [[bulgur wheat]] soaked in 1 pint of warm water for 30 minutes then drained\n| 40 g [[Pistachios|pistachios]], husks removed, (80g with shells)\n| 1 large [[Red pepper|red pepper]], [[Roasted|roasted]] and peeled and chopped finely\n| 3 tablespoons [[pomegranate molasses]]\n| 6 [[Dried apricots|dried apricots]], chopped\n| 4 bay leaves\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Lighly grease a small loaf tin\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a pan and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] until translucent, about 5 minutes\n| Add the [[Spices|spices]], [[salt]] and [[pepper]] and [[Fry|fry]] off for another minute or so then remove from the heat\n| Add the onions to a bowl together with the uncooked [[lamb]], [[bulgur wheat]], beaten [[egg]], [[Pistachios|pistachios]], and [[Peppers|peppers]] and combine with your hands\n| Pack the mix into the loaf tin, brush the surface with 3 tablespoons of [[pomegranate molasses]], scatter the chopped [[apricots]] over the top and garnish with the [[bay leaves]]\n| Leave to stand for a few hours. I felt this was needed to ensure the [[bulgur]] soaked up the surrounding moisture. It may not be needed, it certainly won't hurt though.\n| Stand the meatloaf tin in a deep [[roasting dish]], half-filled with [[Boiling|boiling]] water\n| Cover the the large dish with [[tin foil]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 30 minutes\n| Remove the [[foil]], take the tray out of the [[bain marie]] and [[Bake|bake]] uncovered for a further 10 minutes\n| Remove from the oven and allow to rest for 15 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe sliced, hot or cold\n\nServe with [[Batatas harras (Lebanese spiced potatoes)]]\n===Variations===\n* Add a sprinkle of [[almond flakes]] once it's out of the [[bain marie]]\n* Try [[sultanas]] instead of [[apricots]].\n* This could also be made with [[Minced beef|minced beef]]\n* Line the baking dish with streaky [[Bacon|bacon]] - not very Moroccan though!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pomegranatemolasses #raselhanout #bulgurwheat #fry #moroccanmeatloafwithpeppersandpistachios #onion #egg #apricots #bake #pistachios #bainmarie </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]

Season the [[Soup|soup]], add the [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] to taste and gently reheat.\n| Stir in the fresh [[Coriander|coriander]], reserving a little for the garnish. \n| Drizzle the [[Argan Oil]] over the [[Soup|soup]] before serving.\n}}\n===Variations===\n[[Mint]] is often used as a garnish with Moroccan dishes\n(''Sainsbury's Magazine'')\n\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/argan-oil.html Belazu Argan Oil]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#arganoil #moroccanredlentilsoupwithcoriander #soup #garlic #coriander #carrots #belazu #butter #onions #lemon #spices </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Hot, hot, hot!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span </span></span>\n}} \nA spicy relish from North Africa\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 5 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 large [[Red onion|red onion]], thinly sliced\n| 1 bulb [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled\n| [[Salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Ground coriander|ground coriander]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Muscovado|muscovado]] [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| A few [[Saffron strands|saffron strands]]\n| 50 ml warm water\n| A small piece of [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]]\n| 4 small [[Dried|dried]] [[Bird's Eye chillies]]\n| 1 large [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]]\n| 45 ml [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]]\n| 45 ml hot.\n| Add the [[Onions|onions]], reduce the heat to low immediately and stir.\n| Cover and [[Fry|fry]] until they are soft, stirring from time to time.\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves and continue cooking, covered, until the [[Garlic|garlic]] starts to soften.\n| Next, add the [[Coriander|coriander]] and the [[Sugar|sugar]], stir, and cook uncovered for a further 5 minutes.\n| In the meantime add the [[Saffron|saffron]] to the warm water and leave to soak for 5 minutes.\n| Add to the [[Onions|onions]], with the [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]], [[Sherry|sherry]] vingear and [[Orange juice|orange juice]].\n| Cook gently until the liquid has evaporated.\n| Add the [[Lemon|lemon]] and cook for a further 5 minutes.\n| Remove the [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]], and adjust seasonings if necessary.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThis is best made the day before consumption.  [[Refrigerate]], but allow to come up to room temperature before serving.  Goes well with [[Cheese|cheese]] or cold [[Meat|meat]].\n==See also==\n* Other [[Onion relish]] recipes\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Onion, garlic and chilli relish]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Onion, garlic and chilli relish]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces|Onion, garlic and chilli relish]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Onion, garlic and chilli relish]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Onion, garlic and chilli relish]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Onion, garlic and chilli relish]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#oniongarlicandchillirelish #garlic #orangejuice #onions #bayleaf #saffron #bayleaves #saffronstrands #dried #groundcoriander #panfried </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

#parsley #mint #lentils #lamb #mutton #dough \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Although normally made from lamb, this Algerian soup can also be found made from mutton or veal\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4503\n|PortionCalories = 750\n|DatePublished=17th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 3\n |ImageComment = [[Semolina]] dumplings\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 50 minutes\n |PrepTime = 30 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Semolina_dumplings_recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Sounds like school dinners</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">They always had semolina, though not as dumplings, I recell?</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nAlthough normally made from [[Lamb|lamb]], this Algerian [[Soup|soup]] can also be found made from [[Mutton|mutton]] or [[Veal|veal]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 tablespoons [[Oil|oil]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], finely chopped\n| 225 g [[Lamb|lamb]], [[Mutton|mutton]] or [[Veal|veal]], cut into 1 cm cubes\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Paprika|paprika]]\n| &frac14; teaspoon [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Harissa|harissa]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], finely chopped\n| 2 tablespoons [[Parsley|parsley]], finely chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[Mint|mint]], finely chopped\n| 3 large [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]] and chopped\n| 1.8 [[Litres|litres]] water or [[Stock|stock]]\n| 175 g whole [[Lentils|lentils]]\n}}\n'''For the [[Semolina|semolina]] [[Dumplings|dumplings]]'''\n* 375 g medium [[Semolina|semolina]]\n* &frac12; [[Onion|onion]], finely chopped\n* 1 tablespoon [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], finely chopped\n* 1 tablespoon [[Parsley|parsley]], finely chopped\n* 1 tablespoon [[Mint|mint]], finely chopped\n* 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n* &frac12; teaspoon [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n* 1 [[Egg|egg]], beaten\n* 90 ml [[Oil|oil]]\n* 90 ml water\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large pan and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onion|onion]] until soft.\n| Add the [[Meat|meat]] and cook until it has [[Browned|browned]] on all sides.\n| Stir in the [[Salt|salt]], [[Paprika|paprika]], [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], [[Harissa|harissa]], [[Coriander|coriander]], [[Parsley|parsley]], [[Mint|mint]] and [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]].\n| Cook over a low heat for 10 minutes, stirring regularly.\n| Add the water or [[Stock|stock]] and the [[Lentils|lentils]] and bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| Lower the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 20 minutes.\n| Meanwhile, make the [[Semolina|semolina]] [[Dumplings|dumplings]] by mixing the semolina, [[Onion|onion]], [[Herbs|herbs]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] in a bowl.\n| Mix in the [[Egg|egg]] and the [[Oil|oil]] and add enough water to make a pliable [[Dough|dough]] which holds together.\n| Dampen your hands and roll the [[Dough|dough]] into [[Apricot|apricot]] sized balls.\n| When the [[Soup|soup]] has finished [[Simmering|simmering]] add the [[Dumplings|dumplings]] to the pan and [[Simmer|simmer]] for a further 30 minutes until the [[Meat|meat]] and [[Lentils|lentils]] are cooked.\n| If the [[Soup|soup]] is too thick, add a little more water or [[Stock|stock]].\n| Place the [[Dumplings|dumplings]] in bowls and ladle the [[Soup|soup]] over them.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThis is quite a hearty [[Soup|soup]] so you may not need anything to accompany it, but [[Bread|bread]] would be fine.\n==See also==\n* [[Schwemmkn\u00f6del (Semolina dumplings)]] from Austria\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Osbane es'smid (meat soup fillet if possible)\n| 120 g [[Philadelphia Original]]\n| 100 g [[Ground almonds|ground almonds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Garam masala|garam masala]]\n| 4 cm piece of [[Ginger|ginger]] peeled & chopped\n| 2 [[Cloves|cloves]] [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]] sliced\n| 1 tablespoon [[Oil|oil]]\n}}\n'''to serve'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| serve with [[Pitta breads|pitta breads]] and a [[Green salad|green salad]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Place the Philly, [[Almonds|almonds]], [[Ginger|ginger]] and, [[Garlic|garlic]] into a [[Blender|blender]] with 200ml water and [[Blend|blend]] until smooth then stir in the [[Garam masala|garam masala]].\n| Heat a large pan and add the [[Oil|oil]], [[Brown|brown]] the [[Meat|meat]] on all sides then remove from the pan.\n| Lower the heat, tip in the [[Onions|onions]] and cook until they are soft and [[Brown|brown]].\n| Return the [[Meat|meat]] to the pan and pour over the [[Sauce|sauce]].\n| Bring to a [[Simmer|simmer]] and put a lid on the pan.\n| Cook for 30 mins until the [[Lamb|lamb]] is cooked and tender.\n}}\n\n===Variations===\nIf you don't have [[Garam masala|garam masala]], use a mixture of [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] and a pinch of each, [[Ground cinnamon|ground cinnamon]], [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]], [[Ground coriander|ground coriander]] and [[Black pepper|black pepper]].\n===Recipe title": "Pitta bread recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Pitta bread, a breadmaker recipe Cooking Wiki\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#wholemealflour #yeast #dough #breadmaker #warmplace #vitaminc #pittabreadrecipe #yellowcornmeal #flour #whiteflour #bakingtray \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Pita (pita bread, pitta or pitta bread) is a wheat flatbread made with yeast. It can be white (normal flour) or brown when made with wholemeal flour\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{recipesummary\n|Image comment = The best pitta breads you will ever have tasted\n|Servings = 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 1 hour\n|DatePublished=25th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|PrepTime = 45 minutes\n|CookTime = 15 minutes\n|TotalCalories = 1035\n|PortionCalories = 258\n|Image = [[Image:Pitta bread ready to eat.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nicer than shop bought pittas</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">These have a lovely chwy texture that you don't get from commercial pittas.  The outsides are always crunchy too.  Lovely</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Pitta bread arms length.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Roll them out the length of your arm!]]\nPita (pita bread, pitta or pitta bread) is a [[wheat]] flatbread made with [[yeast]]. It can be white (normal flour) or brown when made with [[wholemeal flour]]. \n\nSimilar to other double-layered flat or pocket breads, pita is traditional in many Middle Eastern and Mediterranean cuisines. It is prevalent from North Africa and the Middle East.\n\nThe Indian flatbread form of [[roti]] is sometimes referred to as \"Indian pita\".\n\nWe also have a [[Crispbread|brilliantly simple recipe]] that in a few moments turns normal pitta breads into buttery crispbread. You won't believe how good it is until you try it.\n\nThis recipe is simple and delicious and the results are far better than shop-bought pittas.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| &#190; a teaspoon of [[Dried active yeast|dried active yeast]]\n| 250 g (8.5 oz) strong white flour\n| &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; or 200 g (7 oz) strong [[white flour]] and 50 g (1.5 oz) strong [[Wholemeal flour|wholemeal flour]] for a light wholemeal pitta\n| A pinch of [[ascorbic acid]] or 1 [[vitamin C]] tablet, crushed between 2 tablespoons - (''300mg to 500 mg'') - ''optional''\n| 1 teaspoon [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 145 ml water\n\n}}\n===Method===\n\n\n'''Hand method'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix a little of the water (which should be at body temperature/lukewarm, about 37\u00b0C) with the [[Sugar|sugar]] and the [[Yeast|yeast]], whisk up and leave in a [[warm place]] for 10 minutes to froth up\n| Mix the [[Yeast|yeast]] solution together with the remaining ingredients and [[Kneading bread|knead]] for 10 minutes until you have a pliable [[dough]]\n| Cover with a damp [[Tea|tea]] towel and leave in a [[warm place]] for about an hour to rise\n}}\n\n'''Breadmaker method'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Tip all of the ingredients into your [[bread maker]]\n| Set it to the short [[dough]] program (normally the pizza dough setting)\n| Panasonic SD253 breadmaker, use pizza setting.\n| '''[[Panasonic SD-ZB2502 automatic breadmaker]] use menu option 22, pizza dough setting.'''\n| 45 minutes later, proceed as below\n}}\n\n'''Either method - continue from here'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Divide into 4 balls [about 100g each] and roll out into oval shapes, about the length of your arm.\n| If you have the time, leave in a [[warm place]] for 30 minutes to rise a little\n| Preheat the [[grill]]\n| Place on a [[Yellow cornmeal|cornmeal dusted]] [[pizza stone]] or lightly oiled [[baking tray]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 5 to 6 minutes, keeping a watchful eye on them.\n}}\n===Chef's tip===\n\nDon't allow these to get too [[Browned|browned]], especially if you are likely to reheat them again before eating.\n\nWe made the batch shown with [[wholemeal flour]] (plus 1/4 of a crushed [[vitamin C]] tablet, for the ascorbic acid needed when using [[wholemeal flour]] in a [[bread maker]])\n\nIf the [[dough]] is a little too wet (or dry), just add a little more [[flour]] (or water) and run it through the [[bread maker]] again. It only takes another 45 minutes and no further involvement on your part.\n\nAlthough this recipe quantity ideally makes 4 pitta breads, you can make 6 mini pittas instead.  They are smaller than pittas we find in the UK, but are great for little snack pockets if filled!\n\n===Arm's length roll out===\nAfter reading The Fabulous Baker Brothers cookbook [ISBN 0755363701, 9780755363704] and following their suggestion to roll the pittas ''the length of your forearm'', that's what I now do.  The pittas generally shrink when they puff up so you get lovely oval pittas.  Thanks guys!\n\n===Variations===\n\nSee the [[Talk:Pitta bread recipe|comments page]] page for variations to this recipe. \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Breadmaker recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Prepared foods]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#wholemealflour #yeast #dough #breadmaker #warmplace #vitaminc #pittabreadrecipe #yellowcornmeal #flour #whiteflour #bakingtray </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 400 ml warm water\n| 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 25g [[Butter|butter]], broken into [[Pea|pea]]-sized pieces\n}}\n'''garnish'''\n* 15 g [[Butter|butter]]\n* 3 tablespoons flaked [[Almond slivers|almond slivers]]\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3), [fan oven 140\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Couscous|couscous]] and the warm water to an [[Oven|oven]]-proof dish and stir in the [[Salt|salt]]\n| Leave for 10 minutes for the water to absorb\n| Using your fingers, rub the [[Oil|oil]] into the [[Couscous|couscous]] and separate the [[Grains|grains]]\n| Dot the [[Butter|butter]] over the top, cover with tin-[[Oil|oil]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 15 minutes\n| Meanwhile, heat the 15g of [[Butter|butter]] in a [[Frying pan|frying pan]] over a medium heat, add the [[Almonds|almonds]] and [[Fry|fry]] until they just start to turn golden, stirring all the while.\n| Arrange the [[Couscous|couscous]] in a mound on a plate and top with the [[Almonds|almonds]] and [[Butter|butter]].\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Algerian recipes]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Libyan recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Student recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#butter #couscous #plainbutteredcouscous #almonds #dried #fry #pea #bake #roast #tagine #oliveoil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

I added a some [[parsley]] to bulk out my meagre winter herbs\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Parson's nose|Remove the parson's nose]] from the chicken.\n| Season the [[Chicken|chicken]] inside and out. [[Mash]] the [[Herbs|herbs]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] with 3 tablespoons of [[Oil|oil]] to form a paste.\n| Slide your fingers between the skin and flesh of the [[Chicken|chicken]] and rub the paste as evenly as possible over the breasts. Chop half of the [[Lemon slices|lemon slices]] and mix with half the [[Olives|olives]] and half the [[Mushrooms|mushrooms]]. Stuff the cavity with this mixture. in the cavity. \n| Put the bird in a heavy [[Casserole|casserole]] (such as [[Le Creuset]]). Scatter round the [[Sun-dried tomatoes|sun-dried tomatoes]], [[green pepper]] slices, [[Onion|onion]], remaining [[Lemon|lemon]], [[olives]] and [[mushrooms]] and pour over the [[Wine|wine]] and the remaining olive oil.\n| [[Roast]] for about 1 &frac34; hours.  Covered for the first 45 minutes, remove the cover then [[Baste|baste]] every 20 minutes until the chicken is properly cooked,\n| To serve, spoon the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] from the cavity and set the [[Chicken|chicken]] on a board. \n| Skim [[Fat|fat]] off the juices in the [[Casserole|casserole]], bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and serve hot with the carved chicken. Delicious with [[barley couscous]].\n}}\n''(Orlando Murrin in The Daily Express)''\n\n\n===Serving suggestion===\nDelicious with [[barley couscous]].\n\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/black-with-herbs.html Belazu black herb olives]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/belazu-pickled-lemons.html Belazu Preserved Lemon]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/traditional-barley-couscous.html Belazu Traditional Barley Couscous]\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:French recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#potroastedmediterraneanchicken #chicken #barleycouscous #herb #belazu #oliveoil #onion #mushrooms #herbs #garlic #olives </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Preserved lemons",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Preserved lemons, a fruit recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#lemon #preservedlemons #lemons #couscous #corianderseeds #pickled #lemonjuice #sterilise #ricedishes #bayleaves \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=These are brilliant and have gone from being a novelty to a necessity in this kitchen\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 360\n|PortionCalories = 51\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 7 lemons fill a 2 litre preserving jar\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 20 minutes\n|PrepTime = 20 minutes\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:RecipePreserved lemons.jpg|200px|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n======Best recipe review======\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Great fun</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Easy to make, fasbulously useful and much nicer then the commercial variety. \ud83c\udf4b\ud83c\udf4b\ud83c\udf4b</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThese are brilliant and have gone from being a novelty to a necessity in this kitchen.  Most recipes call for the flesh to be discarded and only the peel to be used, however we have found that it's all good.\n\nAnother great use is a to use a tablespoon or so of the pungent salty juice in salad dressings and dips.\n\nThey also look great in the kitchen and they are simple to make.  This recipe originates from Morocco.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 7 unwaxed [[lemons]]\n| 1 litre bottled [[lemon]] juice (normally about 4 bottles)\n| 2 tablespoons [[coriander seeds]]\n| 4 fresh [[bay leaves]], rinsed under boiling water\n| 7 tablespoons coarse [[sea salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n\nMany recipes call for the juice from fresh [[lemon]]s, but as we use so much of this, we've found bottled lemon juice to be just as good.\n\nTo ensure no bacteria contaminates this preserve, [[sterilise]] everything and use tongs or clean rubber gloves when handling the contents.\n{{RecipeMethod\n| If using waxed [[lemons]] (the norm), wash under very hot water to remove the wax\n| Cut the [[lemons]] into quarters from the top, not completing the cuts so they open like flowers\n| Pack each [[lemon]] with about a tablespoon of [[sea salt]] and place in the jar\n| Add the coriander seeds and the bay leaves\n| Pour in enough [[lemon]] juice to cover the lemons completely\n| If they bob up over the surface, wedge a piece of sterilised plastic over the top [[lemon]] to hold it under the juice. A disposable coffee spoon works well here. \n| Leave for 1 month before use\n| Will keep for upto 1 year, but you'll use them up way before then!\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nUse the rind and flesh in slow cooked stews, tagines, [[couscous]] and [[rice dishes]].\n\nThe juice alone works especially well anywhere [[lemon juice]] and [[salt]] is called for, but with an extra pungent tang.\n\nIf you find they are too salty for certain dishes, refresh them under cold running water before use. \n\n===Chef's notes===\n\nAlthough they look great on the worktop, these keep better if [[Talk:Preserved lemons|stored in the dark]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Lemons]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Lemons]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces|Lemons]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Lemons]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves]]\n[[Category:Marinades_dressings_and_butters|Lemons]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n[[Category:Pickled]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lemon #preservedlemons #lemons #couscous #corianderseeds #pickled #lemonjuice #sterilise #ricedishes #bayleaves </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

'''do not add any [[Salt|salt]]''', otherwise the peas will not absorb the water properly. Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 1 hour or until softened.  They may take a little longer depending on size and age.\n| Drain, rinse and allow to cool a little\n| Add to a [[Food processor|food processor]] with everything but the [[Olive oil|olive oil]]. Blend to a paste, then as if making [[Mayonnaise|mayonnaise]], gradually drizzle in the [[Olive|olive]] [[Oil|oil]] with the motor running.\n| Adjust the consistency by adding a little cold water if too thick.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Hummus recipe blending.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Blending the hummus\nImage:Chickpeas cooked.jpg|thumb|300px|right|500g of cooked chickpeas\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Crisp Bread|crispbread]] or [[Pittas|pittas]].\n{{SeeAlsoHummus}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Greek recipes|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes|Hummus]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Starters|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Turkish recipes|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Hummus]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chickpeas #preservedlemonhummus #dried #preservedlemon #oliveoil #boil #mayonnaise #simmer #unusualrecipes #garlic #pittas </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Was good though.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nA nice [[Vegetarian|vegetarian]] recipe that uses [[Belazu]] rose [[Harissa|harissa]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 tablespoons [[Belazu]] [[Argan Oil]] \n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped \n| 2 Cloves [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and chopped \n| 1 teaspoon [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Ground cinnamon|ground cinnamon]] \n| 1 tablespoon [[Belazu]] Rose [[Harissa]] \n| 3 [[Plum|plum]] [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]] and chopped \n| 1 x 250g pack [[Green beans|green beans]], ends trimmed, cut into small pieces \n| 500g [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]] peeled and cut into small cubes \n| 1 tablespoon [[Plain flour|plain flour]] \n| [[Juice|juice]] of one [[Lemon|lemon]] \n| 2 [[Belazu]] [[Preserved lemons|preserved lemons]], flesh removed and discarded, peel cut into strips \n| 2 tablespoons chopped fresh [[Coriander|coriander]], plus a few sprigs to garnish \n| 20 [[Black olives|black olives]], pitted \n| [[Salt|salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Argan Oil|argan oil]] in the [[Casserole|casserole]], [[Dutch Oven|dutch oven]] or [[Tagine|tagine]], add the [[Onion|onion]] and cook on a low heat to soften.\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and cook for 1 minute, then stir in the [[Spices|spices]], the [[Harissa]] and half a teaspoon of [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]].\n| Cook for 1 minute. Add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and stir. Add the [[Green beans|green beans]] and place the [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]] cubes on top. Add 225ml of cold water, bring to the [[Boil|boil]] then [[Simmer|simmer]], covered for 25-30 minutes. Do not stir during this time.\n| Check that the [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]] is cooked - if not, stir and cook for a further 5 minutes.\n| Make a paste of the [[Flour|flour]] and [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] and add 2 tablespoons of cooking liquid. Stir this into the [[Casserole|casserole]], then dot the [[Lemon|lemon]] strips and [[Olives|olives]] on the top. \n| Cook for a further 5 minutes on a low heat, stirring gently. Finally, season and stir in the chopped [[Coriander|coriander]] and garnish with the sprigs.\n}}\n''(Sainsbury's Magazine)''\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Couscous|couscous]]. \n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Squash recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/argan-oil.html Belazu Argan Oil]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/black-with-herbs.html Belazu Black olives with herbs]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/belazu-pickled-lemons.html Belazu Preserved Lemon]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/rose-harissa.html Belazu Rose Harissa]\n==See also==\n{{Tagine-recipe-list}}\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#belazu #pumpkinandgreenbeantagine #pumpkin #harissa #onion #garlic #arganoil #lemon #greenbeans #casserole #coriander </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It's a wonderful warm spicy mix, reminiscent of Arabian cuisine.  I notice that Bart's [[Spices]] now produce one, but I doubt if it'll be as good as Birgit's!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 tablespoon [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 2 [[Carrots|carrots]], cut in half, lengthways and sliced thickly\n| 310g skinless [[Chicken|chicken]] breasts, cut into thin strips\n| 3 teaspoons [[Ras el hanout|ras el hanout]]\n| 400g can of [[Plum tomatoes|plum tomatoes]], chopped\n| 300ml hot [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] (make from a Knorr [[Stock cube|stock cube]] if you wish)\n| 410g can of chick peas or [[Beans#Quantities:_dried_beans_vs_cooked_beans_vs_canned_beans|the equivalent amount of dried beans, cooked]]\n| Handful of [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] and stalks, chopped\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large pan or [[Wok|wok]], add the [[Carrots|carrots]] and [[Onions|onions]] and [[sweat]] them down for 10 minutes\n| Remove and reserve the [[Carrots|carrots]] and [[Onions|onions]]\n| Increase the heat and [[Brown|brown]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] strips for 4 minutes or so\n| Stir in the [[Spice|spice]] mix and continue to heat for a few more minutes\n| Return the [[Carrots|carrots]] and [[Onions|onions]] to the pan, then add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] and the [[Stock|stock]]. Season to taste with [[Salt|salt]]\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]], covered for 25 minutes or so.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with plain rice of couscous.\n==See also==\n* [[Ras el hanout chicken (1)|Another version of this recipe]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#raselhanout #garlic #carrots #chicken #parsley #stock #thespiceshop #chickpeas #celery #spices #onions </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Red cabbage and Belazu preserved lemons",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Red cabbage and Belazu preserved lemons a fruit recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#sultanas #onion #cinnamon #belazu #cabbage #preservedlemons #garlic #coriander #redcabbageandbelazupreservedlemons #vegetarian #cinnamonstick \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Another vegetarian side-dish recipe in which to use your preserved lemons\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 501\n|PortionCalories = 125\n|DatePublished=4th April 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 50 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Belazu preserved lemons.jpg|200px|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Different!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">An interesting idea.  I prefer to make my own preserved lemons though.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nAnother [[Vegetarian|vegetarian]] side-dish recipe in which to use your [[Preserved lemons|preserved lemons]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 tablespoons [[Belazu]] [[Extra virgin olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]] \n| 4 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, peeled but whole \n| 2 [[Cloves|cloves]] \n| 1 [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]] \n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] \n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], sliced \n| 1 medium [[Red cabbage|red cabbage]], cored and roughly chopped \n| 2 [[Belazu]] [[Preserved lemons|preserved lemons]] \n| 2 tablespoons [[Sultanas|sultanas]] \n| 2 tablespoons [[White wine vinegar|white wine vinegar]] \n| 1 tablespoon [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]] \n| 125ml fresh [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]] \n| Freshly chopped [[Coriander|coriander]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180C / fan160 / gas 4\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a flameproof [[Casserole|casserole]] with a lid over a medium heat. \n|[[Fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Cloves|cloves]] and [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]] together until the garlic starts to [[Brown|brown]]. Add the [[Cumin|cumin]] and [[Onion|onion]] and stir to coat in the spicy oil. \n| Add the [[Cabbage|cabbage]] and stir again.\n| Halve the [[Lemons|lemons]], then discard all the soggy bits inside. Slice the skin thinly and add to the [[Cabbage|cabbage]]. Add the [[Sultanas|sultanas]], [[Vinegar|vinegar]], [[Sugar|sugar]] and [[Stock|stock]] and stir well. \n| Cover and put in the [[Oven|oven]] for 50 minutes until the cabbage has softened.\n| Remove from the [[Oven|oven]] and rest, covered for another 30 minutes. \n|Discard the [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]] and top with chopped fresh [[Coriander|coriander]].\n}}\n\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n\n\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/early-harvest.html Belazu Early Harvest Extra Virgin Olive Oil Unfiltered]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/products/extra virgin-olive-oils.html Belazu Extra virgin olive oil]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/premier-choix.html Belazu Premier Choix Extra Virgin Olive Oil]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/belazu-pickled-lemons.html Belazu Preserved Lemon]\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#sultanas #onion #cinnamon #belazu #cabbage #preservedlemons #garlic #coriander #redcabbageandbelazupreservedlemons #vegetarian #cinnamonstick </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Reuchta mubowakha (Steamed noodles)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Reuchta mubowakha (Steamed noodles) a beef recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#noodles #chickpeas #colander #sauce #stew #boil #tomato #smen #stock #onion #spaghetti \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This recipe comes from Tripoli, Libya's capital city. The method given below assumes that you do not have a couscoussiere\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 5821\n|PortionCalories = 970\n|DatePublished=25th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Reuchta mubowakha (Steamed noodles) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">I think this is unbeatable if you use goat.</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">..but quite hard to buy here \ud83d\ude2c</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nThis recipe comes from Tripoli, Libya's capital city.  The method given below assumes that you do not have a [[couscoussi\u00e8re]].  However, if you have one, then do use it!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 heaped tablespoon [[smen]] (clarified butter) or 20 g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], roughly chopped\n| Garlic, to taste, finely chopped\n| 900 g [[Lamb|lamb]], [[Goat|goat]] or [[Beef|beef]], cut into 5 cm cubes\n| 2 large [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]] and roughly chopped\n| 2 tablespoons [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e diluted in 5 tablespoons water\n| 1.5 [[Litres|litres]] [[Meat stock|meat stock]]\n| 175 g [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]], soaked overnight, or 2 x 400g tinned chickpeas, drained\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Paprika|paprika]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon gound [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Baharat|baharat]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Saffron|saffron]], diluted in 3-4 tablespoons water\n| 450 g reuchta (thin, flat [[Noodles|noodles]]), or [[Spaghetti|spaghetti]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Melt the [[smen]] or [[Butter|butter]] in a large saucepan, add the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Fry|fry]] until soft.\n| Add the [[Meat|meat]], [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e and cook for 5 minutes.\n| Add the [[Stock|stock]], drained [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] and the [[Spices|spices]] and stir well.\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and place a [[Muslin|muslin]] lined [[Colander|colander]] over the top of the pan.\n| Break the [[Noodles|noodles]] or [[Spaghetti|spaghetti]] into 5 cm lengths and place them in the [[Colander|colander]] with a little of the [[Meat|meat]] [[Sauce|sauce]].  If using a proper [[couscoussi\u00e8re]], add the noodles 15-20 minutes before the end of the cooking time, moistening them regularly with the [[Sauce|sauce]].\n| Cover the [[Colander|colander]], lower the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 20 minutes.\n| Remove 1 or 2 ladlefuls of the [[Sauce|sauce]] from the pan and again, pour it over the [[Noodles|noodles]], making sure that all pieces are moistened.\n| Cover the [[Colander|colander]] again and [[Simmer|simmer]] for a further 40 minutes until the [[Meat|meat]] and [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] are tender, moistening the [[Noodles|noodles]] every 10 minutes.  If using tinned [[chickpeas]], add them 10 minutes before the end of the cooking time.\n| Add more water or [[Stock|stock]] to the [[Stew|stew]] if necessary.\n| To serve, spread the [[Noodles|noodles]] in a large serving dish and pour the [[Meat|meat]] and [[Chickpea|chickpea]] [[Stew|stew]] over them.\n}}\n===Variations===\nIf you don't want the hassle of cooking the [[Noodles|noodles]] over the [[Stew|stew]], simply [[Boil|boil]] them in plain water.  However, they will not take on the flavour of the [[Sauce|sauce]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Reuchta mubowakha (steamed noodles)]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes|Reuchta mubowakha (steamed noodles)]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Reuchta mubowakha (steamed noodles)]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes|Reuchta mubowakha (steamed noodles)]]\n[[Category:Libyan recipes|Reuchta mubowakha (steamed noodles)]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Reuchta mubowakha (steamed noodles)]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Reuchta mubowakha (steamed noodles)]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Reuchta mubowakha (steamed noodles)]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes|Reuchta mubowakha (steamed noodles)]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Reuchta mubowakha (steamed noodles)]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Steamed]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#noodles #chickpeas #colander #sauce #stew #boil #tomato #smen #stock #onion #spaghetti </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Roast leg of lamb (Moroccan-style) a meat recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#roastpotatoes #marinade #legoflamb #butter #harissapaste #ghee #roast #marinate #parsley #cuminseeds #roasted \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=By far the most popular meat of Morocco, this leg of lamb is an oven-roasted version of Mechoui\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4867\n|PortionCalories = 811\n|DatePublished=10th March 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 14 hours 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 12 hours 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Roast leg of lamb (Moroccan-style) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Lamb at its best</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">The more garlic, the better</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nBy far the most popular [[Meat|meat]] of Morocco, this [[Leg of lamb|leg of lamb]] is an [[Oven|oven]]-[[Roasted|roasted]] version of [[M\u00e9choui]].  You won't need to carve this, you should be able to serve by pulling the tender [[Meat|meat]] away from the bone with a fork.  Serve with [[Roast potatoes|roast potatoes]], a selection of vegetables and [[Harissa paste|harissa paste]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.5 kg (3.5 lb) [[Leg of lamb|leg of lamb]]\n}}\n'''[[Marinade|marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 40 g 1.5 oz [[Butter|butter]] or [[Ghee|ghee]]\n| 2 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed (or to taste)\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| &#188; teaspoons [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] (or to taste)\n| 1 teaspoon of fine [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n'''to garnish'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| Fresh [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]] or [[Parsley|parsley]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n*Prepare the [[Meat|meat]] the day before so it can [[Marinate|marinate]] overnight\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Trim the [[Meat|meat]] of excess [[Fat|fat]]\n| Carefully stab the joint all over with a knife\n| Blend the [[Marinade|marinade]] ingredients to a paste.  Soften the [[butter]] or [[ghee]] by microwaving for 20 seconds to make the mixing easier. \n| Spread this all over the surface of the [[Lamb|lamb]], pushing it into all of the the cuts.\n| Place in a [[sealable container]] and leave overnight in a [[Refrigerator|refrigerator]] to [[Marinate|marinate]]\n}}\n'''the next day'''\n# Remove the [[Leg of lamb|leg of lamb]] from the container and place the a large [[roasting tray]].\n# Free any solidified butter by microwaving the container for 30 seconds.  Add this to the joint.\n# [[Roast|roast]] the joint at 220\u00b0 C for 15 minutes.  Don't be concerned by the burning [[Butter|butter]], it will add to the flavour.\n# Reduce the [[Oven|oven]] temperature to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4) and [[Roast|roast]] for a further 2 hours.  [[Baste]] regularly\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Roast leg of lamb (Moroccan-style) preserved lemons.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Buttery marinade (with preserved lemon flesh)\nImage:Roast leg of lamb (Moroccan-style) ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Simple ingredients - (I eventually cut many more slashes than is shown here)\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nAllow to rest for 10 minutes and serve with [[Roast potatoes|roast potatoes]],  [[Harissa paste|harissa paste]] and a selection of [[Vegetables|vegetables]].\n===Variations===\nChop/ squash half of a [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] and add it to the [[marinade]].\n===Chef's notes===\nDon't be put off a recipe that calls for a leg of lamb because of the high cost.  This recipe can be adjusted for [[Frozen lamb - what great value!|half a leg of lamb and you buy that (frozen)]] for just \u00a36.00!
