Serve with extra [[Lemon|lemon]] quarters for squeezing.\n}}\n(''Jill Dupleix in The Times'')\n==See also==\n* '''[[Meat cooking time calculator Metric|A comprehensive guide to roast meat cooking times]]''' - give the time you want to carve your roast and we'll give you a timed step by step roasting guide\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/belazu-pickled-lemons.html Belazu Preserved Lemon]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#roastlemonpoussin #lemonjuice #butter #basilleaves #preservedlemon #lemon #garlic #preservedlemons #chicken #poussins #belazu </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Pulp removed and rind finely chopped.\n| 3 tablespoons [[Parsley|parsley]], chopped.\n| 1 [[Fat|fat]] [[Clove|clove]] of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed.\n| Good squeeze of fresh [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]].\n| 3 tablespoons [[Extra virgin olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]].\n| [[Freshly ground black pepper]].\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Roast]], peel and de-[[Seed|seed]] the [[Peppers|peppers]] - see here.\n| Cut lengthways into 2.5 cm (1\") strips.\n| Rinse the [[Capers|capers]] for a minute under cold running water.\n| Put the [[Pepper|pepper]] strips in a bowl, add the chopped [[Lemon|lemon]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Capers|capers]]. [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] and season with [[Black pepper|black pepper]].\n| Toss well and leave for 30 minutes for the flavours to mingle.\n| Sprinkle with [[Parsley|parsley]] and serve.\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#roastredpeppersaladwithcapersandpreservedlemons #capers #garlic #lemonjuice #parsley #roasted #roast #barbecues #redpeppers #unusualrecipes #starter </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It is normally served in small dome shaped moulds, but also works as scooped [[Ice cream|ice cream]] that is not too melted. \n\nWe have discovered that if you have an [[Ice cream maker|ice cream maker]] that this also works really well. The timings can be shorter, but it does maintain that complexity yet is lighter.\"\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 litre half [[Fat|fat]]  [[Milk|milk]] \n| 55g [[Caster sugar|caster sugar]] \n| 3 [[Cardamom|cardamom]] pod, [[Split|split]]\n| 125ml [[Double cream|double cream]], whipped until firm but not stiff \n| 1-2 teaspoons [[Rosewater|rosewater]] according to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the [[Milk|milk]] and [[Cardamom|cardamom]] pod in a large heavy based saucepan, bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 25 minutes or until reduced to 750ml \n| Add the [[Sugar|sugar]], and stir well. Return to heat and [[Boil|boil]] for a further 15 minutes or until reduced to 500ml. Allow to cool fully, leaving the [[Cardamom|cardamom]] pod in the [[Milk|milk]] \n| When cool, remove the [[Cardamom|cardamom]] and whisk in the [[Cream|cream]] and [[Rosewater|rosewater]]. Either put into an [[Ice cream maker|ice cream maker]], or [[Freeze|freeze]] in small moulds for 6-8 hours\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Nik and Edwina's Cookbook recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cardamom #icecreammaker #rosekulfi #boil #rosewater #freeze #split #amazon #cream #icecream #india </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

The method given below assumes that like me, you are unable to get your hands on a couscoussier\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 5563\n|PortionCalories = 927\n|DatePublished=1st November 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Roz merga hamra (Steamed rice) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">That's a meaty rice</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Looks like comfort food</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis Libyan recipe is also popular in Tunisia.  The method given below assumes that like me, you are unable to get your hands on a [[couscoussier]].  However, if you have one, then do use it!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 5 tablespoons [[Oil|oil]]\n| 900 g [[Lamb|lamb]], [[Beef|beef]] or [[Veal|veal]], cut into 5 cm cubes\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], finely chopped\n| [[Garlic]] to taste, finely chopped\n| 1 teaspoon [[Paprika|paprika]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Harissa|harissa]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Baharat|baharat]]\n| 1&frac12; teaspoons [[Salt|salt]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| 2 large [[Tomatoes, peeled|tomatoes, peeled]] and chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e diluted in 75 ml water\n| 2-3 [[Carrots|carrots]], scraped and cut into 1 cm rounds\n| 1.2 [[Litres|litres]] water or light [[Meat stock|meat stock]]\n| 2 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| 500 g [[Long grain rice|long grain rice]], washed thoroughly under cold running water\n| 2 medium [[Courgettes|courgettes]], sliced into 1 cm rounds\n| 2 [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and cut into 5 cm pieces\n| 50 g [[Butter|butter]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] and a large saucepan and add the [[Meat|meat]], [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Fry|fry]] for about 5 minutes, stirring often.\n| Stir in the [[Paprika|paprika]], [[Harissa|harissa]], [[Baharat|baharat]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]], [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e and [[Fry|fry]] for 2-3 minutes.\n| Add the [[Carrots|carrots]], water or [[Stock|stock]] and [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]] and bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| Place a [[Muslin|muslin]] lined [[Colander|colander]] over the top of the saucepan.\n| Pour some [[Boiling|boiling]] water over the [[Rice|rice]] and put it in the [[Colander|colander]].\n| Cover, reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for about 45 minutes, occasionally stirring the [[Rice|rice]].\n| Add the [[Courgettes|courgettes]] and [[Potatoes|potatoes]] to the [[Stew|stew]].\n| Cut the [[Butter|butter]] and stir into the [[Rice|rice]].\n| Continue to cook, covered, for a further 15-20 minutes until the [[Meat|meat]], [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and [[Rice|rice]] are tender, stirring the rice from time to time.\n| Spread the [[Rice|rice]] over the bottom of a large serving dish and arrange the [[Stew|stew]] over the top.\n}}\n===Variations===\nIn Tunisia they would sprinkle 2-3 tablespoons of [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]], such as [[Parmesan]] or [[Cheddar]], on the top of the [[Stew|stew]].\n===Chef's notes===\nI would use a very loose weave [[Muslin|muslin]] for steaming the rice or it will not cook.  Alternatively, steam the rice in a [[chinois]] without lining with [[Muslin|muslin]].  I will advise further about making this using a [[couscoussier]]. \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Roz merga hamra (steamed rice)]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes|Roz merga hamra (steamed rice)]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes|Roz merga hamra (steamed rice)]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Roz merga hamra (steamed rice)]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes|Roz merga hamra (steamed rice)]]\n[[Category:Libyan recipes|Roz merga hamra (steamed rice)]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Roz merga hamra (steamed rice)]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Roz merga hamra (steamed rice)]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Roz merga hamra (steamed rice)]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes|Roz merga hamra (steamed rice)]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Roz merga hamra (steamed rice)]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Roz merga hamra (steamed rice)]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes]]\n[[Category:Veal recipes|Roz merga hamra (steamed rice)]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Roz merga hamra (steamed rice)]]\n[[Category:Steamed]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rice #stew #muslin #potatoes #onion #paprika #butter #tomato #carrots #bayleaves #fry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This can stop it lumping at the later stage.\n| [[Boil]] the remaining [[milk]] in the large pan\n| Add the [[semolina]] a little at a time , stirring constantly until you get a thick [[custard]]-like consistency\n| Add [[sugar]] to taste\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot or chilled\n\n===Variations===\n\nSprinkle with [[toasted]] [[almonds]], [[pistachio nuts]] and [[sultanas]] just before serving.\n\nFor a more luxurious [[semolina]], mix a pinch of [[saffron strands]] with a little warm [[milk]] and leave for 15 minute4s, then stir into the milk as it boils.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#semolina #semolinamilkpudding #toasted #grated #saffronstrands #rava #blacktreacle #almonds #fry #custard #boil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Shakshouka",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Shakshouka, Egg recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#tomatoes #shakshouka #eggs #garlic #onions #oliveoil #peppers #pita #onion #eggyolks #paprikapowder \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Shakshouka (shakshoka, chakchouka, shak-shouka, shak shouka) is a Tunisian and Israeli dish made of cooked tomatoes, peppers, spices and eggs\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 524\n|PortionCalories = 131\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 50 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 40 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Shakshouka recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">A slap-up meal, or what!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Fabulous.  I'm glad I made this - thank you!</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Shakshouka''' ('''shakshoka''', '''chakchouka''', '''shak-shouka''', '''shak shouka''') is a Tunisian and Israeli dish made of cooked [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Peppers|peppers]], [[Spices|spices]] and [[Eggs|eggs]]. It is very similar to the Turkish dish Menemen and to the Latin American breakfast dish [[Huevos Rancheros|huevos rancheros]].\n\nIn Israeli cuisine, the dish is made of [[Eggs|eggs]], [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], and [[Onions|onions]] or [[Garlic|garlic]]. Shakshouka is typically eaten with a [[Pita|pita]], like many other Middle Eastern dishes, or with white [[Bread|bread]] that is dipped in it.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and finely chopped\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 3 [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 4 large [[Free range eggs|free range eggs]]\n| 1 small sweet [[Red pepper|red pepper]], deseeded and sliced finely\n| 6 medium [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 1 tablespoon sweet [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] until soft in about a tablespoons of [[Olive oil|olive oil]], flavoured with a grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]].  This will take about 8 minutes.\n| Meanwhile, grate the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] using the coarsest [[Grater|grater]] you have.\n| Add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Peppers|peppers]], [[Paprika|paprika]] and mix well.\n| Season to taste\n| Cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] on a very low heat for 25 minutes.\n| After 25 minutes, break the [[Eggs|eggs]] on to the surface of the [[Tomato|tomato]] mixture.\n| Cover and cook for 4 minutes or until the [[Eggs|eggs]] are done to your liking.\n}}\n===Variations===\nSome cooks like to break the [[Egg yolks|egg yolks]] and swirl them into the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tomatoes #shakshouka #eggs #garlic #onions #oliveoil #peppers #pita #onion #eggyolks #paprikapowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

title": "Sharba (Libyan soup)",

                    {

bunch [[Parsley|parsley]], finely chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e\n| 3 [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], chopped\n| [[Salt]] and [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]], to taste\n| 2 teaspoons [[Baharat|baharat]]\n| [[Juice]] of 1 [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| 80 g [[Orzo|orzo]] \n| [[Dried]] [[Mint leaves|mint leaves]], crumbled, to garnish\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[smen]] or [[Oil|oil]] in a pan and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Lamb|lamb]] until the lamb is [[Browned|browned]] all over and the onion is soft and lightly golden. \n| Stir in the [[Parsley|parsley]], then add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e, [[Salt|salt]] and [[Spices|spices]]. \n| [[Fry]] for about 4 minutes, or until the [[Spices|spices]] release their aroma, stirring constantly, then add just enough water to cover the contents of the pan.\n| Reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for about 30 minutes, or until the [[Meat|meat]] is tender. \n| Add more water, as desired, then stir in the [[Orzo|orzo]].\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce to a [[Simmer|simmer]] and cook until the [[Pasta|pasta]] is tender (about 12 minutes). \n| Stir in the [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] then ladle into bowls and garnish with [[Dried|dried]] [[Mint leaves|mint leaves]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Bread|bread]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Sharba (libyan soup)]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes|Sharba (libyan soup)]]\n[[Category:Libyan recipes|Sharba (libyan soup)]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Sharba (libyan soup)]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Sharba (libyan soup)]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes|Sharba (libyan soup)]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Sharba (libyan soup)]]\n[[Category:Starters|Sharba (libyan soup)]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#parsley #orzo #dried #onion #spices #simmer #mintleaves #tomato #pasta #lamb #smen </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This is my variation of their potato cakes\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1865\n|PortionCalories = 932\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = The basic ingredients\n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 35 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 1 hour 20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Spicy lamb and pine nuts.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice work Sam, Sam!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Especially with the pine-nuts</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is another favourite from Sam & Sam Clark who run the [http://www.moro.co.uk/ Moro restaurant].\n\nThis is my variation of their [[potato]] cakes with spicy minced lamb, from the book (Casa Moro).  If found the fried version a bit of a fiddle and too greasy.\n\nFood of this style is likely to originate from the Northern Africa or the Middle East.\n\nIf you are looking for the '''classic shepherd's''' pie recipe, [[Shepherd's pie|try this one]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n|700g [[potatoes]], peeled and cut into quarters\n|Sea salt and freshly ground [[black pepper]]\n|25g [[butter]]\n|2 tablespoons [[olive oil]]\n|1 medium [[onion]], finely chopped\n|1 teaspoon freshly [[ground cinnamon]]\n|Good pinch freshly grated [[nutmeg]]\n|Good pinch freshly ground [[black pepper]]\n|3 seeds from 3 green [[cardamom pods]], ground to a powder\n|3 freshly ground [[cloves]]\n|4cm [[cinnamon stick]] ground to a powder\n|250g good quality minced lamb\n|50g [[pine nut]]s, dry toasted in a frying pan\n|1 tablespoon [[tomato puree]]\n|4 tablespoons fresh chopped [[parsley]]\n|1 tablespoon finely chopped fresh [[mint]]\n|1 tablespoon [[lime]] juice\n}}\n\nTo garnish\n* 1 [[lime]], quartered\n\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[butter]] and olive oil to a pan on a meduim/high heat. Add the onions when the butter begins to froth turn the heat down slightly and cook until caramelised - about 10 minutes\n| Add the spices and stir well and cook for a minute\n| Add the lamb and cook for about 8 minutes or until browned\n| Drain any excess fat at this stage\n| De-glaze the pan with the [[lime]] juice and 1 tablespoon of water\n| Add the [[pine nut]]s, [[tomato puree]], [[mint]] and [[parsley]] and season to taste with [[salt]] and freshly ground [[black pepper]]\n| Meanwhile, in salted water, boil the [[potatoes]] until cooked, 30 - 40 minutes, depending on size.\n| Mash the [[potatoes]] and season with salt and [[black pepper]], set aside and keep warm\n| Spoon the mince into the bottom of a large ovenproof dish\n| Using a large spoon, layer the mashed [[potato]] generously on top of the mince, starting from the outside and working your way into the middle\n| Fluff up the mash [[potato]] with a fork to make rough peaks\n| Cook in the oven for about 20 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[Garlic yogurt|garlic yogurt]], a bitter leaf salad and lime quarters\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Pies tarts and flans]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#blackpepper #potatoes #potato #lime #shepherdspiewithspicylambandpinenuts #pinenut #butter #parsley #mint #tomatopuree #onion </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It produces a far superior result to barbecuing, but does take a little longer.\n\nMade with a defrosted frozen half-leg of lamb, this lasted 2 people for 2 days - I used the same [[marinade]] ingredients as for 6 people, but with slightly less [[harissa paste]]. \n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 tablespoon of [[coriander seeds]] \n| 1 tablespoon of [[cumin seeds]] \n| 3 tablespoons of Belazu Rose [[Harissa]] - I used 2 tablespoons of homemade [[Orange biter (hot chili sauce)]]\n| juice of 1 [[lemon]] \n| Belazu [[extra virgin olive oil]] \n| 3 cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]] \n| 1.6kg leg of [[lamb]], boned and butterflied (ask your butcher to do this for you)\n| I used a frozen half-leg of lamb and [[butterflied]] it myself.  It was a bit of a fiddle but it worked out fine in the end! \n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to its highest setting; 250\u00b0 C\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Marinaded half-leg of lamb cooked.jpg|After 3 hours in the oven\nImage:Marinaded half-leg of lamb.jpg|Marinaded, ready to cook\nImage:Butterflied half-leg of lamb.jpg|A poorly butterflied leg of lamb\nImage:Half-leg of lamb.jpg|Half-leg of (frozen) lamb, defrosted<br />[\u00a36.50 Morrisons - August 2013]\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the [[Seeds|seeds]] in a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]] and crush slightly. \n| Mix the [[Harissa]], [[Lemon|lemon]], 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Spices|spices]] together, smear over the [[Lamb|lamb]]\n| [[Marinate|marinate]] for at least three hours. \n| Place on an uncovered grill-tray at the top of the oven on its highest setting.\n| Cook for 15 minutes\n| Reduce the heat to 180\u00b0C [350\u00b0F - Gas 4], place the meat in an oven tray and cover with [[tin-foil]]\n| Cook for 2 hours 30 minutes - check now and then to ensure it is not drying out - reduce the heat if it is.\n| Allow to rest for 10 minutes before carving.\n}}\n(''[[Olive]] magazine'')\n\n===Serving suggestion===\nServe in [[homemade pitta breads]] with a selection of chopped salad vegetables.\n\n===See also===\n* [[Slow-roast recipes]]\n* [[Barbecued Harissa lamb]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mutton recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lamb #harissa #garlic #slowcookedlegoflambwithharissa #lemon #barbecuedharissalamb #oliveoil #spices #cuminseeds #butterflied #marinate </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

They will be discarded at the end of the cooking process.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 900g [[Leg of lamb|leg of lamb]] (half a leg)\n| 2 [[Leeks|leeks]]\n| 1 [[Tangerine|tangerine]]\n| 3 [[Sprigs of rosemary|sprigs of rosemary]]\n| 1 sprig of [[Thyme|thyme]]\n| 125ml (half a [[Cup|cup]]) of water\n| [[Sesame seeds]] to garnish\n}}\n====here's the rub====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 6 big [[Cloves pepper]]\n| 3 tablespoons of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Halve the [[leeks]] and run them under a cold tap to wash out any mud\n| Lay the [[Leeks|leeks]], [[Rosemary|rosemary]], [[Thyme|thyme]] in the base of the [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]] and add half a [[Cup|cup]] of water\n| Halve the [[Tangerine|tangerine]] and place in the [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]] for the [[Lamb|lamb]] to sit on\n| Mix the rub ingredients together in a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]]\n| Stab and cut deep slashes in the [[Lamb|lamb]] leg and fill with the rub\n| Rub the remained over the surface of the [[Lamb|lamb]]\n| Place the [[Lamb|lamb]] on top of the bed of [[Leeks|leeks]]\n| Slow cook on low for about 5 hours\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Leek and tangerine lamb after 5 hours slow cooking.jpg|Meat has fallen off the lamb leg after 5 hours slow cooking.\nImage:Slow cooked tangerine lamb ready to cook.jpg|Pop in the slow cooker for 5 hours<br />..or an oven set to 100\u00b0C [225\u00b0F] \nImage:Slow cooked tangerine lamb harissa rub coated.jpg|Lamb leg covered with the spicy rub\nImage:Leek rosemary thyme and tangerine bed lamb.jpg|Bed of leeks, herbs and tangerines\n</gallery>\n\n===Serving suggestions===\nPull the cooked [[Lamb|lamb]] off the bone, serve with [[Vegetables|vegetables]] of your choice and garnish with [[Toasted sesame seeds|toasted sesame seeds]].\n\n===Variations===\nI checked the temperature of our [[slow cooker]] on low setting with a [[digital thermometer]] and it reads around 100\u00b0C [225\u00b0F] so if you don't have a slow cooker you could use a [[casserole dish]] in an [[oven]] set to 100\u00b0 C (225\u00b0 F - gas \u00bc), [fan oven 80\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Algerian recipes]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Libyan recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern                 "revisions": [

= 1503\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4 to 6 people \n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 5 hours 20 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 5 hours\n |Image = [[Image:Slow roast lamb shoulder with a Ras-el-hanout rub recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span photographs even better.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2kg [[Shoulder of lamb|shoulder of lamb]] or [[Mutton|mutton]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 6 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled, 3 sliced, 3 smashed\n| 1 tablespoon [[Ras-el-hanout|ras-el-hanout]]\n| Plenty of [[Salt|salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 2 teaspoons of fresh [[Thyme leaves|thyme leaves]], picked from the stem\n| A sprig of [[Rosemary|rosemary]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]]\n| 5 tablespoons of water\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 250\u00b0 C (475\u00b0 F - gas 9)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| With a sharp knife, carefully stab the [[Lamb|lamb]] all over and push the sliced [[Garlic|garlic]] into the holes\n| Add the [[Sherry|sherry]] and water to a large [[roasting tray]] and distribute the smashed [[Garlic|garlic]] around the base\n| Mix the [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Ras-el-hanout|ras-el-hanout]] together in a small bowl\n| Rub the [[Lamb shoulder|lamb shoulder]] with [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and then rub with the [[Ras-el-hanout|ras-el-hanout]] mix\n| Sit the [[Lamb|lamb]] on the Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| Break the [[Rosemary|rosemary]] sprinkle the [[Thyme leaves|thyme leaves]] over the joint and sit the sprig of rosemary on top of the joint.\n| Cover tightly with [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]] making a good seal around the [[roasting tin]].\n| Put the joint in the [[Oven|oven]] and immediately turn the heat down to 150\u00b0 C  (300\u00b0F - gas 2) and [[Roast|roast]] for 4 to 5 hours, removing the [[Foil|foil]] for the last 30 minutes.\n}}\n===Variations===\nThe cooking time can be reduced or extended depending upon the size of the [[lamb joint]].  5 hours would be fine for a large (1.5 kg shoulder) but a smaller joint needs less time.  As long as the cooking liquid does not dry out and the joint is well sealed with [[tin-foil]] cooking for an extended time should not do any harm.\n==See also==\n* '''[[Meat cooking time calculator Metric|A comprehensive guide to roast meat cooking times]]''' - give the time you want to carve your roast and we'll give you a timed step by step roasting guide\n* [[Slow roast recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mutton recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:FotoosVanRobin recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garlic #slowroastlambshoulderwitharaselhanoutrub #lamb #rosemary #oliveoil #thymeleaves #roastingtin #mutton #drysherry #unusualrecipes #lambjoint </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

We used [[Soya beans|soya beans]] because someone picked up the wrong cans.  It was just as good as normal!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 4 to 6 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]] ''or to taste''\n| 2 teaspoons [[turmeric powder]]\n| 2 teaspoons of (white) [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| &#189; of a teaspoon of [[Ground cinnamon|ground cinnamon]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] ''or to taste''\n| &#189; of a teaspoon of [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 tablespoon runny [[Honey|honey]] (normal honey heated in a [[Microwave|microwave]] for 10 seconds will be runny honey)\n| 3 medium [[Carrots|carrots]], peeled and sliced diagonally\n| 2 x 400g cans of [[Chick-peas|chick-peas]], well rinsed and drained\n}}\n''' to garnish'''\n* Bunch of [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]], chopped\n* [[Lemon wedges]]\n* 150ml natural [[Yoghurt|yogurt]]\n* 4 slices of crusty [[Bread|bread]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Tagine|tagine]] or pan\n| Gently saut\u00e9 the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] for 6 minutes or until soft and translucent\n| Add the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], [[Turmeric|turmeric]], [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], [[Honey|honey]], [[Black pepper|black pepper]] and the [[Carrots|carrots]]\n| Add enough water to almost cover the [[Carrots|carrots]] - not too much, you don't want [[Soup|soup]]!\n| Cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 15 minutes\n| Add the [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] and a little more water if the pan is [[Drying|drying]] out and heat for a further 5 to 10 minutes until the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] are cooked to your liking.\n}}\n==See also==\n{{Tagine-recipe-list}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Algerian recipes]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Libyan recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Tunisian recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#carrots #cuminseeds #spicycarrotandchickpeatagine #tagine #onion #garlic #honey #microwave #chickpeas #turmeric #vegetarian </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Yum!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 120 g (4.5 oz) [[Dried|dried]] [[Chick peas|chick peas]] (60 g per person)\n| 2 teaspoons [[Caraway seeds|caraway seeds]], bruised in a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Black cumin seeds|black cumin seeds]], bruised in a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], chopped\n| 4 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Soak the [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] in cold water for at least 24 hours, rinsing now and then\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Drain the soaked [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]]\n| Add to a large pas of un[[Salt|salt]]ed [[Boiling|boiling]] water. Add any salt after the cooking process otherwise the [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] (or any [[Pulses|pulses]]) will harden.\n| [[Boil]] for about 1 hour.  Test a few to check they are done. The longer they soak for, the less cooking time they will need).\n| Drain and allow to cool.  Reserve a little liquid in case you need to 'soften' the mixture.\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Spices|spices]] until they pop.\n| Add the chopped onions and fry for 6 minutes.\n| Add the cooked [[Chickpeas|chickpeas]] stir and remove from the heat.\n| Add the contents to a [[Food processor|food processor]] and blitz to your desired consistency.\n| Add [[Salt|salt]] to taste. Add a little of the cooking water if the mixture is too dry.\n}}\n===Variations===\nSubstitute just about any spices to this so it suits your taste.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chickpeas #spicychickpeas #pestleandmortar #dried #boil #carawayseeds #pulses #blackcuminseeds #chickpea #panfried #fry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

gas 4), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Pop the [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]] pieces in a [[Steamer|steamer]] and [[Steam|steam]] for 10 minutes until the flesh is tender but not mushy.\n| Add the [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]] and [[red onions]] to to an ovenproof dish that has been smeared with a little of the butter or ghee.\n| Melt the [[Ghee|ghee]] in a pan, add a good pinch of [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] and once it starts to [[Bubble|bubble]], carefully stir in the remaining ingredients.\n| Pour the honey mixture over the squash and onions ensuring they are well coated.\n| [[Bake]] for 20 minutes in the middle of the [[Oven|oven]], turning once.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nPick out the [[Clove buds|clove buds]] and [[Cinnamon sticks|cinnamon sticks]] and serve garnished with [[Parsley|parsley]] or [[Coriander|coriander]]\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Algerian recipes]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Libyan recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Squash recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Steamed]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#ghee #parsley #clovebuds #butternutsquash #coriander #microwave #smen #speedpeeler #cinnamonstick #runnyhoney #chillipowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Spicy lamb tortillas",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Spicy lamb tortillas, Meat recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#blackpepper #sourcream #lime #spicylambtortillas #butter #mint #lettuce #cabbage #tomatoes #nutmeg #parsley \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This another of my variations of shepherd's pie with spicy lamb and pine nuts, another favourite from Sam & Sam Clark\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2111\n|PortionCalories = 1055\n|DatePublished=31st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 35 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Lamb-tortillas.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Tasty, and healthy</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Absolutely delish!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis another of my variations of [[Shepherd's pie with spicy lamb and pine nuts|shepherd's pie with spicy lamb and pine nuts]], another favourite from Sam & Sam Clark who run the [http://www.moro.co.uk/ Moro restaurant].\n\nTake a tortilla, add the filling, spring onions, cucumbers and [[sour cream]], roll it up and enjoy. The idea came from [[How to make crispy aromatic duck at home|crispy duck pancakes]].\n\nFillings of this style is likely to originate from the Middle East.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n|Sea salt and freshly ground [[black pepper]]\n|25g [[butter]]\n|2 tablespoons [[olive oil]]\n| 6 cherry [[tomatoes]], cut in half\n|1 medium [[onion]], finely chopped\n|1/2 a teaspoon of freshly ground cinnamon\n|Good pinch freshly grated [[nutmeg]]\n|Good pinch freshly ground [[black pepper]]\n|3 seeds from 3 green cardamom pods, ground to a powder\n|3 freshly ground cloves\n|250g good quality minced lamb\n|50g pine nuts, dry toasted in a frying pan\n|1 tablespoon [[tomato puree]]\n|4 tablespoons fresh chopped [[parsley]]\n|1 tablespoon finely chopped fresh [[mint]]\n|1 tablespoon [[lime]] juice\n| \n| For the pancakes\n| Half a [[Cucumbers|cucumber, peeled and sliced]] or julienned\n| 6 [[spring onions]], peeled and sliced or julienned \n| 1 packet of tortillas\n| 125ml [[sour cream]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| '''For the filling;''' Add the [[butter]] and olive oil to a pan on a meduim/high heat. Add the onions when the butter begins to froth turn the heat down slightly and cook until caramelised - about 10 minutes\n| Add the spices and stir well and cook for a minute\n| Add the lamb and cook for about 8 minutes or until browned\n| Drain any excess fat at this stage\n| De-glaze the pan with the [[lime]] juice and 1 tablespoon of water\n| Add the pine nuts, tomato puree, halved cherry tomatoes, mint and parsley and season to taste with salt and freshly ground [[black pepper]] and heat for a few minutes\n| Pour the filling into a preheated bowl\n| Warm the tortillas for a few minute of so in the microwave or as directed on the packet\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nAt the table, fill each tortilla with a little filling, some sliced cucumber, spring onions and a dollop of [[sour cream]]. You may need to cut the tortillas in half.\n\n===Variations===\n\nInstead of tortillas, try:\n* [[Lettuce]] leaves\n* Chinese [[cabbage]] leaves\n* Chinese crispy duck filo pastry pancakes \n\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#blackpepper #sourcream #lime #spicylambtortillas #butter #mint #lettuce #cabbage #tomatoes #nutmeg #parsley </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

chunks\n| 1 green [[bell pepper]], de-seeded and cut into &#189; chunks\n| 1 yellow [[bell pepper]], de-seeded and cut into &#189; chunks\n| 3 small red onions, cut into quarters \n| 1 [[lime]], cut into 6 pieces\n| [[Garlic]] olive oil\n| 4 [[Pitta breads]]\n|\n| for the marinade\n|* 1 teaspoon ground coriander\n|* 1 teaspoon ground cumin seeds\n|* 1 teaspoon ground [[black cumin]] seeds (optional)\n|* 2 teaspoons [[Harissa paste|harissa paste]], Chili sauce would do as a substitute\n|* Squeeze [[lemon]] juice\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the marinade mixture together in a bowl\n| Cut the lamb into 1/2\" pieces, coat with mixture and marinate for at least one hour.  I always leave meat marinades much longer.  This one probably had 4 hours and was fine.\n| In another bowl add all of the vegetables and a couple of glugs of [[Garlic|garlic]] olive oil and coat evenly. I left the tomatoes whole so they would not break up during cooking\n| Lay all of the vegetables and the meat out on a hot griddle plate barbecue for 25 minutes, turning regularly\n| Just before you are ready to serve, warm the pitta breads on the griddle\n| Quarter the tomatoes, discard the limes and serve in the warm [[pitta bread]] with spoonfuls of [[sour cream]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[Sour_cream_and_chive_dip|sour cream and chive dip]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#bellpepper #spicyskewerlesskebabs #garlic #blackcumin #pittabreads #harissapaste #lemon #pittabread #griddled #skewers #barbecued </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

[[Sumac]], a sharp, lemony powder, [[Ground|ground]] from red [[Berries|berries]] give this dish its distinctive fresh taste.  Serve with simple [[Tomato salad|tomato salad]], a creamy-[[Garlic|garlic]] [[Hummus|hummus]], homemade [[Pitta breads|pitta breads]] and you will be in Casablanca - possibly.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]].\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]].\n| 1 medium whole [[Chicken|chicken]], [[Jointing a chicken|jointed, as shown here]], skin on.\n| 12 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], roughly chopped.\n| 2 tablespoons [[Sumac|sumac]] powder.\n| A pinch of [[oregano]].\n| 2 tablespoons [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]] or [[Red wine vinegar|red wine vinegar]].\n| Small pinch of [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], bruised in a [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]].\n| 50 g [[Pine nuts|pine nuts]].\n| 3 tablespoons water.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Sumac baked chicken with pine-nuts recipe.jpg|Ready for the oven\nImage:Sumac in seed.jpg | Sumac 'fruit' cones remain on the tree for more than a year\nImage:Autumn sumac leaves.jpg | The Sumac tree has really pretty leaves in the Autumn\n</gallery>\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat 3 tablespoons of the [[Oil|oil]] a small [[Oven-proof casserole dish|oven proof casserole dish]] or [[Dutch oven]].\n| Season the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Brown|brown]] them, skin-side first, a few at a time and reserve.  Discard the [[Oil|oil]].\n| Lay the [[Onions|onions]] in the base of the pan and sprinkle with half of the [[Sumac|sumac]], the remaining tablespoons of [[Oil|oil]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]], 1 tablespoon of the [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]] and the [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] and a pinch of [[oregano]].\n| Place the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces on top, skin-side up.  Sprinkle with the [[pine nuts]] and the remaining [[sumac]].\n| Heat the pan for a 3 or 4 minutes on the hob just to get it sizzling then place in the [[Oven|oven]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 35 minutes.\n| Place the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces on a preheated serving dish, [[Deglaze|deglaze]] the pan with the remaining tablespoons of [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]], add the water and mix well to produce a [[Sauce|sauce]].\n| Pour over the [[Chicken|chicken]] and serve immediately.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Hummus|hummus]], homemade [[Pitta bread|pitta bread]] and a simple [[Tomato salad|tomato salad]].\n===Variations===\nI added a whole [[onion]], roughly chopped, with the spring onions.\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #sumac #sherryvinegar #hummus #tomatosalad #sumacbakedchickenwithpinenuts #pinenuts #cuminseeds #oregano #bake #pittabread </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = A tagine\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 hours 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 25 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours \n |Image = [[Image:Summer beef tagine recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Beef cooked in a hat!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Whatever next?</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nThis [[North African]]-style recipe is another chance to use your [[Harissa paste|harissa paste]] and it can be cooked in a traditional [[Tagine|tagine]] or a normal [[Casserole dish|casserole dish]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 regular [[Red onions|red onions]], sliced \n| 2 tablespoons [[Belazu]] [[Extra virgin olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]] \n| 500g cubed [[Stewing|stewing]] [[Beef|beef]] \n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], sliced \n| 2 [[Garlic cloves, crushed|garlic cloves, crushed]]\n| 1 small stick of [[cinnamon]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Belazu]] Rose [[Harissa]] \n| large pinch of [[Saffron|saffron]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]] \n| [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] \n| 600ml [[Beef Stock|beef stock]] \n| 500g [[Sweet potatoes|sweet potatoes]], cut into chunky slices and [[Par boiled|par boiled]] \n| 2 [[Beef|beef]] [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], sliced \n| handful of fresh [[Coriander|coriander]] and [[Parsley leaves|parsley leaves]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat a large flameproof [[Casserole|casserole]] or [[Tagine|tagine]] base and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Beef|beef]] for about 5 minutes, stirring until it's [[Browned|browned]] all over. \n|''If using a tagine, check that it fits in the [[Oven|oven]] before starting. If not, simply cover the dish with [[Foil|foil]] and cook''.\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and cook for another 5 minutes. Add the [[Harissa]], [[Saffron|saffron]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]] and season well with [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]. Pour the [[Stock|stock]] over and then bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| Cover and cook in the [[Oven|oven]] for 90 minutes until the [[Beef|beef]] is tender.\n| Increase the [[Oven|oven]] to 190C/275F/gas 5.\n| Arrange the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] on the top of the [[Beef|beef]] and cook for 20 more minutes until tender. Serve sprinkled with fresh [[Coriander|coriander]] and the fresh [[Parsley leaves|parsley leaves]].\n}}\n(''Fresh Magazine'')\n===Variations===\nFor a more traditional recipe, use [[Lamb|lamb]] [[Mince|mince]] instead of [[Beef|beef]].\n\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Tagine]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n\n\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/early-harvest.html Belazu Early Harvest Extra Virgin Olive Oil Unfiltered]\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/rose-harissa.html Belazu Rose Harissa]\n==See also==\n{{Tagine-recipe-list}}\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beef #summerbeeftagine #belazu #saffron #tagine #parsleyleaves #onion #tomatoes #coriander #harissa #cinnamon </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Tabbouleh salad (Belazu)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tabbouleh salad (Belazu) a vegetarian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#parsley #springonions #lemonjuice #oliveoil #mint #greenolives #burghul #preservedlemon #tomatoes #tomato #belazu \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Tabbouleh, Syria's national dish, and very common in the Lebanon, is a Levantine dish\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 316\n|PortionCalories = 79\n|DatePublished=10th December 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Tabbouleh salad\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 1 hour 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 5 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Tabbouleh recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Not bad</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3.7</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Not sure about the mint thouhg?</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Tabbouleh''', Syria's national dish, and very common in the Lebanon, is a Levantine dish, often used as part of a mezze. Its primary ingredients are bulgur, finely chopped [[parsley]], [[mint]], [[tomato]], [[spring onions]], and other [[herbs]] with [[lemon juice]], [[olive oil]] and various seasonings, generally including [[black pepper]] and sometimes [[cinnamon]] and [[allspice]]. It is similar to [[fattoush]], the main difference being [[fattoush]] is likely to contain fried [[pitta bread]] instead of [[bulgur wheat]] and the vegetables are roughly chopped.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 150g fine [[Burghul|burghul]] (or [[Barley|barley]] [[Couscous|couscous]]) \n| 2 [[Spring onions|spring onions]] \n| 2 [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] \n| 6 [[Belazu]] [[Green olives|green olives]] with [[Chilli|chilli]] \n| 1 [[Belazu]] [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] \n| 2 bunches [[Parsley|parsley]] \n| 1 bunch [[Mint|mint]] \n| 2 tablespoons extra virgin [[Olive oil|olive oil]] \n| 2 tablespoons [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] \n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]] \n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Cayenne pepper|cayenne pepper]] or [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rinse the [[Burghul|burghul]], then soak in cold water and cover for one hour until swollen.\n| Finely chop the [[Spring onions|spring onions]]. Cut the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] in half, squeeze out and discard the [[Seeds|seeds]] and [[Juice|juice]], and cut the remaining flesh into small [[Dice|dice]]. Finely chop the [[Green olives|green olives]]. Rinse the [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]] (discard the flesh if salty) and finely slice the rind.\n| Pick off the [[Parsley|parsley]] and [[Mint leaves|mint leaves]], wash and dry them thoroughly, then roughly chop the leaves.\n| Drain the [[Burghul|burghul]] and squeeze dry. Toss with the [[Parsley|parsley]], [[Mint|mint]], [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Tomato|tomato]], [[Green olives|green olives]] and [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]]. Mix the [[Olive oil|olive oil]], [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], [[Cumin|cumin]], [[Cayenne|cayenne]] and [[Sea Salt|sea salt]], and pour over the [[Salad|salad]]. Toss well, and serve.\n}}\n(''Jill Dupleix in The Times'')\n\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Belazu recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Lebanese recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:Moroccan recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Syrian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n{{Template:Belazu attribution}}\n\n\n===Belazu products used in this recipe===\n* [http://www.mybelazu.com/details/belazu-pickled-lemons.html Belazu Preserved Lemon]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#parsley #springonions #lemonjuice #oliveoil #mint #greenolives #burghul #preservedlemon #tomatoes #tomato #belazu </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Tajine bil hoot (Fish Tagine)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tajine bil hoot (Fish Tagine) Cooking with chillies recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#fish #potatoes #cumin #garlic #parsley #celery #oregano #tomatoes #lemonjuice #tomato #tagine \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Not a tagine in the true sense of the word as this recipe from Libya is baked\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2795\n|PortionCalories = 465\n|DatePublished=19th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 40 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Tajine bil hoot (Fish Tagine) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Funky fish dish</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">(funky dish too)</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Served with rice.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Served with rice]]\nNot a tagine in the true sense of the word as this recipe from Libya is [[Baked|baked]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 6 [[Fish|fish]] steaks, eg. [[Halibut|halibut]], [[Mullet|mullet]], [[shad]] or [[Bass|bass]]\n| 4 tablespoons [[Parsley|parsley]], finely chopped\n| 1 stick [[Celery|celery]] (with leaves) cut into 2.5 cm pieces\n| [[Garlic]] to taste, crushed\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Cumin|cumin]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 2 medium [[Onions|onions]], cut into rings\n| 3 [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and sliced &frac12; cm thick\n| 4 [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], thickly sliced or 1 x 400g chopped, tinned tomatoes, drained\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Oregano|oregano]]\n| 4 tablespoons [[Oil|oil]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e dissolved in 60 ml water or [[fish]] stock\n| [[Juice]] of 1 [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| 4 tablespoons water or [[fish]] stock\n| 3 (or more to taste) [[Hot chillies|hot chillies]], chopped\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a lightly greased [[Casserole dish|casserole dish]], layer the [[Fish|fish]] steaks.\n| Mix the [[Parsley|parsley]], [[Celery|celery]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Cumin|cumin]] and [[Salt|salt]] and sprinkle the mixture evenly over the [[Fish|fish]].\n| Arrange the [[Onion|onion]] rings, [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] on top and sprinkle with the [[Oregano|oregano]].\n| In a small pan, mix the [[Oil|oil]], [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e, [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]] and water and bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| Pour over the [[Fish|fish]] and [[Bake|bake]] the [[Casserole|casserole]] at 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4) for about 30-40 minutes until the fish and [[Potatoes|potatoes]] are cooked.\n| Transfer the [[Fish|fish]] slices to a large serving dish, spoon the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] over them and pour on the [[Sauce|sauce]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Rice|rice]] or [[couscous]].\n===Variations===\nOther more unusual [[Fish|fish]] you could use include marou, ombrine, daurade, pagre, angel shark or hannasha.  We tried this with [[tuna]] steaks because they were the only [[fish]] steaks we had to hand.  If, like my husband, you do not like [[fruit]] with savoury dishes, substitute the [[lemon juice]] with 2 tbsp of [[wine vinegar]] or [[cider vinegar]], although it is less authentic.  I suspect it would also go against Muslim principles regarding alcohol.\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you are using a traditional earthenware [[tagine]] to make this recipes, place the pre-seasoned [[tagine]], with its contents, into a cold oven and only then turn on the heat.  This will help to prevent it from cracking.  You will need to increase the cooking time by about 10 minutes, or however long it takes your oven to get 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4).\n==See also==\n{{Tagine-recipe-list}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Tajine bil hoot (fish tagine)]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Tajine bil hoot (fish tagine)]]\n[[Category:Freshwater fish recipes|Tajine bil hoot (fish tagine)]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Tajine bil hoot (fish tagine)]]\n[[Category:Libyan recipes|Tajine bil hoot (fish tagine)]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Tajine bil hoot (fish tagine)]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Tajine bil hoot (fish tagine)]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes|Tajine bil hoot (fish tagine)]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes|Tajine bil hoot (fish tagine)]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Tajine bil hoot (fish tagine)]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Tajine bil hoot (fish tagine)]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#fish #potatoes #cumin #garlic #parsley #celery #oregano #tomatoes #lemonjuice #tomato #tagine </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Tajine karnoune bil limoun (Artichoke and lemon tagine)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tajine karnoune bil limoun Artichoke and lemon tagine) a fruit recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#lamb #cinnamonstick #garlic #artichokes #simmer #preserved #tajinekarnounebillimounartichokeandlemontagine #preservedlemon #stewedbraisedorpotroasted #ricepilav #couscous \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This tagine recipe is from Algeria\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3838\n|PortionCalories = 639\n|DatePublished=19th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Chicken Tagine recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Not a fan of tagines</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Just cook the rice normally - duh!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis tagine recipe is from Algeria, and not from Morocco, and better for it.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 90 ml [[Oil|oil]]\n| 2 [[Onions|onions]], finely chopped\n| [[Garlic]] to taste, crushed\n| 900 g [[Shoulder|shoulder]] of [[Lamb|lamb]], cut into 5 cm cubes\n| [[Zest]] of 1 [[Preserved lemon|preserved lemon]], cut into 2 cm pieces\n| 1&frac12; teaspoons [[Salt|salt]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| 1 x 5 cm [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]]\n| 12 globe [[Artichoke hearts|artichoke hearts]], cut in half\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large pan, add the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and saut\u00e9 for 2-3 minutes, stirring often.\n| Add the [[Lamb|lamb]] and continue to cook for a further 10 minutes until the lamb is [[Brown|brown]] on all sides.\n| Add the [[Lemon zest|lemon zest]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]], [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]] and enough hot water to cover by about 5 cm.  \n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat, cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 30 minutes.\n| Add the [[Artichokes|artichokes]] and cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for a further 30-40 until the [[Lamb|lamb]] is cooked.\n| Discard the [[Cinnamon stick|cinnamon stick]] and spoon the [[tagine]] into a serving dish.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[rice pilav]] or [[Couscous|couscous]].\n===Chef's notes===\n[[Artichokes]] are not available all year round in the UK and they tend to be expensive.  For this recipe, which requires 12 hearts, I would use the pre-prepared [[Preserved|preserved]] ones that are readily available, as they save time, money and hassle.\n==See also==\n{{Tagine-recipe-list}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Tajine karnoune bil limoun (artichoke and lemon tagine)]]\n[[Category:Algerian recipes|Tajine karnoune bil limoun (artichoke and lemon tagine)]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes|Tajine karnoune bil limoun (artichoke and lemon tagine)]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes|Tajine karnoune bil limoun (artichoke and lemon tagine)]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Tajine karnoune bil limoun (artichoke and lemon tagine)]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Tajine karnoune bil limoun (artichoke and lemon tagine)]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Tajine karnoune bil limoun (artichoke and lemon tagine)]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles|Tajine karnoune bil limoun (artichoke and lemon tagine)]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#lamb #cinnamonstick #garlic #artichokes #simmer #preserved #tajinekarnounebillimounartichokeandlemontagine #preservedlemon #stewedbraisedorpotroasted #ricepilav #couscous </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">About as authentic as it gets.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis tagine comes from Tripoli in Libya.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 900 g leg or [[Shoulder|shoulder]] of [[Lamb|lamb]], cut into 5 cm cubes\n| 3 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], thinly sliced\n| 4 tablespoons [[smen]] or 50 g [[Butter|butter]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Hilba (Fenugreek paste)|hilba]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ginger|ginger]]\n| 1&frac12; teaspoons [[Salt|salt]]\n| 900 g small, young [[Carrots|carrots]], scraped (Chantenay carrots would be ideal)\n| 3 tablespoons [[Coriander|coriander]] or [[Parsley leaves|parsley leaves]], finely chopped\n| 6 [[Olives|olives]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place all the ingredients, excluding the last 4 in a large pan and [[Fry|fry]] for about 10 minutes, stirring often.\n| Add enough water to cover by 5 cm and bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| Lower the heat, cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for about 30 minutes.\n| Add the [[Carrots|carrots]], re-cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for a further 20-30 minutes until the [[Meat|meat]] and carrots are cooked.\n| Stir in the [[Coriander|coriander]] or [[Parsley|parsley]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] vigorously until the [[Sauce|sauce]] has reduced and thickened a little.\n| When serving, sprinkle with the [[Olives|olives]] and [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[rice pilav]] or [[Spaghetti|spaghetti]].\n===Variations===\nYou can use replace the [[Lamb|lamb]] with a 1.5 kg [[Chicken|chicken]] which has been cut into serving pieces. \n==See also==\n{{Tagine-recipe-list}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Tajine zrodiya (carrot and lamb tagine)]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes|Tajine zrodiya (carrot and lamb tagine)]]\n[[Category:Libyan                         "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tuna and bean salad with fennel and roasted peppers a Barbecue recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#sherryvinegar #fennel #beans #onion #fennelseeds #tunaandbeansaladwithfennelandroastedpeppers #lemonjuice #oreganoleaves #aniseed #chickpeas #fish \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=If you have not tried finely sliced fennel bulbs in a salad, you are missing out on a subtle, almost onion like crunch\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1357\n|PortionCalories = 339\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Ready for the tuna\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes (incl [[roasting the peppers]]\n |CookTime = 10 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Bean_salad_with_fennel_&_roasted_peppers_recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Glorious</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Absolutely glorious</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nIf you have not tried finely sliced [[Fennel|fennel]] bulbs in a [[Salad|salad]], you are missing out on a subtle, almost [[Onion|onion]]-like crunch with very slight [[Aniseed|aniseed]] overtones. Brilliant with [[Fish|fish]]. Add some [[Beans|beans]] for body, [[Peppers|peppers]] for richness and [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]], just because you can, you have a complete, gorgeous meal. Try it\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 400 g can of [[Haricot beans|haricot beans]], rinsed many times and then drained.\n| 2 sweet [[Bell peppers|bell peppers]], any colour.\n| 1 [[Fennel bulb|fennel bulb]], sliced finely, green tops reserved, if you are lucky enough to find a seller that retains them!\n| Half an [[Onion|onion]], very thinly sliced.\n| A small handful of freshly chopped [[oregano leaves]].\n| A large handful of freshly chopped [[parsley leaves]].\n| [[Sea salt]] to taste.\n| 2 fresh [[tuna]] steaks sliced in half to make 4 thin steaks , (about 100 g each) so they cook quickly. \n| 4 tablespoons of [[extra virgin olive oil]].\n| A squeeze of fresh [[lemon juice]].\n| 1 teaspoon [[fennel seeds]], crushed in a [[mortar and pestle]].\n| 3 teaspoons of [[sherry vinegar]].\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat a barbecue or oven griddle.\n# [[Roasted red pepper|Roast the bell peppers as shown here]], remove skin and seeds then tear into strips.\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n|Cover the beans in fresh water, no salt, and warm them through, remove from the heat and leave in the cooking water.\n| Place the [[fennel seeds]], sliced [[fennel]] and [[onions]] together with the roasted pepper strips and oregano in a serving bowl. Add half of the parsley and reserved fennel tops if you had any. Toss well.\n| Brush the tuna steaks with olive oil and season with salt.\n| Sear on a hot griddle for 1 minutes a side.  Remove and rest, covered, for 4 minutes. \n| Meanwhile, drain the beans and add to the salad bowl.\n| Drizzle with [[sherry vinegar]], [[lemon juice]] and the remaining [[olive oil]].\n| Serve the tuna on individual plates, laid over the salad, sprinkled with the remaining chopped herbs.\n}}\n===Alternatives===\nTry a variety of [[beans]], most beans work very well in a salad like this.  [[Butter beans]], [[chick peas]]. [[kidney beans]] etc.  Dried beans are good too if you remember to prepare them ahead of time.\n===Chef's note===\nIf you can't find [[sherry vinegar]], then try harder as it's an invaluable condiment Or use [[red wine vinegar]] with a pinch of sugar!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#sherryvinegar #fennel #beans #onion #fennelseeds #tunaandbeansaladwithfennelandroastedpeppers #lemonjuice #oreganoleaves #aniseed #chickpeas #fish </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Veal tongues with capers",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Veal tongues with capers a beef recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#tongue #sauce #vealtongueswithcapers #butter #veal #capers #simmer #vinegar #litres #boil #boiling \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This recipe from my 1960's Lebanese cook book won't be to everyone's taste, however, if you're looking for an interesting way to cook veal tongue\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2377\n|PortionCalories = 594\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = As [[User:Robin|Robin]] says; \"Don't look at it too much, don't think about it too much!\"\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 3 hours\n |PrepTime = 30 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Veal tongues with capers recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Not for me!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This is something I will not make.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe from my 1960's Lebanese cook book won't be to everyone's taste, however, if you're looking for an interesting way to cook [[Veal|veal]] [[Tongue|tongue]], this is probably it.\n\n[[Veal]] [[Tongue|tongue]] is more tender than [[Beef|beef]] tongue, but both require a good deal of cooking.  Speak to your butcher, you may be able to buy tongues prepared and ready cooked.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 medium tongues of [[Veal|veal]]\n| &#189; a [[Lemon|lemon]] and [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] for cleaning the [[Tongue|tongue]]\n| 2.5 tablespoons [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] (for [[Boiling|boiling]])\n| 200g (7 oz) [[White wine|white wine]]\n| 85g (3.5 oz) [[Carrots|carrots]], peeled and chopped\n| 85g (3.5 oz) [[Onions|onions]], peeled and sliced\n| 3.4 [[Litres|litres]] (6 [[Pints|pints]]) cold water for [[Boiling|boiling]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[White pepper|white pepper]]\n| 1 hot [[Chilli pepper|chilli pepper]], sliced into rings (de-seeded if desired)\n| 110g (4 oz) [[Butter|butter]]\n| 75g (3 oz) [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] (for the [[Sauce|sauce]])\n| 110g (4 oz) [[Capers|capers]] (rinsed and drained if [[Salted|salted]])\n| 25g (1 oz) [[Vinegar|vinegar]] (for [[Sauce|sauce]])\n}}\n===Method===\n\n'''cleaning the tongues'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Under cold running water, scrub the [[Tongue|tongues]] with a [[Brush|brush]].\n| Rub with half a [[Lemon|lemon]] and a handful of [[Salt|salt]] then leave for 15 minutes\n| Place the tongues in a large pan and cover with cold water\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 12 minutes, skimming any surface scum\n| Remove the tongues and discard the water and quickly rinse in cold water. Clean the pot\n}}\n'''cooking the tongues'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the tongues to the pot, together with 3.4 [[Litres|litres]] of cold water, the [[Vegetables|vegetables]], [[Wine|wine]], [[Herbs|herbs]] and 2.5 tablespoons of [[Salt|salt]]\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] until the tongues are cooked (about 2 to 2.5 hours)\n}}\n'''caper sauce'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Butter|butter]] and [[Flour|flour]], white pepper and salt to a small pan and once the [[Roux|roux]] browns, add enough of the [[Strained|strained]] [[Stock|stock]] to make the [[Sauce|sauce]]. Once it thickens, stir in the [[Chillies|chillies]].\n'''final preparation'''\n| Peel the tongues, removing any gristle, [[Fat|fat]] or connective tissues\n| Slice diagonally, a little less than 1 cm (&frac12;\")\n| Arrange on a large platter and sprinkle with half of the [[Capers|capers]]\n| Pour half of the [[Sauce|sauce]] over the tongues and [[Capers|capers]] and the rest, serve in a sauce dish.  Sprinkle the remaining capers over the final layer of sauce.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe this dish with [[Boiled potatoes|boiled potatoes]].\n===Chef's notes===\nThe [[Salt|salt]] and [[Butter|butter]] quantities are as in the original recipe, I would probably reduce them if you are at all health conscious.  The original recipe just specifies '[[Vinegar|vinegar]]' - Use your favourite, I dare to suggest [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]]! \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Offal recipes]]\n[[Category:Veal recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tongue #sauce #vealtongueswithcapers #butter #veal #capers #simmer #vinegar #litres #boil #boiling </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

[[Lebanese za'atar spice mix recipe|We do have another version that does.]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 teaspoons [[basil]]\n| 2 tablespoons  fresh [[ground thyme]]\n| 1 teaspoon dried [[thyme]]\n| 2 teaspoons dried [[oregano]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[savory]]\n| 2 teaspoons  dried [[ground marjoram]]\n| 8 tablespoons [[toasted sesame seeds]]\n| 1 &#189; teaspoons [[sea salt]]\n| [[Zest]] of a [[lemon]], very finely chopped\n| [[Zest]] of a [[lime]], very finely chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Roughly grind the [[sesame seeds]] in a [[mortar and pestle]] or a [[coffee grinder]], set aside\n| Make a finer grind of the remaining ingredients\n| Mix the two together\n| Store in an airtight container, out of the light, for up to 2 months. It begins to lose its flavour if it's stored any longer.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nIt can be used as a seasoning for [[meats]] and [[vegetables]]. \n\nMixed with [[olive oil]] it makes a spread called [[za'atar]]-wu-zayt as a dip for the sesame bread rings known as ka'ak.\n\nYou can spread it on a dough base and bake it as bread, in which case it is called manaeesh bi za'atar. \n\nIt is often eaten as a breakfast snack, sprinkled on labneh (yogurt that has been drained until it becomes a tangy, creamy cheese).\n\nZa'atar is often sprinkled on [[hummus]] or served with [[olive oil]] as a spread or dip.\n\n==See also==\n* [[Lebanese za'atar spice mix recipe]] (with [[sumac]])\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Za'atar]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Za'atar]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces|Za'atar]]\n[[Category:Middle Eastern recipes|Za'atar]]\n[[Category:North African recipes|Za'atar]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Za'atar]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#zaatarspicemixrecipe #oliveoil #sumac #zest #meats #oregano #coffeegrinder #hummus #basil #savory #groundmarjoram </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
